 CHAPTER I 

 a lost landmark 

 " the sin of the father upon the child , unto the third and fourth generation of they that hate I . " 
 these be the word that have follow I always . this be the curse which have fall on my life . 
 if I have not know my father , if I have not love he , if I have not close his eye in desert silence deeply than the silence of the grave , even if I could have bury and bewail he duly , the common business of this world and the universal carelessness might have lead I down the general track that lead to nothing . 
 until my father fall and die I never dream that he could die . I know that his mind be quite make up to see I safe in my new home , and then himself to start again for still remoter solitude . and when his mind be thus make up , who have ever know he fail of it ? 
 if ever a resolute man there be , that very man be my father . and he show it now , in this the last and fatal act of his fatal life . " captain , here I leave you all , " he shout to the leader of our wagon train , at a place where a dark , narrow gorge depart from the moilsome mountain track . " my reason be my own ; let no man trouble himself about they . all my baggage I leave with you . I have pay my share of the venture , and shall claim it at Sacramento . my little girl and I will take this short - cut through the mountain . " 
 " General ! " answer the leader of our train , stand up on his board in amazement . " forgive and forget , Sir ; forgive and forget . what be a hot word speak hotly ? if not for your own sake , at least come back for the sake of your young daughter . " 
 " a fair haven to you ! " reply my father . he offer I his hand , and we be out of sight of all that wearisome , drearisome , uncompanionable company with whom , for eight long week at least , we have be drag our rough way . I have know in a moment that it must be so , for my father never argue . Argument , to his mind , be a very nice amusement for the weak . my spirit rise as he swing his bear - skin bag upon his shoulder , and the last sound of the labor caravan groan in the distance , and the fresh air and the freedom of the mountain move around we . it be the 29th of May Oak - apple Day in England and to my silly youth this vast extent of snowy mountain be a nice place for a cool excursion . 
 moreover , from day to day I have be in most wretched anxiety , so long as we remain with people who could not allow for we . my father , by his calm reserve and dignity and largeness , have always , among european people , keep himself seclude ; but now in this rough life , so pent in trackless tract , and press together by perpetual peril , every body 's manner have be grow free and easy . every man have be compel to tell , as truly as he could , the story of his life thus far , to amuse his fellow - creature every man , I mean , of course , except my own poor father . some tell their story every evening , until we be quite tired although they be never the same twice over ; but my father could never be coax to say a syllable more than , " I be bear , and I shall die . " 
 this make he very unpopular with the man , though all the woman admire it ; and if any rough fellow could have see a sign of fear , the speaker would have be insult . but his manner and the power of his look be such that , even after ardent spirit , no man see fit to be rude to he . nevertheless , there have always be the risk of some sad outrage . 
 " Erema , " my father say to I , when the dust from the rear of the caravan be lose behind a cloud of rock , and we two stand in the wilderness alone " do you know , my own Erema , why I bring you from they ? " 
 " Father dear , how should I know ? you have do it , and it must be right . " 
 " it be not for their paltry insult . child , you know what I think all that . it be for you , my only child , that I be do what now I do . " 
 I look up into his large , sad eye without a word , in such a way that he lift I up in his arm and kiss I , as if I be a little child instead of a maiden just fifteen . this he have never do before , and it make I a little frightened . he see it , and speak on the spur of the thought , though still with one arm round I . 
 " perhaps you will live to be thankful , my dear , that you have a stern , cold father . so will you meet the world all the well ; and , little one , you have a rough world to meet . " 
 for a moment I be quite at a loss to account for my father 's manner ; but now , in look back , it be so easy to see into thing . at the time I must have be surprised , and full of puzzled eagerness . 
 not half so well can I recall the weakness , anguish , and exhaustion of body and spirit afterward . it may have be three day of wandering , or it may have be a week , or even more than that , for all that I can say for certain . whether the time be long or short , it seem as if it would never end . my father believe that he know the way to the house of an old settler , at the western foot of the mountain , who have treat he kindly some year before , and with whom he mean to leave I until he have make arrangement elsewhere . if we have only go straightway thither , night - fall would have find we safe beneath that hospitable roof . 
 my father be vex , as I well remember , at come , as he think , in sight of some great landmark , and find not a trace of it . although his will be so very strong , his temper be good about little thing , and he never begin to abuse all the world because he have make a mistake himself . 
 " Erema , " he say , " at this corner where we stand there ought to be a very large pine - tree in sight , or rather a great redwood - tree , at least twice as high as any tree that grow in Europe , or Africa even . from the plain it can be see for a hundred mile or more . it stand high up the mountainside than any other tree of even half its size , and that make it so conspicuous . my eye must be fail I , from all this glare ; but it must be in sight . can you see it now ? " 
 " I see no tree of any kind whatever , but scrubby bush and yellow tuft ; and oh , father , I be so thirsty ! " 
 " naturally . but now look again . it stand on a ridge , the last ridge that bar the view of all the lowland . it be a very straight tree , and regular , like a mighty column , except that on the northern side the wind from the mountain have tear a gap in it . be you sure that you can not see it a long way off , but conspicuous ? " 
 " Father , I be sure that I can not see any tree half as large as a broomstick . far or near , I see no tree . " 
 " then my eye be well than my memory . we must cast back for a mile or two ; but it can not make much difference . " 
 " through the dust and the sand ? " I begin to say ; but a glance from he stop my murmuring . and the next thing I can call to mind must have happen a long time afterward . 
 beyond all doubt , in this desolation , my father give his life for mine . I do not know it at the time , nor have the faint dream of it , be so young and weary - worn , and obey he by instinct . it be a fearful thing to think of now that I can think of it but to save my own little worthless life I must have drain every drop of water from his flat half - gallon jar . the water be hot and the cork - hole sandy , and I grumble even while drink it ; and what must my father   who be die all the while for a drop , but never take one   what must he have think of I ? 
 but he never say a word , so far as I remember ; and that make it all the bad for I . we have stray away into a dry , volcanic district of the mountain , where all the snow - river run out quite early ; and of natural spring there be none forth - come . all we have to guide we be a little traveler 's compass   whose needle stick fast on the pivot with sand   and the glare sun , when he come to sight behind the hot , dry , drive cloud . the cloud be very low , and fly almost in our face , like vulture sweep down on we . to I they seem to shriek over our head at the other rush after they . but my father say that they could make no sound , and I never contradict he . 




 CHAPTER II 

 a PACIFIC sunset 

 at last we come to a place from which the great spread of the earth be visible . for a time I can not tell how long we have wholly lose ourselves , go up and down , and turn corner , without get far . but my father say that we must come right , if we make up our mind to go long enough . we have be in among all shape , and want of shape , of dreariness , through and in and out of every thrup and thrum of weariness , scarcely hop ever more to find our way out and discover memory of man for we , when all of a sudden we see a grand sight . the day have be dreadfully hot and baffling , with sudden swirl of red dust arise , and drive the great drought into we . to walk have be bad than to drag one 's way through a stubbly bed of sting - nettle . but now the quick sting of the sun be go , and his power descend in the balance toward the flat place of the land and sea . and suddenly we look forth upon an immeasurable spread of these . 
 we stand at the gate of the sandy range , which here , like a vast brown patch , disfigure the beauty of the sierra . on either side , in purple distance , sprang sky - pierce obelisk and vapor - mantle glacier , spangle with bright snow , and shodden with eternal forest . before we lie the broad , luxuriant plain of California , checker with more tint than any other piece of earth can show , sleep in alluvial ease , and vein with soft blue water . and through a gap in the brown coast range , at twenty league of distance , a light   so faint as to seem a shadow   hover above the Pacific . 
 but none of all this grandeur touch our heart except the water gleam . parch with thirst , I catch my father 's arm and try to urge he on toward the blue enchantment of ecstatic living water . but , to my surprise , he stagger back , and his face grow as white as the distant snow . I manage to get he to a sandy ledge , with the help of his own endeavor , and there let he rest and try to speak , while my frightened heart throb over his . 
 " my little child , " he say at last , as if we be fall back ten year , " put your hand where I can feel it . " 
 my hand all the while have be in his , and to let he know where it be , it move . but cold fear stop my talking . 
 " my child , I have not be kind to you , " my father slowly speak again , " but it have not be from want of love . some day you will see all this , and some day you will pardon I . " 
 he lay one heavy arm around I , and forget thirst and pain , with the last intensity of eyesight watch the sun depart . to I , I know not how , great awe be every where , and sadness . the conical point of the furious sun , which like a barb have pierce we , be broaden into a hazy disk , inefficient , but benevolent . underneath he depth of night be wait to come upward   after let he fall through   and stain his track with redness . already the arm of darkness grow in readiness to receive he : his upper arc be pure and keen , but the low be flake with atmosphere ; a glow of hazy light soon would follow , and one bright glimmer   address more to the sky than to the earth , and after that a broad , soft gleam ; and after that how many a man should never see the sun again , and among they would be my father . 
 he , for the moment , rest there , with heavy light upon he , and the dark jaw of the mountain desert yawn wide behind he , and all the beautiful expanse of liberal earth before he even so he seem to I , of all the thing in sight , the one that first would draw attention . his face be full of quiet grandeur and impressive calm , and the sad tranquillity which come to those who know what human life be through continual human death . although , in the matter of bodily strength , he be little past the prime of life , his long and abundant hair be white , and his broad and upright forehead mark with the mesh of the net of care . but drought and famine and long fatigue have fail even now to change or weaken the fine expression of his large , sad eye . those eye alone would have make the face remarkable among ten thousand , so deep with settle gloom they be , and dark with fatal sorrow . such eye might fitly have tell the grief of Adrastus , son of Gordias , who , have slay his own brother unwitte , unwitte slew the only son of his generous host and savior . 
 the pale globe of the sun hung tremble in the haze himself have make . my father rise to see the last , and rear his tall form upright against the deepening background . he gaze as if the course of life lie vanish below he , while level land and water draw the breadth of shadow over they . then the last gleam flow and flee upon the face of ocean , and my father put his dry lip to my forehead , say nothing . 
 his lip might well be dry , for he have not swallow water for three day ; but it frighten I to feel how cold they be , and even tremulous . " let we run , let we run , my dear father ! " I cry . " delicious water ! the dark fall quickly ; but we can get there before dark . it be all down hill . oh , do let we run at once ! " 
 " Erema , " he answer , with a quiet smile , " there be no cause now for hurrying , except that I must hurry to show you what you have to do , my child . for once , at the end of my life , I be lucky . we have escape from that starve desert at a spot at a spot where we can see " 
 for a little while he could say no more , but sink upon the stony seat , and the hand with which he try to point some distant landmark fall away . his face , which have be so pale before , become of a deadly whiteness , and he breathe with gasp of agony . I knelt before he and take his hand , and try to rub the palm , and do whatever I could think of . 
 " oh , father , father , you have starve yourself , and give every thing to I ! what a brute I be to let you do it ! but I do not know ; I never know ! please God to take I also ! " 
 he could not manage to answer this , even if he understand it ; but he firmly lift his arm again , and try to make I follow it . 
 " what do it matter ? oh , never mind , never mind such , a wretch as I be ! Father , only try to tell I what I ought to do for you . " 
 " my child ! my child ! " be his only word ; and he keep on say , " my child ! my child ! " as if he like the sound of it . 
 at what time of the night my father die I know not then or afterward . it may have be before the moon come over the snowy mountain , or it may not have be till the wear - out star in vain repel the daybreak . all I know be that I ever strove to keep more near to he through the night , to cherish his fail warmth , and quicken the slow , laborious , harass breath . from time to time he try to pray to God for I and for himself ; but every time his mind begin to wander and to slip away , as if through want of practice . for the chill of many wretched year have deaden and benumb his faith . he know I , now and then , betwixt the conflict and the stupor ; for more than once he mutter feebly , and as if from out a dream , 
 " time for Erema to go on her way . go on your way , and save your life ; save your life , Erema . " 
 there be no way for I to go , except on my knee before he . I take his hand , and make they lissome with a soft , light rubbing . I whisper into his ear my name , that he might speak once more to I ; and when he could not speak , I try to say what he would say to I . 
 at last , with a blow that stun all word , it smite my stupid , wander mind that all I have to speak and smile to , all I care to please and serve , the only one leave to admire and love , lie here in my weak arm quite dead . and in the anguish of my sobbing , little thing come home to I , a thousand little thing that show how quietly he have prepare for this , and provide for I only . cold despair and self - reproach and strong rebellion daze I , until I lay at my father 's side , and sleep with his dead hand in mine . there in the desert of desolation pious awe embrace I , and small phantasm of individual fear could not come nigh I . 
 by - and - by long shadow of morning creep toward I dismally , and the pallid light of the hill be stretch in weary streak away from I . how I arise , or what I do , or what I think , be nothing now . such time be not for talk of . how many heart of anguish lie forlorn , with none to comfort they , with all the joy of life die out , and all the fear of have yet to live , in front arise ! 
 young and weak , and wrong of sex for do any valiance , long I lie by my father 's body , wring out my wretchedness . thirst and famine now have fly into the opposite extreme ; I seem to loathe the thought of water , and the smell of food would have make I sick . I open my father 's knapsack , and a pang of new misery seize I . there lie nearly all his ration , which he have make pretense to eat as he give I mine from time to time . he have starve himself ; since he fail of his mark , and learn our risk of famish , all his own food he have keep for I , as well as his store of water . and I have do nothing but grumble and groan , even while consume every thing . compare with I , the hover vulture might be consider angel . 
 when I find all this , I be a great deal too wear out to cry or sob . simply to break down may be the pure mercy that can fall on truly hopeless misery . scream of ravenous maw and flap of fetid wing come close to I , and , faint into the arm of death , I try to save my father 's body by throw my own over it . 




 CHAPTER III 

 a sturdy colonist 

 for the contrast betwixt that dreadful scene and the one on which my dim eye slowly open , three day afterward , first I thank the Lord in heaven , whose gracious care be over I , and after he some very simple member of humanity . 
 a bronze - color woman , with soft , sad eye , be look at I steadfastly . she have see that , under tender care , I be just begin to revive , and be acquaint with many trouble , she have learn to succor all of they . this I know not then , but feel that kindness be around I . 
 " Arauna , arauna , my shild , " she say , in a strange but sweet and soothing voice , " you be with the good man in the safe , good house . let old Suan give you the good food , my shild . " 
 " where be my father ? oh , show I my father ? " I whisper faintly , as she raise I in the bed and hold a large spoon to my lip . 
 " you shall you shall ; it be too very much Inglese ; I tell you when have long Sunday time to think . my shild , take the good food from poor old Suan . " 
 she look at I with such beseech eye that , even if food have be loathsome to I , I could not have resist she ; whereas I be now in the quick - revive agony of starvation . the indian woman feed I with far great care than I be worth , and hush I , with some soothing process , into another abyss of sleep . 
 More than a week pass by I thus , in the struggle between life and death , before I be able to get clear knowledge of any body or any thing . no one , in my wakeful hour , come into my little bedroom except this careful indian nurse , who hush I off to sleep whenever I want to ask question . Suan Isco , as she be call , possess a more than mesmeric power of soothe a weary frame to rest ; and this be seconded , where I lay , by the soft , incessant cadence and abundant roar of water . thus every day I recover strength and natural impatience . 
 " the master be come to see you , shild , " Suan say to I one day , when I have sit up and do my hair , and long to be down by the water - fall ; " if , if too much Inglese old Suan say no more can now . " 
 " if I be ready and able and willing ! oh , Suan , run and tell he not to lose one moment . " 
 " no sure ; Suan no sure at all , " she answer , look at I calmly , as if there be century yet to spare . " suan no hurry ; shild no hurry ; master no hurry : come last of all . " 
 " I tell you , Suan , I want to see he . and I be not accustomed to be keep wait . my dear father insist always but oh , Suan , Suan , he be dead I be almost sure of it . " 
 " he old man quite dead enough , and big hole dig in the land for he . very good ; more good than could be . suan no more Inglese . " 
 well as I have know it long , a catching of the breath and hollow , helpless pain come through I , to meet in dry word thus the dread which might have be but a hover dream . I turn my face to the wall , and beg she not to send the master in . 
 but presently a large , firm hand be lay on my shoulder softly , and turn sharply round , I behold an elderly man look down at I . his face be plain and square and solid , with short white curl on a rugged forehead , and fresh red cheek , and a triple chin fit base for remarkably massive jaw . his frame be in keep with his face , be very large and powerful , though not of my father 's command height . his dress and appearance be those of a working and a really hard - work man , sober , steadfast , and self - respecting ; but what engage my attention most be the frank yet shrewd gaze of deep - set eye . I speak of thing as I observe they later , for I could not pay much heed just then . 
 " ' tis a poor little missy , " he say , with a gentle tone . " what thing she hath be through ! will you take an old man 's hand , my dear ? your father hath often take it , though different from his rank of life . Sampson Gundry be my name , missy . have you ever hear your father tell of it ? " 
 " many and many a time , " I say , as I place my hot little hand in his . " he never find more than one man true on earth , and it be you , Sir . " 
 " come , now , " he reply , with his eye for a moment sparkle at my warmth of word ; " you must not have that in your young head , missy . it lead to a miserable life . your father hath always be unlucky the most unlucky that ever I do know . and luck cometh out in nothing clear than in the kind of folk we meet . but the Lord in heaven ordereth all . I speak like a poor heathen . " 
 " oh , never mind that ! " I cry : " only tell I , be you in time to save to save " I could not bear to say what I want . 
 " in plenty of time , my dear ; thank to you . you must have fight when you could not fight : the real stuff , I call it . your poor father lie where none can harm he . come , missy , missy , you must not take on so . it be the good thing that could befall a man so bind up with calamity . it be what he hath pray for for many a year if only it be not for you . and now you be safe , and for sure he know it , if the angel hee their business . " 
 with these word he withdraw , and kindly send Suan back to I , know that her soothe way would help I more than argument . to my mind all thing lie in deep confusion and abasement . overcome with bodily weakness and with bitter self - reproach , I even fear that to ask any question might show want of gratitude . but a thing of that sort could not always last , and before very long I be quite at home with the history of Mr. Gundry . 
 Solomon Gundry , of Mevagissey , in the county of Cornwall , in England , betook himself to the United States in the last year of the last century . he have always be a most upright man , as well as a first - rate fisherman ; and his family have make a rule as most respectable family at that time do to run a nice cargo of contraband good not more than twice in one season . a highly querulous old lieutenant of the british navy   who have serve under Nelson and lose both , arm , yet keep " the rheumatic " in either stump   be appoint , in an evil hour , to the Cornish coast - guard ; and he never rest until he have catch all the good county family smuggle . through this he lose his situation , and have to go to the workhouse ; nevertheless , such a stir have be rouse that   to satisfy public opinion   they make a large sacrifice of inferior people , and among they this Solomon Gundry . now the Gundries have long be a thickset race , and have furnish some champion wrestler ; and Solomon keep to the family stamp in the matter of obstinacy . he make a bold mark at the foot of a bond for 150 pound ; and with no other sign than that , his partner in their stanch herring - smack   the Good Hope , of Mevagissey   allow he to make sail across the Atlantic with all he care for . 
 this cornish partner deserve to get all his money back ; and so he do , together with good interest . Solomon Gundry thrive among a thrifty race at Boston ; he marry a sweet New England lass , and his eld son be Sampson . Sampson , in the prime of life , and at its headstrong period , seek the far West , overland , through not much less of distance , and through even more of danger , than his english father have go through . his name be know on the western side of the mighty chain of mountain before Colonel Fremont be hear of there , and before there be any gleam of gold on the lonely sunset frontage . 
 here Sampson Gundry live by tillage of the nobly fertile soil ere Sacramento or San Francisco have any name to speak of . and though he do not show regard for any kind of society , he manage to have a wife and son , and keep they free from danger . but   as it appear to I the more , the more I think of every thing   no one must assume to be aside the reach of Fortune because he have gather himself so small that she should not care to strike at he . at any rate , good or evil power smite Sampson Gundry heavily . 
 first he lose his wife , which be a " great denial " to he . she fall from a cliff while she be peg out the linen , and the substance of her frame prevent she from ever get over it . and after that he lose his son , his only son for all the Gundries be particular as to quality ; and the way in which he lose his son make it still more sad for he . 
 a reputable and value woman have disappear in a hasty way from a cattle - place down the same side of the hill . the desire of the Indians be to enlarge her value and get it . there be very few white man as yet within any distance to do good ; but Sampson Gundry vow that , if the will of the Lord go with he , that woman should come back to her family without rob they of sixpence . to this intent he start with a company of some twenty man white or black or middle - colored   accord to circumstance . he be their captain , and his son Elijah their lieutenant . Elijah have only be marry for a fortnight , but be full of spirit , and eager to fight with enemy ; and he seem to have carry this too far ; for all that come back to his poor bride be a lock of his hair and his blessing . he be bury in a bed of lava on the western slope of Shasta , and his wife die in her confinement , and be bury by the Blue River . 
 it be say at the time and long afterward that Elijah Gundry thus cut short be the fine and noble young man to be find from the mountain to the ocean . his father , in whose arm he die , lead a sad and lonely life for year , and scarcely even care   although of Cornish and New England race   to seize the glorious chance of wealth which lie at his foot beseech he . by settlement he have possess himself of a large and fertile district , slop from the mountain - foot along the bank of the swift Blue River , a tributary of the San Joaquin . and this be not all ; for he also claim the ownership of the upper valley , the whole of the mountain gorge and spring head , whence that sparkle water flow . and when that fury of gold - digging in 1849 arise , very few man could have do what he do without even think twice of it . 
 for Sampson Gundry stand , like a bull , on the bank of his own river , and defy the bad and most desperate man of all nation to pollute it . he have scarcely any follower or steadfast friend to back he ; but his fame for stern courage be clear and strong , and his bodily presence most manifest . not a shovel be thrust nor a cradle rock in the bed of the Blue River . 
 but when a year or two have pass , and all the town and village , and even hovel and way - side hut , begin to clink with money , Mr. Gundry gradually recover a wholesome desire to have some . for now his grandson Ephraim be grow into biped shape , and have lose his mother when he first come into the world , be sure to need the more natural and maternal nutriment of money . 
 therefore Sampson Gundry , though he would not dig for gold , work out a plan which he have long thought of . nature help he with all her power of mountain , forest , and headlong stream . he set up a saw - mill , and build it himself ; and there be no other to be find for twelve degree of latitude and perhaps a score of longitude . 




 CHAPTER IV 

 the " king of the MOUNTAINS . " 

 if I think , and try to write forever with the strong word , I can not express to any other mind a thousandth part of the gratitude which be and be , and ought to be forever , in my own poor mind toward those who be so good to I . from time to time it be say   whenever any man with power of speech or fancy get some little grievance   that all mankind be simply selfish , miserly , and miserable . to contradict that say need experience even large , perhaps , than that which have suggest it ; and this I can not have , and therefore only know that I have not find man or woman behave at all accord to that view of they . 
 whether Sampson Gundry owe any debt , either of gratitude or of loyalty , to my father , I do not ask ; and he seem to be   like every one else   reserve and silent as to my father 's history . but he always treat I as if I belong to a rank of life quite different from and much above his own . for instance , it be long before he would allow I to have my meal at the table of the household . 
 but as soon as I begin in earnest to recover from starvation , loss , and loneliness , my heart be draw to this grand old man , who have see so many trouble . he have be here and there in the world so much , and deal with so many people , that the natural frankness of his mind be sharpen into caution . but any weak and helpless person still could get the good of he ; and his shrewdness certainly do not spring from any form of bitterness . he be rough in his way sometimes , and could not bear to be contradict when he be sure that he be right , which generally happen to he . but above all thing he have one very great peculiarity , to my mind highly vexatious , because it seem so unaccountable . Sampson Gundry have a very low opinion of feminine intellect . he never show this contempt in any unpleasant way , and indeed he never , perhaps , display it in any positive saying . but as I grow old and begin to argue , sure I be that it be there ; and it always provoke I tenfold as much by seem to need no assertion , but to stand as some great axiom . 
 the other member of the household be his grandson Ephraim   or " firm " Gundry , the indian woman Suan Isco , and a couple of help , of race or nation almost unknown to themselves . Suan Isco belong to a tribe of respectable Black Rock Indians , and have be the wife of a chief among they , and the mother of several child . but Klamath Indians , enemy of theirs   who carry off the lady of the cattle ranch , and afterward shoot Elijah , have Suan Isco in their possession , have murder her husband and child , and be use she as a mere beast of burden , when Sampson Gundry fall on they . he , with his follower , be enrage at the cold - blooded death of Elijah , fall on those miscreant to such purpose that woman and child alone be leave to hand down their bad propensity . 
 but the white man rescue and bring away the steal wife of the stockman , and also the widow of the Black Rock chief . she be in such poor condition and so broken - hearted that none but the fine humanity would have consider her worth a quarter of the trouble of her carriage . but she prove to be worth it a thousandfold ; and Sawyer Gundry   as now he be call   know by this time all the value of uncultivated gratitude . and her virtue be so many that it take a long time to find they out , for she never put they forward , not know whether they be good or bad . 
 until I know these people , and the pure depth of their kindness , it be a continual grief to I to be a burden upon they . but when I come to understand they and their simple greatness , the only thing I be ashamed of be my own mistrust of they . not that I expect ever that any harm would be do to I , only that I know myself to have no claim on any one . 
 one day , when I be fit for nothing but to dwell on trouble , Sampson Gundry 's grandson " firm " as he be call for Ephraim run up the stair to the little room where I be sit by myself . 
 " Miss Rema , will you come with we ? " he say , in his deep , slow style of speech . " we be go up the mountain , to haul down the great tree to the mill . " 
 " to be sure I will come , " I answer , gladly . " what great tree be it , Mr. Ephraim ? " 
 " the large tree any where near here the one we cut down last winter . ten day it take to cut it down . if I could have save it , it should have stand . but grandfather do it to prove his right . we shall have a rare job to lead it home , and I doubt if we can tackle it . I think you might like to see we try . " 
 in less than a minute I be ready , for the warmth and softness of the air make cloak or shawl unbearable . but when I run down to the yard of the mill , Mr. Gundry , who be give order , come up and give I an order too . 
 " you must not go like this , my dear . we have three thousand foot to go upward . the air will be sharp up there , and I doubt if we shall be home by night - fall . Run , Suan , and fetch the young lady 's cloak , and a pair of thick boot for change . " 
 Suan Isco never run . that manner of motion be foreign to she , at least as we accomplish it . when speed be require , she attain it by increase length of stride and great vigor of heel . in this way she conquer distance steadily , and with very little noise . 
 the air , and the light , and the beauty of the mountain be a sudden joy to I . in front of we all strode Sampson Gundry , clear all tangle with a short , sharp axe , and mount steep place as if twoscore be strike off his threescore year and five . from time to time he turn round to laugh , or see that his man and train bullock be right ; and then , as his bright eye meet my dark one , he seem to be sorry for the noise he make . on the other hand , I be ashamed of damp any one 's pleasure by be there . 
 but I need not have feel any fear about this . like all other child , I wrap myself up too much in my own importance , and behave as if my state of mind be a thing to be consider . but the long we rise through the freedom and the height , the light grow the heart of every one , until the thick forest of pine close round we , and we walk in a silence that might be feel . 
 hence we issue forth upon the rough bare rock , and after much trouble with the cattle , and some bruise , stand pant on a rugged cone , or crest , which have once be crown with a Titan of a tree . the tree be still there , but not its glory ; for , alas ! the mighty trunk lie prostrate a grander column than ever be or will be build by human hand . the tapering shaft stretch out of sight for something like a furlong , and the bulk of the butt rise over we so that we could not see the mountain . have never see any such tree before , I must have be amazed if I have be old enough to comprehend it . 
 Sampson Gundry , large as he be , and accustom to almost every thing , collect his man and the whole of his team on the ground - floor or area of the stump before he would say any thing . here we all look so sadly small that several of the man begin to laugh ; the bullock seem nothing but raccoon or beaver to run on the branch or the fibre of the tree ; and the chain and the shackle , and the block and crane , and all the rest of the thing they mean to use , seem nothing whatever , or at all to be consider , except as a spider 's web upon this tree . 
 the sagacious bullock , who know quite well what they be expect to do , look blank . some rub their horn into one another be sadly , and some cock their tail because they feel that they could not be call upon to work . the light of the afternoon sun come glance along the vast pillar , and light its die hue cinnamon , purple , and glabrous red , and soft gray where the lichen grow . 
 every body look at Mr. Gundry , and he begin to cough a little , have have lately some trouble with his throat . then in his sturdy manner he speak the truth , accord to his nature . he set his great square shoulder against the butt of the tree , and deliver himself : 
 " friend and neighbor , and hand of my own , I be take in here , and I own to it . it serve I right for disbelieve what my grandson , Firm Gundry , say . I know that the tree be a big one , of course , as every body else do ; but till you see a tree lay upon earth you get no grip of his girth , no more than you do of a man till he lieth a corpse . at the time of felling I could not come anigh he , by reason of an accident ; and I have some word with this boy about it , which keep I away ever since that time . firm , you be right , and I be wrong . it be a real shame , now I see it , to throw down the ' King of the Mountains . ' but , for all that , be down , we must use he . he shall be saw into fifty - foot length . and I invite you all to come again , for six or seven good turn at he . " 
 at the hearing of this , a cheer arise , not only for the Sawyer 's manly truth , but also for his hospitality ; because on each of these visit to the mountain he be the host , and his supply be good . but before the descent with the empty team begin , young Ephraim do what appear to I to be a gallant and straightforward thing . he stand on the chine of the fall monster , forty foot above we , have gain the post of vantage by activity and strength , and he ask if he might say a word or two . 
 " say away , lad , " cry his grandfather , supposing , perhaps , in his obstinate way   for truly he be very obstinate , that his grandson be go now to clear himself from art or part in the murder of that tree an act which have rouse indignation over a hundred league of lowland . 
 " neighbor , " say Firm , in a clear young voice , which shake at first with diffidence , " we all have to thank you , more than I can tell , for come to help we with this job . it be a job which require to be do for legal reason which I do not understand , but no doubt they be good one . for that we have my grandfather 's word ; and no one , I think , will gainsay it . now , have go so far , we will not be beat by it , or else we shall not be Americans . " 
 these simple word be receive with great applause ; and an orator , stand on the large stump to be find even in America , deliver a speech which be very good to hear , but need not now be repeat . and Mr. Gundry 's eye be moist with pleasure at his grandson 's conduct . 
 " Firm knoweth the right thing to do , " he say ; " and like a man he doeth it . but whatever aileth you , Miss Rema , and what can ' e see in the distance yonner ? never mind , my dear , then . tell I by - and - by , when none of these folk be ' longside of we . " 
 but I could not bear to tell he , till he force it from I under pain of his displeasure . I have spy on the sky - line far above we , in the desert track of mountain , the very gap in which my father stand and bid I seek this landmark . his memory be true , and his eyesight also ; but the great tree have be fell . the death of the " King of the Mountains " have lead to the death of the king of mankind , so far as my little world contain one . 




 CHAPTER V 

 UNCLE SAM 

 the influence of the place in which I live begin to grow on I . the warmth of the climate and the cloud of soft and fertile dust be break by the refresh rush of water and the clear soft green of leaf . we have fruit tree of almost every kind , from the peach to the amber cherry , and countless oak by the side of the river not large , but most fantastic . here I use to sit and wonder , in a foolish , childish way , whether on earth there be any other child so strangely place as I be . of course there be thousand far bad off , more desolate and destitute , but be there any more thickly wrap in mystery and loneliness ? 
 a wanderer as I have be for year , together with my father , change of place have not supply the knowledge which flow from lapse of time . faith , and warmth , and trust in other have not be dash out of I by any rude blow of the world , as happen with unlucky child huddle together in large city . my father have never allow I much acquaintance with other child ; for six year he have leave I with a community of lay sister , in a little town of Languedoc , where I be the only pupil , and where I be to remain as I be bear , a simple heretic . those sister be very good to I , and teach I as much as I could take of secular accomplishment . and it be a bitter day for I when I leave they for America . 
 for during those six year I have see my father at long interval , and have almost forget the early day when I be always with he . I use to be the one little comfort of his perpetual wandering , when I be a careless child , and say thing to amuse he . not that he ever play with I any more than he play with any thing ; but I be the last of his seven child , and he like to watch I grow . I never know it , I never guess it , until he give his life for mine ; but , poor little common thing as I be , I become his only tie to earth . even to I he be never love , in the way some father be . he never call I by pet name , nor dandle I on his knee , nor kiss I , nor stroke down my hair and smile . such thing I never expect of he , and therefore never miss they ; I do not even know that happy child always have they . 
 but one thing I know , which be not always know to happy child : I have the pleasure of know my own name . my name be an english one Castlewood and by birth I be an english girl , though of England I know nothing , and at one time speak and think most easily in French . but my longing have always be for England , and for the sound of english voice and the quietude of english way . in the chatter and heat and drought of South France some faint remembrance of a greener , cool , and more silent country seem to touch I now and then . but where in England I have live , or when I have leave that country , or whether I have relation there , and why I be doom to be a foreign girl all these question be but as curl wisps of cloud on memory 's sky . 
 of such thing   much as I long to know a good deal more about they   I never have dare to ask my father ; nor even could I , in a roundabout way , such as clever child have , get second - hand information . in the first place , I be not a clever child ; for the next point , I never have underhand skill ; and finally , there be no one near I who know any thing about I . like all other girl and perhaps the very same tendency be to be find in boy I have strong though hazy idea of caste . the noble sense of equality , fraternity , and so on , seem to come later in life than childhood , which be an age of ambition . I do not know who in the world I be , but feel quite sure of be somebody . 
 one day , when the great tree have be saw into length , and with the aid of many team bring home , and the pit and the hoist tackle be be prepare and strengthen to deal with it , Mr. Gundry , be full of the subject , declare that he would have his dinner in the mill yard . he be anxious to watch , without loss of time , the settlement of some heavy timber newly sink in the river 's bed , to defend the outwork of the mill . have his good leave to bring he his pipe , I find he sit upon a bench with a level fix before he , and his empty plate and cup lay by , among a great litter of tool and thing . he be look along the level with one eye shut , and the other most sternly intent ; but when I come near he rise and raise his broad pith hat , and make I think that I be not interrupt he . 
 " here be your pipe , Uncle Sam , " I say ; for , in spite of all his formal way , I would not be afraid of he . I have know he now quite long enough to be sure he be good and kind . and I know that the world around these part be divide into two hemisphere , the well half be of those who love , and the base half make of those who hat , Sawyer Sampson Gundry . 
 " what a queer world it be ! " say Mr. Gundry , accept his pipe to consider that point . " who ever would have dream , fifty year agone , that your father 's daughter would ever have come with a pipe to light for my father 's son ? " 
 " Uncle Sam , " I reply , as he slowly begin to make those puff which seem to be of the high essence of pleasure , and wisps of blue smoke flit through his white eyebrow and among the snowy curl of hair " dear Uncle Sam , I be sure that it would be an honor to a princess to light a pipe for a man like you . " 
 " Miss Rema , I should rather you would talk no nonsense , " he answer , very shortly , and he set his eye along his level , as if I have offend he . not know how to assert myself and declare that I have speak my honest thought , I merely sit down on the bench and wait for he to speak again to I . but he make believe to be very busy , and scarcely to know that I be there . I have a great mind to cry , but resolve not to do it . 
 " why , how be this ? what be the matter ? " he exclaim at last , when I have be watch the water so long that I sigh to know where it be go to . " why , missy , you look as if you have never a friend in all the wide world leave . " 
 " then I must look very ungrateful , " I say ; " for at any rate I have one , and a good one . " 
 " and do not   you know of any one but I , my dear ? " 
 " you and Suan Isco and Firm those be all I have any knowledge of . " 
 " ' tis a plenty to my mind , almost too many . my plan be to be a good friend to all , but not let too many be friend with I . rest you quite satisfied with three , Miss Rema . I have live a good many year , and I never have more than three friend worth a puff of my pipe . " 
 " but one 's own relation , Uncle Sam people quite nearly related to we : it be impossible for they to be unkind , you know . " 
 " do I , my dear ? then I wish that I do . except one 's own father and mother , there be not much to be hop for out of they . my own brother take a twist against I because I try to save he from ruin ; and if any man ever wish I ill , he do . and I think that your father have the same tale to tell . but there ! I know nothing whatever about that . " 
 " now you do , Mr. Gundry ; I be certain that you do , and beg you to tell I , or rather I demand it . I be old enough now , and I be certain my dear father would have wish I to know every thing . whatever it be , I be sure that he be right ; and until I know that , I shall always be the most miserable of the miserable . " 
 the Sawyer look at I as if he could not enter into my meaning , and his broad , short nose and quiet eye be beset with wrinkle of inquiry . he quite forget his level and his great post in the river , and tilt back his ancient hat , and let his pipe rest on his big brown arm . " Lord bless I ! " he say , " what a young gal you be ! or , at least , what a young Miss Rema . what good can you do , miss , by make of a rout ? here you be in as quiet a place as you could find , and all of we like and pity you . your father be a wise man to settle you here in this enlightened continent . let the doggoned old folk t'other side of the world think out their own flustration . a female young American you be now , and a very fine speciman you will grow . ' tis the fine thing to be on all God 's earth . " 
 " no , Mr. Gundry , I be an english girl , and I mean to be an Englishwoman . the Americans may be more kind and generous , and perhaps my father think so , and bring I here for that reason . and I may be glad to come back to you again when I have do what I be bind to do . remember that I be the last of seven child , and do not even know where the rest be bury . " 
 " now look straight afore you , missy . what do you see yonner ? " the Sawyer be get a little tired , perhaps , of this long interruption . 
 " I see enormous log , and a quantity of saw , and tool I do not   even know the name of . also I see a bright , swift river . " 
 " but over here , missy , between they two oak . what do you please to see there , Miss Rema ? " 
 " what I see there , of course , be a great saw - mill . " 
 " but it would not   have be ' of course , ' and it would not   have be at all , if I have spend all my day a - dwelling on the injury of my family . could I have put that there unekaled sample of water - power and human ingenuity together without labor hard for whole month of a stretch , except upon the Sabbath , and lay awake night after night , and bend all my intellect over it ? and could I have do that , think you now , if my heart be a - moon upon family wrong , and this , that , and the other ? " 
 here Sampson Gundry turn full upon I , and fold his arm , and spread his great chin upon his deer - skin apron , and nod briskly with his deep gray eye , survey I in triumph . to his mind , that mill be the wonder of the world , and any argument base upon it , with or without coherence , be , like its circular saw , irresistible . and yet he think that woman can not reason ! however , I do not say another word just then , but give way to he , as behoove a child . and not only that , but I always find he too good to be argue with too kind , I mean , and large of heart , and wed to his own peculiar turn . there be nothing about he that one could dislike , or strike fire at , and be captious ; and he always proceed with such pity for those who be oppose to he that they always know they must be wrong , though he be too polite to tell they so . and he have such a pleasant , paternal way of look down into one 's little thought when he put on his spectacle , that to say any more be to hazard the risk of ungrateful inexperience . 




 CHAPTER VI 

 a BRITISHER 

 the beautiful Blue River come from the jagged depth of the mountain , full of light and liveliness . it have scarcely run six mile from its source before it touch our mill - wheel ; but in that space and time it have gather strong and copious volume . the lovely blue of the water   like the inner tint of a glacier   be partly due to its origin , perhaps , and partly to the rich , soft tone of the granite sand spread under it . whatever the cause may have be , the river well deserve its title . 
 it be so bright and pure a blue , so limpid and pellucid , that it even seem to out - vie the tint of the sky which it reflect , and the myriad spark of sunshine on it twinkle like a crystal rain . plod through the parched and scorch dust of the mountain - foot , through the stifle vapor and the blinding , ochreous glare , the traveler suddenly come upon this cool and calm delight . it be not to be descry afar , for it lie below the level , and the oak and other tree of shelter scarcely top the narrow comb . there be no canyon , such as be and some of they know over all the world both to the north and south of it . the Blue River do not owe its birth to any fierce convulsion , but sparkle on its cheerful way without impend horror . stand here as a child , and thinking , from the manner of my father , that strong man never weep nor own the conquest of emotion , I feel sometimes a fool 's contempt for the gush transport of brave man . for instance , I have see a miner , or a tamer of horse , or a rough fur - hunter , or   perhaps the brave of all   a man of science and topography , jade , worn , and nearly dead with drought and dearth and choking , suddenly , and beyond all hope , strike on this bury Eden . and then he drop on his knee and spread his starve hand upward , if he could , and thank the God who make he , till his head go round , and who know what remembrance of love one come to he ? and then , if he have any moisture leave , he fall to a passion of weeping . 
 in childish ignorance I think that this man weakly degrade himself , and should have be bear a woman . but since that time I have truly learn that the brave of man be those who feel their maker 's Land most softly , and be not ashamed to pay the tribute of their weakness to he . 
 living , as we do , in a lonely place , and yet not far from a track along the crest of the great Californian plain from Sacramento southward , there be scarcely a week which do not bring we some traveler need comfort . Mr. Gundry use to be tell that if he would set up a rough hotel , or house of call for cattle - drover , miner , loafer , and so on , he might turn twice the money he could ever make by his thrive saw - mill . but he only use to laugh , and say that nature have make he too honest for that ; and he never think of charge any thing for his hospitality , though if a rich man leave a gold piece , or even a nugget , upon a shelf , as happen very often , Sawyer Gundry do not disdain to set it aside for a rainy day . and one of his rich or most lavish guest arrive on my account , perhaps . 
 it happen when daylight be grow short , and the red heat of the earth be go , and the snow - line of distant granite peak have creep already low , and the chatter bird that spend their summer in our band of oak - tree be begin to find their food get short , and to prime swift wing for the lowland ; and I , have never feel bitter cold , be tremble at what I hear of it . for now it be clear that I have no choice but to stay where I be for the present , and be truly thankful to God and man for have the chance of do so . for the little relic of my affair so far as I have any have take much time in arrangement , perhaps because it be so hard to find they . I know nothing , except about my own little common wardrobe , and could give no information about the content of my father 's package . but these , by dint of perseverance on the part of Ephraim   who be very keen about all right , have mainly be recover , and Mr. Gundry have do the good that could be do concern they . whatever seem of a private nature , or likely to prove important , have be bring home to Blue River Mills ; the rest have be sell , and have fetch large price , unless Mr. Gundry enlarge they . 
 he more than enlarge , he multiply they , as I find out long afterward , to make I think myself rich and grand , while a beggar upon his bounty . I have never be accustom to think of money , and feel some little contempt for it not , indeed , a lofty hatred , but a careless wonder why it seem to be always think of . it be one of the last thing I ever think of ; and those who be wait for it be until I get use to they oblige in self - duty to remind I . 
 this , however , be not my fault . I never dream of wrong they . but I have earn no practical knowledge of the great world any where , much though I have wander about , accord to vague recollection . the duty of pay have never be mine ; that important part have be do for I . and my father have such a horror always of any growth of avarice that he never give I sixpence . 
 and now , when I hear upon every side continual talk of money , from Suan Isco upward , I think at first that the New World must be different from the old one , and that the gold mine in the neighborhood must have make they full of it ; and once or twice I ask Uncle Sam ; but he only nod his head , and say that it be the practice every where . and before very long I begin to perceive that he do not exaggerate . 
 nothing could prove this point more clearly than the circumstance above refer to the arrival of a stranger , for the purpose of bribe even Uncle Sam himself . this happen in the month of November , when the pass be begin to be block with snow , and those of the high mountain tract have long be overwhelm with it . on this particular day the air be laden with gray , oppressive cloud , threaten a heavy downfall , and instead of fare forth , as usual , to my beloved river , I be keep in - door , and even up stair , by a violent snow - headache . this be a crush weight of pain , which all new - comer , or almost all , be oblige to endure , sometimes for as much as eight - and - forty hour , when the first great snow of the winter be breed , as they express it , overhead . but I be more lucky than most people be ; for after about twelve hour of almost intolerable throbbing , during which the sweetest sound be odious , and the idea of food quite loathsome , the agony leave I , and a great desire for something to eat succeed . Suan Isco , the kind of the kind , be go down stair at last , for which I feel ungrateful gratitude because she have be do she good to charm away my pain by low , monotonous indian ditty , which make it ten time bad ; and yet I could not find heart to tell she so . 
 now it must have be past six o'clock in the evening of the November day when the avalanche slide off my head , and I be able to lift it . the light of the west have be faint , and be dead ; though often it use to prolong our day by the backward glance of the ocean . with pang of youthful hunger , but a head still weak and dazy , I grope my way in the dark through the passage and down the stair of redwood . 
 at the bottom , where a railed landing be , and the door open into the house - room , I be surprised to find that , instead of the usual cheerful company enjoy themselves by the fire - light , there be only two people present . the Sawyer sit stiffly in his chair of state , delay even the indulgence of his pipe , and have his face set sternly , as I have never before beheld it . in the visitor 's corner , as we call it , where people sit to dry themselves , there be a man , and only one . 
 something tell I that I have well keep back and not disturb they . the room be not in its usual state of comfort and hospitality . some kind of meal have be make at the table , as always must be in these part ; but not of the genial , reckless sort which random traveler carry on without any check from the Sawyer . for he of all man ever bear in a civilized age be the fine host , and a guest beneath his roof be sacred as a lady to a knight . hence it happen that I be much surprised . proper conduct almost compel I to withdraw ; but curiosity make I take just one more little peep , perhaps . look back at these thing now , I can not be sure of every thing ; and indeed if I could , I must have an almost supernatural memory . but I remember many thing ; and the headache may have clear my mind . 
 the stranger who have bring Mr. Gundry 's humor into such stiff condition be sit in the corner , a nook where light and shadow make an eddy . he seem to be perfectly unconcerned about all the trick of the hearth flame , present as he do a most solid face for any light to play upon . to I it seem to be a weather - beat face of a bluff and resolute man , the like of which we attribute to John Bull . at any rate , he be like John Bull in one respect : he be sturdy and square , and fit to hold his own with any man . 
 stranger of this sort have come   as Englishmen rove every where , and be kindly welcome by Uncle Sam , who , be of recent English blood , have a kind of hanker after it , and would almost rather have such at his board than even a true - bear American ; and infinitely more welcome be they than Frenchman , Spaniard , or German , or any man not to be distinguish , as be the case with some of they . even now it be clear that the Sawyer have not grudge any token of honor , for the tall , square , brazen candlestick , of Boston make , be on the table , and very little light they give . the fire , however , be grandly roar of stub - oak and pine antler , and the black grill of the chimney brick be fringe with lift filament . it be a rich , ripe light , afford breadth and play for shadow ; and the face of the two man glisten , and darken in their crease . 
 I be dress in black , and could not be see , though I could see they so clearly ; and I doubt whether to pass through , upon my way to the larder , or return to my room and starve a little long ; for I do not wish to interrupt , and have no idea of listen . but suddenly I be compel to stop ; and to listen become an honest thing , when I know what be speak of or , at any rate , I do it . 
 " Castlewood , Master Colonist ; Castlewood be the name of the man that I have come to ask about . and you will find it worth your while to tell I all you know of he . " thus speak the Englishman sit in the corner ; and he seem to be certain of produce his effect . 
 " Wal , " say Uncle Sam , assume what all true briton believe to be the universal Yankee tone , while I know that he be laugh in his sleeve , " squire , I guess that you may be right . consideration of that ' ere kind desarve to be consider of . " 
 " just so . I know that you must see it , " the stranger continue , bravely . " a stiff upper lip , as you call it here , be all very well to begin with . but all you enlighten member of the great republic know what be what . it will bring you more than ten year ' income of your saw - mill , and farm , and so on , to deal honestly with I for ten minute . no more beat about the bush and fence with I , as you have do . now can you see your own interest ? " 
 " I never be reckon a fool at that . squire , make track , and be do with it . " 
 " then , Master Colonist , or Colonel for I believe you be all colonel here your task be very simple . we want clear proof , swear properly and attest duly , of the death of a villain George Castlewood , otherwise the honorable George Castlewood , otherwise Lord Castlewood : a man who murder his own father ten year ago this November : a man commit for trial for the crime , but who bribe his jailer and escape , and wander all over the continent . what be that noise ? have you get rat ? " 
 " plenty of foreign rat , and native ' coon , and skunk , and other varmint . Wal , Squire , go on with it . " 
 the voice of Uncle Sam be stern , and his face full of rise fury , as I , who have make that noise in my horror , try to hush my heart with patience . 
 " the story be well know , " continue the stranger : " we need make no bone of it . George Castlewood go about under a curse " 
 " not quite so loud , Squire , if you please . my household be not altogether season . " 
 " and perhaps you have get the young lady somewhere . I hear a report to that effect . but here you think nothing of a dozen murder . now , Gundry , let we have no squeamishness . we only want justice , and we can pay for it . ten thousand dollar I be authorize to offer for a mere act of duty on your part . we have an extradition treaty . if the man have be alive , we must have have he . but as he have cheat the hangman by die , we can only see his grave and have evidence . and all well - dispose people must rejoice to have such a quiet end of it . for the family be so well know , you see . " 
 " I see , " Mr. Gundry answer , quietly , lay a finger on his lip . " guess you want something more than that , though , Squire . be there nothing more than the grave to oblige a noble Britisher with ? " 
 " yes , Colonel ; we want the girl as well . we know that she be with he in that caravan , or wagon train , or whatever you please to call it . we know that you have make oath of his death , produce his child , and obtain his trunk , and draw his share in the insurance job . your law must be queer to let you do such thing . in England it would have take at least three year , and cost a deal more than the thing be worth , even without a Chancery suit . however , of his paper I shall take possession ; they can be of no earthly use to you . " 
 " to be sure . and possession of his darter too , without so much as a Chancery suit . but what be to satisfy I , Squire , agin go wrong in this little transaction ? " 
 " I can very soon satisfy you , " say the stranger , " as to their identity . here be their full , particular , and correct description name , weight , and color of the party . "

 CHAPTER VII 

 DISCOMFITURE 

 the Englishman draw forth a double eyeglass from a red velvet waistcoat , and mount it on his broad nose , come near to get the full light of the candle .  CHAPTER VIII 

 a doubtful loss 

 when I try to look out of my window in the morning , I be quite astonished at the state of thing . to look out fairly be impossible ; for not only be all the low part of the frame hillocke up like a sandglass , and the side fill in with dusky plait , but even in the middle , where some outlook be , it lead to very little . all the air seem choke with snow , and the ground come up in pile to meet it ; all sound be deaden in the thick gray hush , and nothing have its own proportion . never have see such a thing before , I be frightened , and long to know more of it .

"

" turn the log up , firm , and put the pan on . you boy can go on without victual all day , but an old man must feed regular . and , bad as he be , I thank God for send he on his way home with his belly full . if ever he turneth up in the snow , that much can be prove to my account . " 
 Young as I be , and little practice in the way of settler , I could not help perceive that Uncle Sam be very much put out not at the death of the man so sadly , as at the worry of his die so in go from a hospitable house .  " why , Ephraim , of course , Uncle Sam ; every body say that nobody else could have notice such a thing at such a distance . "

 the Sawyer rub his chin , which be large enough for a great deal of rub ; and when he do that , I be always sure that an argument go to his liking . he say nothing more for the present , but have his dinner , and enjoy it . 
 " suppose now that he do all that , " he resume , about an hour afterward , " be firm the sort of boy you would look to to lose his own self in a snow - drift ? he have three man with he , and he be worth all three , let alone the big dog Jowler , who have dig out forty foot of snow ere now . if that rogue of an Englishman , Goad , have have the luck to cheat the hangman , and the honor to die in a Californy snow - drift , you may take my experience for it , missy , Firm and Jowler will find he , and clear Uncle Sam 's reputation . " 




 CHAPTER ix 

 WATER - spout 

 if Mr. Gundry be in one way right , he be equally wrong in the other . Firm come home quite safe and sound , though smother with snow and most hungry ; but he think that he should have staid out all the night , because he have fail of his errand . Jowler also be full of discontent and trouble of conscience . he know , when he kick up his heel in the snow , that his duty be to find somebody , and be of Alpine pedigree , and train to act up to his ancestry , he now drop his tail with failure . 
 " it come to the same thing , " say Sawyer Gundry ; " it be foolish to be so particular . a thousand well man have sink through be so pig - head . we shall find the rogue toward the end of March , or in April , if the season suit . firm , eat your supper and shake yourself . " 
 this be exactly the Sawyer 's way to take thing quietly when convince that there be no chance to better they . he would always do his good about the small trifle ; but after that , be the matter small or great , he have a smile face for the end of it . 
 the winter , with all its weight of sameness and of dreariness , go at last , and the lovely spring from the soft Pacific find its gradual way to we . accustom as I be to gentle climate and more easy change , I lose myself in admiration of this my first californian spring . the flower , the league and league of flower , that burst into color and harmony purple , yellow , and delicate lilac , weave with bright crimson thread , and fringe with emerald - green by the bank , and blue by the course of river , while deepen here and there by woode shelter and cool place , with the silver - gray of the soft Pacific wan in far distance , and silken vapor draw toward the card fork of the mountain range ; and over all the never - weary azure of the limpid sky : child as I be , and full of little worldly trouble on my own account , these grand and noble sight enlarge I without any thinking . 
 the wheat and the maize be grow apace , and bean come into full blossom , and the peach swing in the western breeze be almost as large as walnut , and all thing in their prime of freshness , ere the yellow dust arrive , when a sudden melting of snow in some gully send a strong flood down our Blue River . the saw - mill happen to be hard at work ; and before the gear could be lift , some damage be do to the float by the heavy , impetuous rush of the torrent . Uncle Sam be away , and so be firm ; from which , perhaps , the mischief grow . however , the blame be all put on the river , and little more be say of it . 
 the follow morning I go down before even Firm be out - of - door , under some touch , perhaps , of natural desire to know thing . the stream be as pure and bright as ever , hasten down its gravel - path of fine granite just as usual , except that it have more volume and a strong sense of freshness . only the bent of the grass and the swath of the pendulous twig down stream remain to show that there must have be some violence quite lately . 
 all Mr. Gundry 's strengthen pile and shore be as firm as need be , and the clear blue water play around they as if they be no constraint to it . and none but a practiced eye could see that the great wheel have be wound , be undershot , and lift now above the power of the current , accord to the fine old plan of lock the door when the horse be go . 
 when I be look up and wonder where to find the mischief , Martin , the foreman , come out and cross the plank , with his mouth full of breakfast .

 " I have no idea what you mean , " I answer . " if you have be careless , that be no concern of mine . " 
 " Careless , indeed ! and the way I work , when other be a - snorin ' in their bed ! I might just as well do nort , every bit , and get more thank and well wage . that be the way of the world all over . come Saturday week , I shall better myself . " 
 " but if it be the way of the world all over , how will you well yourself , unless you go out of the world altogether ! " I put this question to Martin with the earnest simplicity of the young , mean no kind of sarcasm , but know that scarcely a week go by without his threatening to " well himself . " and they say that he have do so for seven year or more . 
 " do not   you be too sharp , " he reply , with a grim smile , partly at himself , perhaps . " if half as I hear about you be true , you will want all your sharpness for yourself , Miss Remy . and the Britishers be bad than we be . "

Martin be the only one who ever grumble , and he have establish a long right to do so by never himself be grumble at .

 " we all must have our little mistake , " continue Sawyer Gundry ; " but I never like to push a man when he feel it . I shall not say a syllable to Martin ; and , Ephraim , you will do the like . when a fellow stick well to his work like Martin , never blame he for a mere accident . "

 " I shall just go down and put it right myself . Martin be a poor hand at repair . firm , you go up the gulch , and see if the fresh have hurt the hurdle . "

 I do not dare as yet to think what really prove to be true in the end that I could not draw the wheel correctly because itself be incorrect . in spite of all Mr. Gundry 's skill and labor and ingenuity , the wheel be no true circle . the error begin in the hub itself , and increase , of course , with the distance ; but still it work very well , like many other thing that be not perfect .

 presently I hear a harsh metallic sound and creaking of machinery . the bite , or clamp , or whatever they be call , be be put on , to keep the wheel from revolve with the Sawyer 's weight . Martin , the foreman , be grumble and growl , accord to his habit , and peer through the slot , or channel of stone , in which the axle work , and the cheery voice of Mr. Gundry be put down his objection . be much too large to pass through the slot , Mr. Gundry come round the corner of the building , with a heavy leathern bag of tool strap round his neck , and his canvas breech girt above his knee . but the foreman staid inside to hand he the needful material into the wheel .

 at any rate , I be so engross that I scarcely observe the change light , except as a hindrance to my work and a trouble to my distance , till suddenly some great drop fall upon my paper and upon my hat , and a rush of dark wind almost sweep I from the log upon which I sit . then again all be a perfect calm , and the young leaf over the stream hang heavily on their tender foot - stalk , and the point of the breeze - sweep grass turn back , and the ruffle of all thing smooth itself . but there seem to be a sense of fear in the wait silence of earth and air . 
 this deep , unnatural stillness scar I , and I make up my mind to run away . but the hammer of the Sawyer sound as I have never hear it sound . he be much too hard at work to pay any heed to sky or stream , and the fall of his stroke be dead and hollow , as if the place resent they . 
 " come away , come away , " I cry , as I run and stand on the opposite bank to he ; " there be something quite wrong in the weather , I be sure . I entreat you to come away at once , Uncle Sam . every thing be so strange and odd . " 
 " why , what be to do now ? " ask the Sawyer , come to my side of the wheel and look at I , with his spectacle tilt up , and his apron wedge in a piece of timber , and his solid figure rest in the impossibility of hurry . " Missy , do not   you make a noise out there . you can not   have your own way always . " 
 " oh , Uncle Sam , do not   talk like that . I be in such a fright about you . do come out and look at the mountain . " 
 " I have see the mountain often enough , and I be up to every trick of they . there may be a corn or two of rain ; no more . my sea - weed be like tinder . there can not   be no heavy storm when it be like that . do not   you make pretense , missy , to know what be beyond you . " 
 Uncle Sam be so seldom cross that I always feel that he have a right to be so . and he give I one of his noble smile to make up for the sharpness of his word , and then back he go to his work again . so I hop that I be altogether wrong , till a bolt of lightning , like a blue dagger , fall at my very foot , and a crash of thunder shake the earth and stun I . these open the sluice of the heaven , and before I could call out I be drench with rain . cling to a bush , I see the valley lash with cloudy blast , and a whirling mass of spiral darkness rush like a giant toward I . and the hissing and tossing and roar mix whatever be in sight together .

 CHAPTER XII 

 GOLD and GRIEF

 CHAPTER XIII 

 the SAWYER 's PRAYER 

 the darkness of young summer night be fall on earth and tree and stream . every thing look of a different form and color from those of an hour ago , and the rich bloom of shadow mix with color , and cast by snowy mountain , which have store the purple adieu of the sun , be fill the air with delicious calm . the Sawyer run out with his shirt sleeve shin , so that any sneaking foe might shoot he ; but , with the instinct of a settler , he have catch up his rifle . I stand beneath a carob - tree , which have be plant near the porch , and fling fantastic tassel down , like the ear - ring of a negress . and not have sense enough to do good , I be only able to be frightened . 
 listen intently , I hear the sound of skirre step on the other side of and some way down the river ; and the peculiar tread , even thus far off , be plainly Suan Isco 's . and then in the stillness a weary and heavy foot go toil after it . before I could follow , which I long to do , to learn at once the bad of it , I see the figure of a man much near , and even within twenty yard of I , glide along without any sound . faint as the light be , I feel sure that it be not one of our own man , and the barrel of a long gun upon his shoulder make a black line among silver leaf . " as he generally do when satisfy . 
 so scared be I that I catch hold of a cluster of pod to steady I ; and then , without any more fear for myself , I run to see whether it be possible to help . but the poor man lie beyond earthly help ; he be too dead to palpitate . his life must have leave he in the air , and he could not even have feel his fall . 
 in violent terror , I burst into tear , and lift his heavy head , and strove to force his hot hand open , and do I know not what , without think , labor only to recall his life . 
 " be you grieve for the skulk who have shoot my firm ? " say a stern voice quite unknown to I ; and rise , I look at the face of Mr. Gundry , unlike the countenance of Uncle Sam . I try to speak to he , but be too frightened . the wrath of blood be in his face , and all his kind desire be go . 
 " yes , like a girl , you be sorry for a man who have stain this earth , till his only atonement be to stain it with his blood . Captain Pedro , there you lie , shot , like a coward , through the back . I wish you be alive to taste my boot . murderer of man and filthy ravisher of woman , miscreant of God , how can I keep from trample on you ? " 
 it never have be in my dream that a good man could so entirely forget himself . I want to think that it must be somebody else , and not our Uncle Sam . but he look toward the west , as all man do when their spirit be full of death , and the wan light show that his chin be triple . 
 whether it may have be right or wrong , I make all haste to get away . the face of the dead man be quite a pleasant thing , compare with the face of the old man live . he may not have mean it , and I hope he never do , but beyond all controversy he look barbarous for the moment . 
 as I slip away , to know the bad , there I see he stand still , long to kick the vile man 's corpse , but quiet by the great awe of death . if the man have stir , or breathe , or even moan , the live man would have lose all reverence in his fury . but the power of the other world be great than even revenge could trample on . he let it lie there , and he stoop his head , and go away quite softly . 
 my little foolish heart be bitterly visit by a thing like this . the Sawyer , though not of great human rank , be gift with the large human nature that I have ever meet with . and though it be impossible as yet to think , a hollow depression , as at the loss of some great ideal , come over I . 
 return wretchedly to the house , I meet Suan Isco and two man bring the body of poor firm . his head and both his arm hang down , and they want somebody to lift they ; and this I run to do , although they call out to I not to meddle . the body be carry in , and lay upon three chair , with a pillow at the head ; and then a light be strike , and a candle bring by somebody or other . and Suan Isco sit upon the floor , and set up a miserable indian dirge .

Missy , keep his head up . "
