 " Almighty Father of the living and the dead , I have live long , and shall soon be dead , and my day have be full of trouble . but I never have such trouble as this here before , and I do not   think I ever shall get over it . I have sin every day of my life , and not think of Thee , but of victual , and money , and stuff ; and nobody know , but myself and Thou , all the little bad thing inside of I . I care a deal more to be respectable and get on with my business than to be prepare for kingdom come . and I have just be proud about the shooting of a villain , who might ' a go free and repent . there be nobody leave to I in my old age . Thou hast take all of they . Thou know what be right . please to do it . amen . " 




 CHAPTER XIV 

 not far to seek 

 in the present state of controversy most profoundly religious , the Lord alone can decide   though thousand of man would hurry to pronounce   for or against the orthodoxy of the ancient sawyer 's prayer . but if sound doctrine can be establish by success   as it always be , Uncle Sam 's theology must have be unusually sound ; for it please a gracious power to know what he want , and to grant it . 
 Brave as Mr. Gundry be , and much - endure and resign , the latter year of his life on earth must have drag on very heavily , with abstract resignation only , and none of his blood to care for he . be so obstinate a man , he might have never admit this , but prove against every one 's voice , except his own , his special blessedness . but this must have be a trial to he , and happily he be spar from it . 
 for although Firm have be very badly shot , and keep we for week in anxiety about he , his strong young constitution and well - nourish frame get over it . a truly good and learn doctor come from Sacramento , and we hang upon his word , and find that there he leave we hang . and this be the wise thing perhaps that he could do , because in America medical man be not absurdly expect , as they be in England , to do any good , but be value chiefly upon their power of predict what they can not help . and this man of science perceive that he might do harm to himself and his family by predict amiss , whereas he could do no good to his patient by predict rightly . and so he foretell both good and evil , to meet the intention of Providence . 
 he have not be send for in vain , however ; and to give he his due , he save Ephraim 's life , for he draw from the wound a large bullet , which , if leave , must have poison all his circulation , although it be make of pure silver . the Sawyer wish to keep this silver bullet as a token , but the doctor say that it belong to he accord to miner ' law ; and so it come to a moderate argument . each be a thoroughly stubborn man , accord to the bent of all good man , and reasoning increase their unreason . but the doctor win as indeed he deserve , for the extraction have be delicate because , when reason have be exhaust , he just say this :

 the leader of the robber , know far and wide as " Captain Pedro , " be bury where he fall ; and the whole so raise Uncle Sam 's reputation that his house be never attack again ; and if any bad character be force by circumstance to come near he , they never ask for any thing strong than ginger - beer or lemonade , and depart very promptly . for as soon as Ephraim Gundry could give account of his disaster , it be clear that Don Pedro owe his fate to a bottle of the Sawyer 's whiskey . Firm have only intend to give he a lesson for misbehavior , be fire by his grandfather 's word about swing I on the saddle . this idea have justly appear to he to demand a protest ; to deliver which he at once set forth with a valuable cowhide whip . come thus to the Rovers ' camp , and find their captain sit in the shade to digest his dinner , Firm lay hold of he by the neck , and give way to feeling of severity . Don Pedro regret his misconduct , and be lift up for the moment above his ordinary view , perceive that he might have do well , and shape the pattern of his tongue to it . firm , hear this , have good hope of he ; yet know how volatile repentance be , he strove to form a well - mark track for it . and when the captain cease to receive cowhide , he must have have it long enough to miss it . 
 now this might have end honorably and amicably for all concern , if the captain have know when he be well off . unluckily he have purloin a bottle of Mr. Gundry 's whiskey , and he draw the cork now to rub his stripe , and the smell of it move he to try it inside . and before very long his idea of honor , which he have sense enough to drop when sober , begin to come into his eye again , and to stir he up to mischief . hence it be that he follow Firm , who be rid home well satisfied , and appease his honor by shoot in cold blood , and justice by be shoot anyhow . 
 it be beautiful , through all this try time , to watch Uncle Sam 's proceeding : he appear so delightfully calm and almost careless whenever he be look at . and then he be ashamed of himself perpetually , if any one go on with it . nobody try to observe he , of course , or remark upon any of his doing , and for this he would become so grateful that he would long to tell all his thought , and then stop . this must have be a great worry to he , see how open his manner be ; and whenever he want to hide any thing , he inform we of that intention . so that we exhort Firm every day to come round and restore we to our usual state . this be the poor fellow 's special desire ; and often he be angry with himself , and make himself bad again by declare that he must be a milksop to lie there so long . whereas , it be much more near the truth that few other man , even in the Western States , would ever have get over such a wound . I be not learn enough to say exactly where the damage be , but the doctor call it , I think , the sternum , and pronounce that " a building - up process " be require , and must take a long time , if it ever could be do . 
 it be do at last , thank to Suan Isco , who scarcely ever leave he by day or night , and treat he skillfully with healing herb . but he , without mean it , vex she often by call for I a mere ignorant child . Suan be dreadfully jealous of this , and perhaps I be proud of that sentiment of her , and try to justify it , instead of labor to remove it , as would have be the more proper course . and Firm most ungratefully say that my hand be light than poor Suan 's , and every thing I do be well do , accord to he , which be shameful on his part , and as untrue as any thing could be . however , we yield to he in all thing while he be so delicate ; and it often make we poor weak thing cry to be the master of a tall strong man . 
 Firm Gundry receive that shot in May , about ten day before the twelvemonth be complete from my father 's death . the brightness of summer and beauty of autumn go by without his feel they , and while his system be work hard to fortify itself by wall up , as the learn man have call it . there have be some difficulty in this process , cause partly , perhaps , by our too lavish supply of the raw material ; and before Firm 's gap in his ' sternum " be stop , the mountain be come down upon we , as we always use to say when the snow - line stoop . in some season this be a sharp time of hurry , break with storm , and capricious , while man have to slur in the drive weather task that should have be mature long since . but in other year the long descent into the depth of winter be take not with a jump like that , but gently and softly and windingly , with a great many glimpse back at the summer , and a good deal of lean on the arm of the sun . 
 and so it be this time . the autumn and the winter for a fortnight stand look quietly at each other . they have quite agree to share the hour , to suit the arrangement of the sun . the night be starry and fresh and brisk , without any touch of tartness ; and the day be sunny and soft and gentle , without any sense of languor . it be a lovely scene blue shadow glide among golden light . 
 the Sawyer come forth , and cry , " what a shame ! this make I feel quite young again . and yet I have do not a stroke of work . no excuse ; make no excuse . I can do that pretty well for myself . praise God for all his mercy . I might do bad , perhaps , than have a pipe . " 
 then Firm come out to surprise he , and to please we all with the sight of himself . he steady his step with one great white hand upon his grandfather 's Sunday staff , and his clear blue eye be tremble with a sense of gratitude and a fear of tear . and I step behind a red strawberry - tree , for my sense of respect for he almost make I sob . 
 then Jowler think it high time to appear upon the scene , and convince we that he be not a dead dog yet . he have know tribulation , as his master have , and have find it a difficult thing to keep from the shadowy hunting ground of dog who have live a conscientious life . I have wonder at first what his reason could have be for not come forward , accord to his custom , to meet that troop of robber . but his reason , alas ! be too cogent to himself , though nobody else in that dreadful time could pay any attention to he . the Rovers , well know poor Jowler 's repute , and decline the fair mode of test it , have send in advance a very crafty scout , a half - breed Indian , who know as much about dog as they could ever hope to know about themselves . this rogue approach faithful Jowler so we be tell long afterward not in an upright way , but as if he have be a brother quadrupe . and he take advantage of the dog 's unfeigned surprise and interest to accost he with a piece of kidney contain a powerful poison . accord to all sound analogy , this should have stop the dear fellow 's earthly track ; but his spirit be such that he simply go away to nurse himself up in retirement . neither man nor dog can tell what agony he suffer ; and doubtless his torture of mind about duty unperforme be the bad of all . these thing be out of human knowledge in its present unsympathetic state . enough that poor Jowler come home at last , with his rib all up and his tail very low . 
 like friend who have come together again , almost from the jaw of death , we sit in the sunny noon , and thoroughly enjoy ourselves . the tree above we look proud and cheerful , lay aside the mere frippery of leaf with a good grace and contented arm , and a surety of have quite enough next spring . much of the fruity wealth of autumn still be cluster in our sight , heavily fetch the arched bough down to lessen the fall , when fall they must . and against the golden leaf of maple behind the unpretende roof a special wreath of blue shine like a climb Ipomaea . but come to examine this , one find it to be nothing more nor less than the smoke of the kitchen chimney , busy with a quiet roasting job . 
 this show how clear the air be ; but a thousand time as much could never tell how clear our spirit be . nobody make any " demonstration , " or cut any frolicsome caper , or even say any thing exuberant . the steadfast brood breed of England , which despise antic , be present in we all , and strengthen by a soil whose native growth be peril , chance , and marvel . and so we nod at one another , and I run over and courtesie to Uncle Sam , and he take I to he . 
 " you have be a dear good child , " he say , as he rise , and look over my head at Firm . " my own granddarter , if such there have be , could not have do more to comfort I , nor half so much , for aught I know . there be no picking and choose among the female , as God give they . but he have give you for a blessing and save to my old age , my dearie . " 
 " oh , Uncle Sam , now the nugget ! " I cry , desire like a child to escape deep feeling , and fear any strong word from Firm . " you have promise I ever so long that I should be the first to show Firm the nugget . " 
 " and so you shall , my dear , and firm shall see it before he be an hour old , and Jowler shall come down to show we where it be . " 
 Firm , who have little faith in the nugget , but take it for a dream of mine , and have prove conclusively from his pillow that it could not exist in earnest , now with a gentle , satirical smile declare his anxiety to see it ; and I lead he along by his well arm , fast , perhaps , than he ought to have walk . 
 in a very few minute we be at the place , and I run eagerly to point it ; but behold , where the nugget have be , there be nothing except the white bed of the river ! the blue water flow very softly on its way , without a gleam of gold to corrupt it . 
 " oh , nobody will ever believe I again ! " I exclaim , in the sad of sad dismay . " I dream about it first , but it never can have be a dream throughout . you know that I tell you about it , Uncle Sam , even when you be very busy , and that show that it never could have be a dream . " 
 " you tell I about it , I remember now , " Mr. Gundry answer , dryly ; " but it do not follow that there be such a thing . my dear , you may have imagine it ; because it be the proper time for it to come , when my good friend have no money to lend . your heart be so good that it get into your brain , and you must not be vex , my dear child ; it have do you good to dream of it . " 
 " I say so all along , " Firm observe . " Miss Rema feel that it ought to be , and so she believe that it must be , there . she be always so warm and trustful . " 
 " be that all you be good for ? " I cry , with no gratitude for his compliment . " as sure as I stand here , I see a great bowlder of gold , and so do Jowler , and I give you the piece that he bring up . do you take they all in a dream , Uncle Sam ? Come , can you get over that ? " 
 I assure you that for the moment I know not whether I stand upon my foot or head , until I perceive an extraordinary grin on the Sawyer 's ample countenance ; but Firm be not in the secret yet , for he gaze at I with compassion , and Uncle Sam look at we both as if he be balance our ability . 
 " send your dog in , missy , " at last he say . " he be more your dog than mine , I believe , and he obey you like a Christian . let he go and find it if he can . " 
 at a sign from I , the great dog dash in , and scratch with all four foot at once , and make the valley echo with the ring of mighty barking ; and in less than two minute there shine the nugget , as yellow and as big as ever . 
 " ha ! ha ! I never see a fine thing , " shout Uncle Sam , like a school - boy . " I be too many for you , missy dear ; but the old dog wollop the whole of we . I just shoot a barrow - load of gravel on your nugget , to keep it all snug till firm should come round ; and if the boy have never come round , there the gold might have wait the will of the Almighty . it be a big spot , anyhow . " 
 it certainly be not a little spot , though they all seem to make so light of it which vex I , because I have find it , and be as proud as if I have make it . not by any mean that the Sawyer be half as careless as he seem to be ; he put on much of this for my sake , have very lofty principle , especially concern the duty of the young . young people be never to have small idea , so far as he could help it , particularly upon such matter as Mammon , or the world , or fashion ; and not so very seldom he be oblige to catch himself up in his talking , when he chance to be go on and forget that I , who require a high vein of thought for my youth , be take his word downright ; and I think that all this have a great deal to do with his treat all that gold in such an exemplary manner ; for if it have really matter nothing , what make he go in the dark and shoot a great barrow - load of gravel over it ? 




 CHAPTER XV 

 BROUGHT to BANK 

 the sanity of a man be mainly test among his neighbor and kindre by the amount of consideration which he have consistently give to cash . if money have be the chief object of his life , and he for its sake have spar nobody , no soon be he know to be successful than admiration overpower all the ill - will he have cause . he be shrewd , sagacious , long - head , and great ; he have earn his success , and few man grudge , while many seek to get a slice of it ; but he , as a general rule , decline any premature distribution , and for this custody of his wealth he be admire all the more by those who have no hope of share it . 
 as soon as ever it be know that Uncle Sam have lodge at his banker 's a tremendous lump of gold , which rumor declare to be worth at least a hundred thousand dollar , friend from every side pour in , all in hot haste , to lend he their last farthing . the Sawyer be pleased with their kindness , but think that his second - good whiskey meet the merit of the case . and he be more particular than usual with his word ; for , accord to an old saying of the digger , a big nugget always have child , and , be too heavy to go very far , it be likely to keep all its little one at home . many people , therefore , be long to seek for the frog of this great toad ; for so in their slang the miner call they , with a love of preternatural history . but Mr. Gundry allow no search for the frog , or even the tadpole , of his patriarchal nugget . and much as he hat the idea of sow the seed of avarice in any one , he show himself most consistent now in avoid that imputation ; for not only do he refuse to show the bed of his great treasure , after he have secure it , but he fence the whole of it in , and tar the fence , and put loophole in it ; and then he establish Jowler where he could neither be shoot nor poison , and keep a man with a double - barrel rifle in the ruin of the mill , handy to shoot , but not easy to be shoot ; and this be a resolute man , be Martin himself , who have now no business . of course Martin grumble ; but the bad his temper be , the well for his duty , as seem to be the case with a great many man ; and if any one have come to console he in his grumbling , never would he have go away again . 
 it would have be reckless of I to pretend to say what any body ought to do ; from the first to the last I leave every thing to those who know so much well ; at the same time I feel that it might have do no harm if I have be more consult , though I never dream of say so , because the great gold have be find by I , and although I care for it scarcely more than for the tag of a boot - lace , nobody seem to I able to enter into it quite as I do ; and as soon as Firm 's danger and pain grow less , I begin to get rather impatient , but Uncle Sam be not to be hurry . 
 before ever he hoist that rock of gold , he have make up his mind for I to be there , and he even put the business off , because I would not come one night , for I have a superstitious fear on account of its be my father 's birthday . Uncle Sam have forget the date , and beg my pardon for propose it ; but he say that we must not put it off later than the follow night , because the moonlight would be fail , and we durst not have any kind of lamp , and before the next moon the hard weather might begin . all this be before the liberal offer of his friend , of which I have speak first , although they happen to come after it . 
 while the Sawyer have be keep the treasure perdu , to abide the issue of his grandson 's illness , he have take good care both to watch it and to form some opinion of its shape and size ; for , know the pile which I have describe , he could not help find it easily enough ; and indeed the great fear be that other might find it , and come in great force to rob he ; but nothing of that sort have happen , partly because he hold his tongue rigidly , and partly , perhaps , because of the simple precaution which he have take . 
 now , however , it be needful to impart the secret to one man at least ; for firm , though recover , be still so weak that it might have kill he to go into the water , or even to exert himself at all ; and strong as Uncle Sam be , he know that even with hoisting - tackle , he alone could never bring that piece of bullion to bank ; so , after much consideration , he resolve to tell Martin of the mill , as be the most trusty man about the place , as well as the most surly ; but he do not tell he until every thing be ready , and then he take he straightway to the place . 
 here , in the moonlight , we stand wait , Firm and myself and Suan Isco , who have more dread than love of gold , and might be useful to keep watch , or even to lend a hand , for she be as strong as an ordinary man . the night be sultry , and the fire - fly   though dull in the radiance of the moon   dart , like soft little shooting - star , across the still face of shadow , and the flood of the light of the moon be at its height , submerge every thing . 
 while we be whisper and keep in the shade for fear of attract any wanderer 's notice , we see the broad figure of the Sawyer rise from a hollow of the bank , and behind he come Martin the foreman , and we soon see that due preparation have be make , for they take from under some drift - wood   which have prevent we from observe it   a small movable crane , and fix it on a platform of plank which they set up in the river - bed . 
 " paleface eat gold , " Suan Isco say , reflectively , and as if to satisfy herself . " dem eat , drink , die gold ; dem pull gold out of one other 's ear . welly hope Mellican man get enough gold now . " 
 " do not   be sarcastic , now , Suan , " I answer ; " as if it be possible to have enough ! " 
 " for my part , " say Firm , who have be unusually silent all the evening , " I wish it have never be find at all . as sure as I stand here , mischief will come of it . it will break up our household . I hope it will turn out a lump of quartz , gilt on the face , as those big nugget do , ninety - nine out of a hundred . I have have no faith in it all along . " 
 " because I find it , Mr. Firm , I suppose , " I answer , rather pettishly , for I never have like Firm 's incessant bitterness about my nugget . " perhaps if you have find it , Mr. Firm , you would have have great faith in it . " 
 " can not   say , can not   say , " be all Firm 's reply ; and he fall into the silent vein again . 
 " Heave - ho ! heave - ho ! there , you son of cook ! " cry the Sawyer , who be splash for his life in the water . " I have   tackle ' un now . just tighten up the belt , to see if he biteth centre - like . you can not   lift ' un ! Lord bless ' ee , not you . it will take all I know to do that , I guess ; and Firm be not   to lay no hand to it . do not   you be in such a doggoned hurry . hold hard , can not   you ? " 
 for Suan and Martin be haul for their life , and even I catch hold of a rope - end , but have no idea what to do with it , when the Sawyer swing himself up to bank , and in half a minute all be orderly . he show we exactly where to throw our weight , and he use his own to such good effect that , after some creaking and groaning , the long horn of the crane rise steadily , and a mass of dripping sparkle shine in the moonlight over the water . 
 " Hurrah ! what a whale ! how the tough ash bend ! " cry Uncle Sam , pant like a boy , and do nearly all the work himself . " Martin , lie your chest to it . we will grass he in two second . Californy never see a sight like this , I reckon . " 
 there be plenty of room for we all to stand round the monster and admire it . in shape it be just like a fat toad , squat with his shoulder up and pant . even a rough resemblance to the head and the haunch might be discover , and a few spot of quartz shone here and there on the glistening and bossy surface . some of we begin to feel and handle it with vast admiration ; but Firm , with his heavy boot , make a vicious kick at it , and a few bright scale , like spark , fly off . 
 " why , what ail the lad ? " cry the Sawyer , in some wrath ; " what harm hath the stone ever do to he ? to my mind , this here lump be a proof of the whole creation of the world , and who hath live long enough to gainsay ? here this lump hath lain , without change color , since creation 's day ; here it be , as big and heavy as when the Lord lay hand to it . what good to argue agin such fact ? Supposin ' the world come out o ' nothing , with nobody to fetch it , or to say a word of order , how ever could it ' a manage to get a lump of gold like this in it ? they clever feller be too clever . let them put all their head together , and turn out a nugget , and I will believe they . " 
 Uncle Sam 's reasoning be too deep for any but himself to follow . he be not long in perceive this , though we be content to admire his word without ask he to explain they ; so he only say , " well , well , " and begin to try with both hand if he could heft this lump . he stir it , and move it , and raise it a little , as the glisten of the light upon its rounding show ; but lift it fairly from the ground he could not , however he might bow his sturdy leg and bend his mighty back to it ; and , strange to say , he be pleased for once to acknowledge his own discomfiture . 
 " five hundred and a half I use to lift to the height of my knee - cap easily ; I may ' a fall off now a hundred - weight with year , and string in my back , and rheumatic ; but this here little toad be a clear hundredweight out and beyond my heftage . if there be a pound here , there be not an ounce under six hundred - weight , I will lay a thousand dollar . Miss Rema , give a name to he . all the thunder nugget have thunder name . " 
 " then this shall be call ' Uncle Sam , ' " I answer , " because he be the large and the good of all . " 
 " it shall stand , miss , " cry Martin , who be in great spirit , and seem to have better himself forever . " you could not have give it a fine name , miss , if you have consider for a century . Uncle Sam be the name of our glorious race , from the kindness of our natur ' . every body 's uncle we be now , in vartue of superior knowledge , and freedom , and give of general advice , and stickin ' to all the world , or all the good of it . darn if old Sam be not   the front of creation ! " 
 " well , well , " say the Sawyer , " let we call it ' Uncle Sam , ' if the dear young lady like it ; it would be bad luck to change the name ; but , for all that , we must look uncommon sharp , or some of our glorious race will come and steal it afore we unbutton our eye . " 
 " Pooh ! " cry Martin ; but he know very well that his master 's word be common - sense ; and we leave he on guard with a double - barrel gun , and Jowler to keep watch with he . and the next day he tell we that he have spend the night in such a frame of mind from continual thought that when our pet cow come to drink at daybreak , it be but the blowing of her breath that save she from take a bullet between her soft tame eye . 
 now it could not in any kind of way hold good that such thing should continue ; and the Sawyer , though loath to lose sight of the nugget , perceive that he must not sacrifice all the moral of the neighborhood to it , and he barely have time to dispatch it on its road at the bottom of a load of lumber , with Martin to drive , and Jowler to sit up , and firm to ride behind , when a troop of mixed robber come rid across , with a four - wheel cart and two sturdy mule enough to drag off every thing . they have clearly hear of the golden toad , and desire to know more of he ; but Uncle Sam , with his usual blandness , meet these man at the gate of his yard , and upon the top rail , to ease his arm , he rest a rifle of heavy metal , with seven revolve chamber . the robber find out that they have lose their way , and Mr. Gundry answer that so they have , and the soon they find it in another direction , the well it would be for they . they think that he have all his man inside , and they be mighty civil , though we have only two negro to help we , and Suan Isco , with a great gun cock . but their curiosity be such that they could not help ask about the gold ; and , soon than shoot they , Uncle Sam reply that , upon his honor , the nugget be go . and the fame of his word be so well know that these fellow   none of whom could tell the truth , even at confession   believe he on the spot , and beg his pardon for trespassing on his premise . they hop that he would not say a word to the Vigilance Committee , who hang a poor fellow for lose his road ; and he tell they that if they make off at once , nobody should pursue they ; and so they ride off very happily . 




 CHAPTER XVI 

 firm and INFIRM 

 strange as it may appear , our quiet little home be not yet disturb by that great discovery of gold . the Sawyer go up to the summit of esteem in public opinion ; but to himself and to we he be the same as ever . he work with his own hard hand and busy head just as he use to do ; for although the mill be still in ruin , there be plenty of the fine work to do , which always require hand - labor . and at night he would sit at the end of the table furth from the fire - place , with his spectacle on , and his red cheek glow , while he design the future mill , which be to be build in the spring , and transcend every mill ever hear , think , or dream of . 
 we all look forward to a quiet winter , snug with warmth and cheer in - door , and bright outside with sparkle tree , brisk air , and frosty appetite , when a foolish idea arise which spoil the comfort at least of two of we . Ephraim Gundry find out , or fancy , that he be entirely fill with love of a very young maid , who never dream of such thing , and hat even to hear of they ; and the maid , unluckily , be myself . 
 during the time of his ailment I have be with he continually , be only too glad to assuage his pain , or turn his thought away from it . I partly suspect that he have incur his bitter wound for my sake ; though I never impute his zeal to more than a young man 's natural wrath at an outrage . but now he leave I no long in doubt , and make I most uncomfortable . perhaps I be hard upon he , and afterward I often think so , for he be very kind and gentle ; but I be an orphan child , and have no one to advise I in such matter . I believe that he should have consider this , and allow I to grow a little old ; but perhaps he himself be too young as yet and too bashful to know how to manage thing . it be the very evening after his return from Sacramento , and the beauty of the weather still abode in the soft warm depth around we . in every tint of rock and tree and playful glass of river a quiet clearness seem to lie , and a rich content of color . the grandeur of the world be such that one could only rest among it , seek neither voice nor think . 
 therefore I be more surprised than pleased to hear my name ring loudly through the echo hollow , and then to see the bush shake , and an eager form leap out . I do not answer a word , but sit with a wreath of white bouvardia and small adiantum round my head , which I have plait anyhow . 
 " what a lovely dear you be ! " cry firm , and then he seem frightened at his own word . 
 " I have no idea that you would have finish your dinner so soon as this , Mr. Firm . " 
 " and you do not want I . you be vex to see I . tell the truth , Miss Rema . " 
 " I always tell the truth , " I answer ; " and I do not want to be disturb just now . I have so many thing to think of . " 
 " and not I among they . oh no , of course you never think of I , Erema . " 
 " it be very unkind of you to say that , " I answer , look clearly at he , as a child look at a man . " and it be not true , I assure you , firm . whenever I have think of dear Uncle Sam , I very often go on to think of you , because he be so fond of you . " 
 " but not for my own sake , Erema ; you never think of I for my own sake . " 
 " but yes , I do , I assure you , Mr. Firm ; I do greatly . there be scarcely a day that I do not remember how hungry you be , and I think of you . " 
 " tush ! " reply Firm , with a lofty gaze . " even for a moment that do not in any way express my meaning . my mind be very much above all eat when it dwell upon you , Erema . I have always be fond of you , Erema . " 
 " you have always be good to I , firm , " I say , as I manage to get a great branch between we . " after your grandfather , and Suan Isco , and Jowler , I think that I like you good of almost any body leave to I . and you know that I never forget your slipper . " 
 " Erema , you drive I almost wild by never understand I . now will you just listen to a little common - sense ? you know that I be not romantic . " 
 " yes , Firm ; yes , I know that you never do any thing wrong in any way . " 
 " you would like I well if I do . what an extraordinary thing it be ! oh , Erema , I beg your pardon . " 
 he have see in a moment , as man seem to do , when they study the much quick face of a girl , that his word have keenly wound I that I have apply they to my father , of whom I be always think , though I scarcely ever speak of he . but I know that Firm have mean no harm , and I give he my hand , though I could not speak . 
 " my darling , " he say , " you be very dear to I dearer than all the world besides . I will not worry you any more . only say that you do not hate I . " 
 " how could I ? how could any body ? now let we go in and attend to Uncle Sam . he think of every body before himself . " 
 " and I think of every body after myself . be that what you mean , Erema ? " 
 " to be sure ! if you like . you may put any meaning on my word that you think proper . I be accustom to thing of that sort , and I pay no attention whatever , when I be perfectly certain that I be right . " 
 " I see , " reply Firm , apply one finger to the side of his nose in deep contemplation , which , of all his manner , annoy I most . " I see how it be ; Miss Rema be always perfectly certain that she be right , and the whole of the rest of the world quite wrong . well , after all , there be nothing like hold a first - rate opinion of one 's self . " 
 " you be not what I think of you , " I cry , be vex beyond bearance by such word , and feel their gross injustice . " if you wish to say any thing more , please to leave it until you recover your temper . I be not quite accustomed to rudeness . " 
 with these word , I draw away and walk off , partly in earnest and partly in joke , not wish to hear another word ; and when I look back , be well out of sight , there he sit still , with his head on his hand , and my heart have a little ache for he . 
 however , I determine to say no more , and to be extremely careful . I could not in justice blame Ephraim Gundry for look at I very often . but I take good care not to look at he again unless he say something that make I laugh , and then I could scarcely help it . he be sharp enough very soon to find out this ; and then he do a thing which be most unfair , as I find out long afterward . he buy an american jest - book , full of idea wholly new to I , and these he commit to heart , and bring they out as his own production . if I have only know it , I must have be exceedingly sorry for he . but Uncle Sam use to laugh and rub his hand , perhaps for old acquaintance ' sake ; and when Uncle Sam laugh , there be nobody near who could help laugh with he . and so I begin to think firm the most witty and pleasant of man , though I try to look away . 
 but perhaps the most careful and delicate of thing be to see how Uncle Sam go on . I could not understand he at all just then , and think he quite change from my old Uncle Sam ; but afterward , when I come to know , his behavior be as clear and shallow as the water of his own river . he have very strange idea about what he generally call " the female kind . " accord to his idea   and perhaps they be not so unusual among mankind , especially settler , all " female " be of a good but weak and consistently inconsistent sort . the sure way to make they do whatever their better want , be to make they think that it be not want , but be hedge with obstacle beyond their power to overcome , and so to provoke and tantalize they to set their heart upon do it . in accordance with this idea   than which there can be none more mistaken , he take the great pain to keep I from have a word to say to Firm ; and even go so far as to hint , with wink and nod of pleasantry , that his grandson 's heart be set upon the pretty Miss Sylvester , the daughter of a man who own a herd of pig , much too near our saw - mill , and herself a young woman of outrageous dress , and in a large light contemptible . but when Mr. Gundry , without any word , convey this piece of news to I , I immediately feel quite a liking for gaudy but harmless Pennsylvania for so her parent have name she when she be too young to help it ; and I heartily hop that she might suit Firm , which she seem all the more likely to do as his conduct could not be call noble . upon that point , however , I say not a word , leave he purely to judge for himself , and feel it a great relief that now he could not say any thing more to I . I be glad that his taste be so easily pleased , and I tell Suan Isco how glad I be . 
 this I have well have leave unsaid , for it lead to a great explosion , and drive I away from the place altogether before the new mill be finish , and before I should otherwise have go from friend who be so good to I ; not that I could have staid there much long , even if this have never come to pass ; for week by week and month by month I be grow more uneasy : uneasy not at my obligation or dependence upon mere friend   for they manage that so kindly that I seem to confer the favor , but from my own sense of lag far behind my duty . 
 for now the bright air , and the wholesome food , and the pleasure of goodness around I , be make I grow , without knowledge or notice , into a tall and not altogether to be overlook young woman . I be exceedingly shy about this , and blush if any one speak of it ; but yet in my heart I feel it be so ; and how could I help it ? and when people say , as rough people will , and even Uncle Sam sometimes , " Handsome be as handsome do , " or " Beauty be only skin - deep , " and so on , I make it my duty not to be put out , but to bear it in mind and be thankful . and though I have no idea of any such influence at the moment , I hope that the grandeur of nature around and the lofty style of every thing may have save I from dwell too much on myself , as Pennsylvania Sylvester do . 
 now the more I feel my grow - up age and health and buoyant vigor , the surer I know that the time be come for I to do some good with they ; not to benefit the world in general , in a large and scattery way   as many young people set out to do , and never get any far , but to right the wrong of my own house , and bring home justice to my own heart . this may be think a partial and paltry object to set out with ; and it be not for I to say otherwise . at the time , it occur to I in no other light except as my due business , and I never take any large view at all . but even now I do believe   though not yet in pickle of wisdom   that if every body , in its own little space and among its own little movement , will only do and take nothing without pure taste of the salt of justice , no reeking atrocity of national crime could ever taint the heaven . 
 such question , however , become I not . I have only to deal with very little thing , sometimes too slim to handle well , and too hazy to be weave ; and if they seem below my sense and dignity to treat of , I can only say that they seem very big at the time when I have to encounter they . 
 for instance , what could be more important , in a little world of life , than for Uncle Sam to be put out , and dare even to think ill of I ? yet this he do ; and it show how shallow be all those theory of the other sex which man be so pleased to indulge in . scarcely any thing could be more ridiculous from first to last , when calmly and truly consider , than the firm belief which no power of reason could for the time root out of he . 
 Uncle Sam , the dear of all mankind to I , and the very kind , be positively low - enough to believe , in his sad opinion of the female race , that my young head be turn because of the wealth to which I have no claim , except through his own justice . he have insist at first that the whole of that great nugget belong to I by right of sole discovery . I ask he whether , if any stranger have find it , it would have be consider his , and whether he would have allow a " greaser , " upon find , to make off with it . at the thought of this , Mr. Gundry give a little grunt , and could not go so far as to maintain that view of it . but he say that my reasoning do not fit ; that I be not a greaser , but a settle inhabitant of the place , and entitle to all a settler 's right ; that the bed of the river would have be his grave but for the risk of my life , and therefore whatever I find in the bed of the river belong to I , and I only . 
 in argument he be so much strong than I could ever attempt to be that I give it up , and could only say that if he argue forever it could never make any difference . he do not argue forever , but only grow obstinate and unpleasant , so that I yield at last to own the half share of the bullion . 
 very well . every body would have think , who have not study the nature of man or be drag through it heavily , that now there could be no more trouble between two people entirely trust each other , and only anxious that the other should have the good of it . yet , instead of that be the case , the mischief , the myriad mischief , of money set in , until I heartily wish sometimes that my miserable self be down in the hole which the pelf have leave behind it . 
 for what do Uncle Sam take into his head   which be full of generosity and large idea , so loosely pack that little one grow between they , especially about womankind   what else do he really seem to think , with the downright stubbornness of all his thought , but that I , his poor debtor and pensioner and penniless dependent , be so set up and elate by this sudden access of fortune that henceforth none of the saw race be high enough for I to think of ? it take I a long time to believe that so fair and just a man ever could set such interpretation upon I . and when it become too plain that he do so , truly I know not whether grief or anger be uppermost in my troubled heart . 




 CHAPTER XVII 

 hard and soft 

 before very long it be manifest enough that Mr. Gundry look down upon Miss Sylvester with a large contempt . but while this raise my opinion of his judgment , it almost deprive I of a great relief the relief of suppose that he wish his grandson to marry this Pennsylvania . for although her father , with his pig and cattle , and a low sort of hostelry which he keep , could settle " a good pile of dollar " upon she , and have keep she at the " learnedest lady ' college " even in San Francisco till he himself tremble at her erudition , still it be scarcely to be believe that a man of the Sawyer 's strong common - sense and disregard of finery would ever accept for his grandchild a girl make of affectation , vulgarity , and conceit . and one day , quite in the early spring , he be so much vex with the fine lady 's air that he leave no doubt about his meaning . 
 Miss Sylvester be very proud of the figure she make on horseback ; and have be bring up , perhaps as a child , to ride after pig and so on , she must have have fine opportunity of acquire a graceful style of horsemanship . and now she dash through thick and thin in a most commanding manner , care no more for a snow - drift than lady do for a scraping of the road . no one with the least observation could doubt that this young woman be extremely anxious to attract Firm Gundry 's notice ; and therefore , on the day above speak of , once more she ride over , with her poor father in wait upon she as usual .

 CHAPTER xviii 

 OUT of the golden GATE 

 little thing , or what we call little , always will come in among great one , or at least among those which we call great . before I pass the Golden Gate in the clipper ship Bridal Veil   so call from one of the Yosemite cascade   I find out what I have long wish to know why Firm have a crooked nose . at least , it could hardly be call crooked if any body look aright at it ; but still it depart from the bold straight line which nature must have mean for it , every thing else about he be as straight as could be require . this subject have trouble I more than once , though of course it have nothing whatever to do with the point of view whence I regard he . 
 Suan Isco could not tell I , neither could Martin of the mill ; I certainly could not ask Firm himself , as the Sawyer tell I to do when once I put the question , in despair , to he . but now , as we stand on the wharf exchange farewell , perhaps forever , and tear of anguish be in my eye , and my heart be both full and empty , ample and unexpected light be throw on the curvature of Firm 's nose . 
 for a beautiful girl , of about my own age , and very nicely dress , come up and speak to the Sawyer   who stand at my side , and then , with a blush , take his grandson 's hand . Firm take off his hat to she very politely , but allow she to see perhaps by his manner that he be particularly engage just now ; and the young lady , with a quick glance at I , walk off to rejoin her party . but a garrulous old negro servant , who seem to be in attendance upon she , run up and catch firm by his coat , and peer up curiously at his face . 
 " how young massa 's poor nose dis long time ? how he feel , spose now again ? " he inquire , with a deferential grin . " young massa ebber able take a pinch of good snuff ? he ! he ! missy berry heavy den ? Missy no learn to dance de nose polka den ? " 
 " what on earth do he mean ? " I could not help ask , in spite of our sorrowful farewell , as the negro go on with sundry other joke and cackle at his own facetiousness . and then Uncle Sam , to divert my thought , while I wait for signal to say good - by , tell I how Firm get a slight twist to his nose . 
 Ephraim Gundry have be well teach , in all the common thing a man should learn , at a good quiet school at Frisco , which distinguish itself from all other school by not call itself a college . and when he be leave to begin home life , with as much put into he as he could manage for his nature be not bookish when he be just seventeen year old , and tall and straight and upright , but not set into great bodily strength , which could not yet be expect , a terrible fire break out in a great block of house newly occupy , over against the school - house front . without wait for master 's leave or matron 's , the boy , in the californian style , jump over the fencing and go to help . and they find a great crowd collect , and flame flare out of the top of the house . at the top of the house , accord to a stupid and therefore general practice , be the nursery , make of more nurse than child , as often happen with rich people . the nurse have run away for their life , take two of the child with they ; but the third , a fine little girl of ten , have be leave behind , and now run to the window with red hot flame behind she . the window be open , and barb of fire , like serpent ' tongue , play over it . 
 " jump , child , jump ! for God 's sake , jump ! " cry half a hundred people , while the poor scared creature quiver on the ledge , and shrink from the frightful depth below . at last , sting by a scorch volley , she gather her night - gown tight , and leap , trust to the many face and many arm raise toward she . but though many gallant man be there , only one stand fast just where she fall , and that one be the youth , Firm Gundry . upon he she fall , like a stone from heaven , and though he hold up his arm in the smoky glare , she come down badly : badly , at least , for he , but , as her father say , providentially ; for one of her sol , or heel , alight on the bridge of Ephraim 's young nose . he catch she on his chest , and forgetful of himself , he bear she to her friend triumphantly , unharmed , and almost smile . but the symmetry of an important part of his face be spoil forever . 
 when I hear of this noble affair , and thought of my own pusillanimous rendering for verily I have be low enough , from rumor of Firm 's pugnacity , to attribute these little defect of line to some fisticuff with some miner I look at Firm 's nose through the tear in my eye , and have a great mind not to go away at all . for what be the noble of all thing in man as I bitterly learn thereafter , and already have some guess ? not the power of move multitude with eloquence or by order ; not the elevation of one tribe through the lowering of other , nor even the imaginary lift of all by sentiment as yet above they : there may be glory in all of these , but the greatness be not with they . it remain with those who behave like Firm , and get their nose break . 
 however , I do not know those thing at that time of life , though I think it right for every man to be brave and good ; and I could not help ask who the young lady be , as if that be part of the heroism . the Sawyer , who never be unready for a joke , of however ancient quality , give a great wink at Firm   which I fail to understand , and ask he how much the young lady be worth . he expect that Firm would say , " five hundred thousand dollar " which be about her value , I believe and Uncle Sam want I to hear it ; not that he care a single cent himself , but to let I know what firm could do . 
 Firm , however , be not to be lead into any trap of that sort . he know I well than the old man do , and that nothing would stir I to jealousy , and he quite disappoint the Sawyer . 
 " I have never ask what she be worth , " he say , with a glance of contempt at money ; " but she scarcely seem worth look at , compare compare with certain other . "
