 but the last of all to say " good - by " be my beloved Jowler . he jump into the boat after I   for we be oblige to have a boat , the ship have laden far down , and he put his fore - paw on my shoulder , and whine and droop his under - jaw . and when he look at I as he use , to know whether I be in fun or earnest , with more expression in his bright brown eye than any human being have , I fall back under his weight and sob , and could not look at any one . 
 we have beautiful weather , and the view be glorious , as we pass the Golden Gate , the entrance to what will one day be the capital of the world , perhaps . for , as our captain say , all power and human energy and strength be always go westward , and when they come here they must stop , or else they would be go eastward again , which they never yet have do . his argument may have be right or wrong and , indeed , it must have be one or the other but who could think of such thing now , with a grander thing than human power human love fade away behind ? I could not even bear to see the glorious mountain sink , but run below and cry for hour , until all be dark and calm . 
 the reason for my sailing by this particular ship , and , indeed , rather suddenly , be that an old friend and cornish cousin of Mr. Gundry , who have spend some year in California , be now return to England by the Bridal Veil . this be Major Hockin , an officer of the british army , now on half - pay , and get on in year . his wife be go home with he ; for their child be marry and settle in England , all but one , now in San Francisco . and that one be well place in the firm of Heniker , bank , and Co. , have obtain for his father and mother passage upon favorable term , which be , as we say , " an object to they . " 
 for the Major , though admirably connect   as his kinship to Colonel Gundry show , and have a baronet not far off   if the twist of the world be set aside , also have serve his country , and receive a furrow on the top of his head , which make he brush his hair up , nevertheless , or all the more for that , be as poor as a british officer must be without official sesame . how he manage to feed and teach a large and not clever family , and train they all to fight their way in a battle bad than any of his own , and make gentleman and lady of they , whatever they do or wherever they go , he only know , and his faithful wife , and the Lord who help brave poverty . of such thing he never speak , unless his temper be arouse by luxury and self - indulgence and laziness . 
 but now he be a little well off , through have his child off his hand , and by mean of a little property leave he by a distant relative . he be on his way home to see to this ; and a well man never return to England , after always stand up for she . 
 be a child in the way of the world , and accustom to large people , I could not make out Major Hockin at first , and think he no more than a little man with many peculiarity . for he be not so tall as myself , until he put his high - heeled boot on , and he make such a stir about trifle at which Uncle Sam would have only grunt , that I take he to be nothing more than a fidgety old campaigner . he wear a black - rim double eyeglass with blue side - light at his temple , and his hat , from the shape of his forehead , hang back ; he have narrow white wiry whisker , and a roman nose , and most prominent chin , and keen gray eye with gingery brow , which contract , like sharp little gable over they , whenever any thing displease he . rosy cheek , tight - draw , close - shaven , and gleam with friction of yellow soap , add vigor to the general expression of his face , which be firm and quick and straightforward . the weather be warm , and the tropic close at hand , Major Hockin be dress in a fine suit of Nankin , spruce and trim , and beautifully make , set off his spare and active figure , which , though he be sixty - two year of age , seem always to be ready for a game of leap - frog . 
 we be three day out of the Golden Gate , and the hill of the coast ridge be faint and small , and the spire of the low Nevada could only be catch when the hot haze lift ; and every body lie about in our ship where it seem to afford the least smell and heat , and nobody for a moment dream for we really all be dream of any body with energy enough to be disturb about any thing , when Major Hockin burst in upon we all   who be try not to be red - hot in the feeble shade of poop awning , lead by the hand an ancient woman , scarcely dress with decency , and howl in a tone very sad to hear . 
 " this lady have be rob ! " cry the Major ; " rob , not fifteen foot below we . robbed , lady and gentleman , of the most cherished treasure of her life , the portrait of her only son , the saving of a life of honest toil , her poor dead husband 's tobacco - box , and a fine cut of Colorado cheese . " 
 " ten pound and a quarter , gospel true ! " cry the poor woman , wring her hand , and search for any kind face among we . 
 " go to the captain , " mutter one sleepy gentleman . " go to the devil , " say another sleepy man : " what have we to do with it ? " 
 " I will neither go to the captain , " reply the Major , very distinctly , " nor yet to the devil , as a fellow who be not a man have dare to suggest to I " 
 " all tie in my own pocket - handkerchief ! " the poor old woman begin to scream ; " the one with the three - cornered spot upon ' un . only two have I ever own in all my life , and this be the very good of them . oh dear ! oh dear ! that ever I should come to this exposing of my thing ! " 
 " Madam , you shall have justice do , as sure as my name be Hockin . gentleman and lady , if you be not all asleep , how would you like to be treat so ? because the weather be a trifle warm , there you lie like a parcel of Mexicans . if any body pick your pocket , would you have life enough to roll over ? " 
 " I do not   think I should , " say a fat young Briton , with a very good - natured face ; " but for a poor woman I can stand upright . major Hockin , here be a guinea for she . perhaps more of we will give a trifle . " 
 " well do ! " cry the Major ; " but not so much as that . let we first ascertain all the right of the case . perhaps half a crown apiece would reach it . " 
 half a crown apiece would have go beyond it , as we discover afterward , for the old lady 's handkerchief be in her box , lose under some more of her property ; and the tide of sleepy charity take this direction under such vehement impulse , several other steerage passenger lose their good , but find themselves too late in do so . but the Major be satisfied , and the rude man who have tell he to go amiss , beg his pardon , and thus we sail on slowly and peaceably . 




 CHAPTER XIX 

 inside the CHANNEL 

 that little incident throw some light upon Major Hockin 's character . it be not for himself alone that he be so particular , or , as many would call it , fidgety , to have every thing do properly ; for if any thing come to his knowledge which he think unfair to any one , it concern he almost as much as if the wrong have be do to his own home self . through this he have fall into many trouble , for his impression be not always accurate ; but they teach he nothing , or rather , as his wife say , " the Major could not help it . " the lead journal of the various place in which Major Hockin sojourn have publish his letter of grievance sometimes , in the absence of the chief editor , and have suffer in purse by do so . but the Major always say , " ventilate it , ventilate the subject , my dear Sir ; bring public opinion to bear on it . " and Mrs. Hockin always say that it be her husband to whom belong the whole credit of this new and spirited use of the fine word " ventilation . " 
 as betwixt this faithful pair , it be scarcely needful perhaps to say that the Major be the master . his sense of justice dictate that , as well as his general briskness . though he be not at all like Mr. Gundry in undervaluing female mind , his large experience and more frequent intercourse with our sex have teach he to do justice to we ; and it be pleasant to hear he often defer to the judgment of lady . but this he do more , perhaps , in theory than in practice ; yet it make all the lady declare to one another that he be a perfect gentleman . and so he be , though he have his fault ; but his fault be such as we approve of . 
 but Mrs. Hockin have no fault in any way worth speak of . and whatever she have be her husband 's doing , through her desire to keep up with he . she be pretty , even now in her sixtieth year , and a great deal pretty because she never try to look young . silver hair , and gentle eye , and a forehead in which all the care of eight child have scarcely imprint a wrinkle , also a kind expression of interest in whatever be speak of , with a quiet voice and smile , and a power of not say too much at a time , combine to make this lady pleasant . 
 without any fuss or declaration , she take I immediately under her care ; and I doubt not that , after two year pass in the society of Suan Isco and the gentle Sawyer , she find many thing in I to amend , which she do by example and without reproof . she shield I also in the clever way from the curiosity of the saloon , which at first be very try . for the Bridal Veil be a well - know ship both for swift passage and for equipment , almost every berth be take , and when the weather be calm , quite a large assembly sit down to dinner . among these , of course , be some ill - breed people , and my youth and reserve and self - consciousness , and so on , make my reluctant face the mark for many a long and search gaze . my own wish have be not to dine thus in public ; but hear that my absence would only afford fresh ground for curiosity , I take my seat between the Major and his wife , the former have pledge himself to the latter to leave every thing to her management . his temper be try more than once to its utmost which be not a very great distance but he keep his word , and do not interfere ; and I have have some experience with firm , eschew all perception of glance . and as for all word , Mrs. Hockin meet they with an obtuse obliqueness ; so that after a day or two it be settle that nothing could be do about " Miss Wood . " 
 it have be a very sore point to come to , and cost an unparalleled shed of pride , that I should be shorn of two - third of my name , and call " Miss Wood , " like almost anybody else . I refuse to entertain such a very poor idea , and clung to the name which have always be mine for my father would never depart from it and I even burst into tear , which would , I suppose , be call ' sentimental ; " but still the stern fact star I in the face I must go as " Miss Wood , " or not go at all . upon this Major Hockin have insist ; and even Colonel Gundry could not move he from his resolution . 
 Uncle Sam have do his utmost , as be say before , to stop I from wish to go at all ; but when he find my whole heart bend upon it , and even my soul imperil by the sense of neglect life 's chief duty , his own stern sense of right come in and side with my prayer to he . and so it be that he let I go , with pity for my youth and sex , but a knowledge that I be in good hand , and an inborn , perhaps " Puritanical " faith , that the Lord of all right would see to I . 
 the Major , on the other hand , have none of this . he differ from Uncle Sam as much as a trim - cut and highly cultured garden tree differ from a great spread king of the wood . he be not without a strict sense of religion , especially when he have to march man to church ; and he never even use a bad word , except when wicked fact compel he . when properly let alone , and allow to nurse his own opinion , he have a respectable idea that all thing be certain to be order for the good ; but nothing enrage he so much as to tell he that when thing go against he , or even against his prediction . 
 it be lucky for I , then , that Major Hockin have take a most adverse view of my case . he form his opinion with the great haste , and with the great perseverance stick to they ; for he be the most generous of mankind , if generous mean one quite full of his genus . and in my little case he have make up his mind that the whole of the fact be against I . " fact " be his favorite word , and one which he always use with great effect , for nobody know very well what it mean , as it do not belong to our language . and so when he say that the fact be against I , who be there to answer that fact be not truth ? 
 this fast - set conclusion of his be know to I not through himself , but through his wife . for I could not yet bring myself to speak of the thing that lie close at my heart to he , though I know that he must be aware of they . and he , like a gentleman , leave I to begin . I could often see that he be ready and quite eager to give I the benefit of his opinion , which would only have turn I against he , and irritate he , perhaps , with I . and have no home in England , or , indeed , I might say , any where , I be to live with the Major and his wife , suppose that they could arrange it so , until I should discover relative . 
 we have a long and stormy voyage , although we set sail so fairly ; and I think that we never should round Cape Horn in the tooth of the furious northeast wind ; and after that we lay becalm , I have no idea in what latitude , though the passenger now talk quite like seaman , at least till the sea get up again . however , at last we make the English Channel , in the dreary day of November , and after more peril there than any where else , we be safely dock at Southampton . here the Major be meet by two dutiful daughter , bring their husband and child , and I see more of family life   at a distance   than have fall to my lot to observe before ; and although there be many little jar and brawl and cut at one another , I be sadly inclined to wish sometimes for some brother and sister to quarrel with . 
 but have none to quarrel with , and none to love , except good Mrs. Hockin , who go away by train immediately , I spend such a wretched time in that town that I long to be back in the Bridal Veil in the very bad of weather . the ooze of the shore and the reek of the water , and the dreary flatness of the land around   after the glorious heaven - clothe height , which make I ashamed of littleness , also the rough , stupid stare of the man , when I go about as an american lady may freely do in America , and the sharpness of every body 's voice   instead of the genial tone which those who can not produce they call " nasal , " but which from a high view be cordial   take one after other , or all together , these thing make I think , in the first flush of thought , that England be not a nice country . after a little while I find that I have be a great deal too quick , as foreigner be with thing which require quiet comprehension . for instance , I be annoy at have a stupid woman put over I , as if I could not mind myself a cook , or a nurse , or housekeeper , or something very useful in the Hockin family , but to I a mere incumbrance , and   as I think in my wrath sometimes   a spy . what be I likely to do , or what be any one likely to do to I , in a thoroughly civilized country , that I could not even stay in private lodging , where I have a great deal to think of , without this dull creature be force upon I ? but the Major so order it , and I give in . 
 there I must have staid for the slow three mouth ever pass without slow starvation finish my growth , but not know how to " form my mind , " as I be tell to do . Major Hockin come down once or twice to see I , and though I do not like he , yet it be almost enough to make I do so to see a little liveliness . but I could not and would not put up with a frightful german baron of music , with a polished card like a toast - rack , whom the Major try to impress on I . as if I could stop to take music lesson ! 
 " Miss Wood , " say Major Hockin , in his strong manner , the last time he come to see I , " I stand to you in loco parentis . that mean , with the duty , relationship , responsibility , and what not , of the unfortunate I should say rather of the beloved parent decease . I wish to be more careful of you than of a daughter of my own a great deal more careful , ten time , Miss Wood ; I may say a thousand time more careful , because you have not have the discipline which a daughter of mine would have enjoy . and you be so impulsive when you take an idea ! you judge every body by your liking . that lead to error , error , error . " 
 " my name be not Miss Wood , " I answer ; " my name be ' Erema Castlewood . ' whatever need may have be on board ship for nobody know who I be , surely I may have my own name now . " 
 when any body say ' surely , " at once up spring a question ; nothing be sure , and the word itself at heart quite interrogative . the Major know all those little thing which manage woman so manfully . so he take I by the hand and lead I to the light and look at I . 
 I have not one atom of russian twist or dye China grass in my hair , nor even the ubiquitous aid of horse and cow ; neither in my face or figure be I conscious of false presentment . the Major be welcome to lead I to the light and to throw up all his spectacle and gaze with all his eye . my only vexation be with myself , because I could not keep the weakness which a stranger should not see out of my eye , upon sudden remembrance who it be that use to have the right to do such thing to I . this it be , and nothing else , that make I drop my eye , perhaps . 
 " there , there , my dear ! " say Major Hockin , in a soft voice than usual . " pretty fit you be to combat with the world , and defy the world , and brave the world , and abolish the world or at least the world 's opinion ! ' bo to a goose , ' you can say , my dear ; but no ' bo ' to a gander . no , no ; do quietly what I advise by - the - bye , you have never ask my advice . " 
 I can not have be hypocritical , for of all thing I detest that most ; but in good faith I say , be conquer by the Major 's relaxation of his eye , 
 " oh , why have you never offer it to I ? you know that I never could ask for it . " 
 for the moment he look surprised , as if our idea have go crosswise ; and then he remember many little symptom of my faith in his opinion ; which be now grow inevitable , with his wife and daughter , and many grandchild all certain that he be a Solomon . 
 " Erema , " he say , " you be a dear good girl , though sadly , sadly romantic . I have no idea that you have so much sense . I will talk with you , Erema , when we both have leisure . " 
 " I be quite at leisure , Major Hockin , " I reply , " and only too happy to listen to you . " 
 " yes , yes , I dare say . you be in lodging . you can do exactly as you please . but I have a basin of ox - tail soup , a cutlet , and a woodcock wait for I at the Cosmopolitan Hotel . bless I ! I be five minute late already . I will come and have a talk with you afterward . " 
 " thank you , " I say ; " we have well leave it . it seem of no importance , compare compare with " 
 " my dinner ! " say the Major ; but he be offend , and so be I a little , though neither of we mean to vex the other . 




 CHAPTER XX 

 BRUNTSEA 

 it would be unfair to Major Hockin to take he for an extravagant man or a self - indulgent one because of the good dinner he have order , and his eagerness to sit down to it . through all the good year of his life he have be most frugal , abstemious , and self - deny , grudge every penny of his own expense , but spar none for his family . and now , when he find himself so much well off , with more income and less outlay , he could not be blame for enjoy good thing with the wholesome zest of abstinence . 
 for , come to the point , and go well into the matter , the Major have discover that the " little property " leave to he , and which he be come to see to , really be quite a fine estate for any one who know how to manage it , and would not spare courage and diligence . and of these two quality he have such abundance that , without any outlet , they might have turn he sour . 
 the property lately devise to he by his cousin , Sir Rufus Hockin , have long be far more plague than profit to that idle baronet . Sir Rufus hat all exertion , yet could not comfortably put up with the only alternative extortion . have no knowledge of his cousin Nick   except that he be indefatigable , and know his own son to be lazy even than himself have be , long also to inflict even posthumous justice upon the land agent , with the glad consent of his heir he leave this distant , fretful , and naked spur of land to his beloved cousin Major Nicholas Hockin . 
 the Major first hear of this unexpected increase of his belonging while he be hover , in the land of gold , between his desire to speculate and his dread of speculation . at once he consult our Colonel Gundry , who meet he by appointment at Sacramento ; and Uncle Sam have a vast idea of the value of land in England , which the Major naturally make the most of , now be an english land - owner , they spend a most pleasant evening , and agree upon the line mark out by Providence . 
 thus it be that he come home , bring   by kind arrangement   I , who be much more trouble than comfort to he , and at first dispose to be cold and curt . and thus it be that I be leave so long in that wretched Southampton , under the care of a very kind person who never could understand I . and all this while   as I ought to have know , without any one to tell I   Major Hockin be test the value and beat the bound of his new estate , and prolong his dinner from one to two course , or three if he have be travel . his property be large enough to afford he many dinner , and rich enough   when rightly treat   to insure their quality . 
 Bruntsea be a quiet little village on the southeast coast of England , in Kent or in Sussex , I be not sure which , for it have a constitution of its own , and say that it belong to neither . it use to be a place of size and valor , furnish ship , and find money for patriotic purpose . and great people both embark and land , one do this and the other that , though nobody seem to have ever do both , if history be to be rely upon . the glory of the place be still preserve in a seal and an immemorial stick , each of which be bless with mark as incomprehensible as could be wish , though both be to be see for sixpence . the name of the place be write in more than forty different way , they say ; and the old inhabitant be less positive than the young how to spell it . 
 this village lie in the mouth , or rather at the eastern end of the mouth , of a long and wide depression among the hill , through which a sluggish river win its muddy consummation . this river once go far along the sea - brink , without enter   like a child who be afraid to bathe , as the Adur do at Shoreham , and as many other river do . and in those day the mouth and harbor be under the cliff at Bruntsea , whence its seal and corporation , stick , and other blessing . but three or four century ago the river be draw by a violent storm , like a badger from his barrel , and force to come straight out and face the sea , without any three mile of dalliance . the time - serve water make the good of this , forsook its ancient bed   as classic nymph and fountain use to do , and leave poor Bruntsea with a dry bank , and no haven for a cockle - shell . a new port , such as it be , incrust the fickle jaw of the river ; pile be drive and earth - work form , lest the water should return to its old love ; and Bruntsea , as concern her traffic , become but a mark of memory . her noble corporation never demand their old channel , but regard the whole as the will of the Lord , and have the good sense to insist upon nothing except their time - honor ceremony . 
 in spite of all these and their importance , land become of no value there . the owner of the Eastern Manor and of many ancient right , have no mean of get at they , sell they for an " old song , " which they be ; and the buyer be one of the Hockin race , a shipwreck mariner from Cornwall , who have be kindly treat there , and take a fancy accordingly . he sell his share in some mine to pay for it , settle here , and die here ; and his son , get on in the world , build a house , and take to serious smuggling . in the chalk cliff 's eastward he find hole of honest value to he , capable of cheap enlargement   which the cornish hole be not , and much more accessible from France . become a magistrate and deputy - lieutenant , he have the duty and privilege of inquire into his own deed , which enable he to check those few who otherwise might have compete with he . he flourish , and buy more secure estate ; and his son , for activity against smuggler , be make a gentle baronet . 
 these thing now have pass away , and the first fee - simple of the Hockin family become a mere load and incumbrance . Sir George and Sir Robert and Sir Rufus , one after another , do not like the hint about contraband dealing which meet they whenever they deign to come down there , till at last the estate   be leave to an agent   cost a great deal more than he ever pay in . and thus as should have be more briefly tell the owner be our Major Hockin . 
 no wonder that this gentleman , with so many care to attend to , have no time at first to send for I . and no wonder that when he come down to see I , he be oblige to have good dinner . for the work do by he in those three month surprise every body except himself , and make in old Bruntsea a stir unknown since the time of the spanish Armada . for he own the house under the eastern cliff , and the warren , and the dairy - farm inland , and the slope of the ground where the sea use to come , and field where the people grow potato gratis , and all the eastern village , where the tenant pay their rent whenever they find it rational . 
 a hot young man , in a place like this , would have do a great deal of mischief . either he would have accept large view , and applaud this fine communism   if he could afford it , and have no wife , or else he would have rush at every body headlong , and bat they back to their abutment . neither course would have create half the excitement which the Major 's do . at least , there might have be more talk at first , but not a quarter so much in sum total . of those thing , however , there be time enough to speak , if I dare to say any thing about they . 
 the thing more to my mind   and therefore more likely to be make plain to another mind   be not the petty flicker phantom of the shadow we call human , and which alone we realize , and dwell inside it and upon it , as if it be all creation ; but the infinitely nobler thing of ever - change but perpetual beauty , and no selfishness . these , without deign to we even sense to be aware of they , shape our little mind and body and our large self - importance , and fail to know when the lord or king who own be bury under they . to have perception of such mighty truth be good for all of we : and I never have keener perception of they than when I sit down on the Major 's camp - stool , and see all his land around I , and even the sea where all the fish be his , as soon as he could catch they and largely reflect that not a square foot of the whole world would ever belong to I . 
 " Bruntlands , " as the house be call , perhaps from stand well above the sea , be shelter by the curve of the eastern cliff , which look down over Bruntsea . the cliff be of chalk , very steep toward the sea , and show a prominent headland toward the south , but prettily rise in grassy curve from the inland and from the westward . and then , where it suddenly chin away from land - slope into sea - front , a long bar of shingle begin at right angle to it , and , as level as a railroad , go to the river 's mouth , a league or so now to the westward . and beyond that another line of white cliff rise , and look well till they come to their headland . inside this bank of shingle , from end to end , might be trace the old course of the river , and to landward of that trough at the hither end stand , or lay , the calm old village . 
 forsake as it be by the river , this village stick to its ancient site and home , and instead of migrating , contract itself , and cast off needless member . shrink Bruntsea clung about the old of its church , while the four other fall to rack and ruin , and settle into cow - yard and barn , and place where old man might sit and sigh . but Bruntsea distinctly and trenchantly keep the old town 's division into east and west . 
 East Bruntsea be wholly in the Major 's manor , which have a special charter ; and most of the house belong to he . this ownership hitherto have mean only that the landlord should do all the tumble - down repair   when the agent report that they must be do , but never must enter the door for his rent . the borough have be disfranchise , though the snug of the snug for generation ; and the freeman , thus be rob of their right , have no power to discharge their duty . and to complicate matter yet far , for the few who wish to simplify they , the custom of " borough - English " prevail , and govern the descent of dilapidation , make nice nicety for clever man of law . 
 " you see a fine property here , Miss Wood , " Major Hockin say to I , as we sit , on the day after I be allow to come , enjoy the fresh breeze from the sea and the newness of the February air , and look abroad very generally : " a very fine property , but neglect shamefully , horribly , atrociously neglect but capable of noble thing , of grand thing , of magnificent , with a trifle of judicious outlay . " 
 " oh , please not to talk of outlay , my dear , " say good Mrs. Hockin , gently ; " it be such an odious word ; and where in the world be it to come from ? " 
 " leave that to I . when I be a boy my favorite copy in my copy - book be , ' where there be a will there be a way . ' Miss Wood , what be your opinion ? but wait , you must have time to understand the subject . first we bring a railway always the first step ; why , the line be already make for it by the course of the old river , and the distance from Newport three mile and a half . it ought not to cost quite 200 pound a mile the mere outlay for rail and sleeper . the land be all mine , and and of course other land proprietor ' . very well : these would all unite , of course ; so that not a farthe need be pay for land , which be the good half of the battle . we have the station here not too near my house ; that would never do ; I could not bear the noise but in a fine central place where nobody on earth could object to it lively , and close at hand for all of they . unluckily I be just too late . we have lose a parliamentary year through that execrable calm you remember all about it . otherwise we would have have Billy Puff stable at Bruntsea by the first of May . but never mind ; we shall do it all the well and cheap by take our time about it . very well : we have the railway open and the trade of the place develop . we build a fine terrace of elegant villa , a crescent also , and a large hotel replete with every luxury ; and we form the fine sea - parade in England by simply assist nature . half London come down here to bathe , to catch shrimp , to flirt , and to do the rest of it . we become a select , salubrious , influential , and yet economical place ; and then what do we do , Mrs. Hockin ? " 
 " my dear , how can I tell ? but I hope that we should rest and be thankful . " 
 " not a bit of it . I should hope not , indeed . Erema , what do we do then ? " 
 " it be useless to ask I . well , then , perhaps you set up a handsome saw - mill ! " 
 " a saw - mill ! what a notion of Paradise ! no ; this be what we do but remember that I speak in the strict confidence ; dishonest antagonism might arise , if we ventilate our idea too soon Mrs. Hockin and Miss Wood , we demand the restoration of our river ! the return of our river to its ancient course . " 
 " I see , " say his wife ; " oh , how grand that would be ! and how beautiful from our window ! that really , now , be a noble thought ! " 
 " a just one simply a just one . justice ought not to be noble , my dear , however rare it may be . generosity , magnanimity , heroism , and so on those be the thing we call noble , my dear . " 
 " and the founding of city . oh , my dear , I remember , when I be at school , it be always say , in what we call our history , that the founder of city have honor pay they , and altar build , and divinity do , and holiday hold in their honor . " 
 " to that I object , " cry the Major , sternly . " if I found fifty city , I would never allow one holiday . the Sabbath be enough ; one day in seven fifteen per cent , of one 's whole time ; and twenty per cent , of your Sunday go in church . very right , of course , and loyal , and truly edify Mrs. Hockin 's father be a clergyman , Miss Wood ; and the last thing I would ever allow on my manor would be a dissenting chapel ; but still I will have no new church here , and a man who might go against I . they all want to pick their own religious view , instead of reflect who support they ! it never use to be so ; and such thing shall never occur on my manor . a good hotel , attendance include , and a sound and moderate table d'hote ; but no church , with a popish bag send round , and money to pay , ' without anything to eat . ' " 
 " my dear ! my dear ! " cry Mrs. Hockin , " I never like you to talk like that . you quite forget who my father be , and your own second son such a very sound priest ! " 
 " a priest ! do not   let he come here , " cry the Major , " or I will let he know what tonsure be , and read he the order of Melchisedec . a priest ! after go round the world three time , to come home and be hail as the father of a priest ! do not   let he come near I , or I will sacrifice he . " 
 " now , Major , you be very proud of he , " his good wife answer , as he shake his stick . " how could he help take order when he be under order to do so ? and his view be sound to the last degree , most strictly correct and practical at least except as to celibacy . " 
 " he hold that his own mother ought never to have be bear ! Miss Wood , do you call that practical ? " 
 " I have no acquaintance with such thing , " I reply ; " we have none of they in California . but be it practical , Major Hockin of course you know well in your engineering I mean , would it not require something like a tunnel for the river and the railway to run on the same ground ? " 
 " why , bless I ! that seem to have escape my notice . you have not be with old Uncle Sam for nothing . we shall have to appoint you our chief engineer . " 




 CHAPTER XXI 

 LISTLESS 

 it seem an unfortunate thing for I , and unfavorable to my purpose , that my host , and even my hostess too , should be so engross with their new estate , its beauty and capability .
