" 
 " but suppose that this excellent woman be dead , or not to be find , or have change her opinion ? " 
 " her opinion she never could change . but if she be not to be find , I shall find her husband , or her child , or somebody ; and besides that , I have a hundred thing to do . I have the address of the agent through whom my father draw his income , though Uncle Sam let I know as little as he could . and I know who his banker be   when he have a bank , and he may have leave important paper there . " 
 " come , that look a little more sensible , my dear ; banker may always be rely upon . and there may be some valuable plate , Erema . but why not let the Major go with you ? his advice be so invaluable . " 
 " I know that it be , in all ordinary thing . but I can not have he now , for a very simple reason . he have make up his mind about my dear father horribly , horribly ; I can not   speak of it . and he never change his mind ; and sometimes when I look at he I hate he . " 
 " Erema , you be quite a violent girl , although you so seldom show it . be the whole world divide , then , into two camp those who think as you wish and those who be lead by their judgment to think otherwise ? and be you to hate all who do not think as you wish ? " 
 " no , because I do not hate you , " I say ; " I love you , though you do not think as I wish . but that be only because you think your husband must be right of course . but I can not like those who have make up their mind accord to their own coldness . " 
 " Major Hockin be not cold at all . on the contrary , he be a warm - hearted man I might almost say hot - hearted . " 
 " yes , I know he be . and that make it ten time bad . he take up every body 's case but mine . " 
 " sad as it be , you almost make I smile , " my hostess answer , gravely ; " and yet it must be very bitter for you , know how just and kind my husband be . I be sure that you will give he credit for at least desiring to take your part . and do so , at least you might let he go with you , if only as a good protection . " 
 " I have no fear of any one ; and I might take he into society that he would not like . in a good cause he would go any where , I know . but in my cause , of course he would be scrupulous . your kindness I always can rely upon , and I hope in the end to earn his as well . " 
 " my dear , he have never be unkind to you . I be certain that you never can say that of he . major Hockin unkind to a poor girl like you ! " 
 " the last thing I wish to claim be any body 's pity , " I answer , less humbly than I should have speak , though the pride be only in my tone , perhaps . " if people choose to pity I , they be very good , and I be not at all offend , because because they can not help it , perhaps , from not know any thing about I . I have nothing whatever to be pity for , except that I have lose my father , and have nobody leave to care for I , except Uncle Sam in America . " 
 " your Uncle Sam , as you call he , seem to be a very wonderful man , Erema , " say Mrs. Hockin , craftily , so far as there could be any craft in she ; " I never see he a great loss on my part . but the Major go up to meet he somewhere , and come home with the stock of his good tie break , and two button go from his waistcoat . do Uncle Sam make people laugh so much ? or be it that he have some extraordinary gift of induce people to taste whiskey ? my husband be a very most abstemious man , as you must be well aware , Miss Wood , or we never should have be as we be , I be sure . but , for the first time in all my life , I doubt his discretion on the following day , when he have what shall I say ? when he have be exchange sentiment with Uncle Sam . " 
 " Uncle Sam never take too much in any way , " I reply to this new attack ; " he know what he ought to take , and then he stop . do you think that it may have be his ' sentiment , ' perhaps , that be too strong and large for the Major ? " 
 " Erema ! " cry Mrs. Hockin , with amazement , as if I have no right to think or express my thought on life so early ; " if you can talk politic at eighteen , you be quite fit to go any where . I have hear a great deal of american lady , and see not a little of they , as you know . but I think that you call yourself an english girl , and insist particularly upon it . " 
 " yes , that I do ; and I have good reason . I be bear of an old english family , and I hope to be no disgrace to it . but be bring up in a number of way , as I have be without think of it , and be quite different from the fashionable girl Major Hockin like to walk with " 
 " my dear , he never walk with any body but myself ! " 
 " oh yes , I remember ! I be think of the deck . there be no fashionable girl here yet . till the terrace be build , and the esplanade " 
 " there shall be neither terrace nor esplanade if the Major be to do such thing upon they . " 
 " I be sure that he never would , " I reply ; " it be only their dress that he like at all , and that very , to my mind , extraordinary style , as well as unbecoming . you know what I mean , Mrs. Hockin , that wonderful what shall I call it ? way of loop up . " 
 " call I ' Aunt Mary , ' my dear , as you do when the wave be so dreadful . you mean that hideous mexican poncho , as they call it , stick up here , and go down there . Erema , what observation you have ! nothing ever seem to escape you . do you ever see any thing so indecorous ? " 
 " it make I feel just as if I ought not to look at they , " I answer , with perfect truth , for so it do ; " I have never be accustom to such thing . but see how the Major approve of they , and like to be walk up and down between they , I know that they must be not only decorous , but attractive . there be no appeal from his judgment , be there ? " 
 " I agree with he upon every point , my dear child ; but I have always long to say a few word about that . for I can not help think that he go too far . " 




 CHAPTER XXII 

 BETSY BOWEN 

 so far , then , there be nobody find to go into my case , and to think with I , and to give I friendly countenance , with the exception of Firm Gundry . and I fear that he try to think with I because of his faithful and manly love , more than from balance of evidence . the Sawyer , of course , hold my father guiltless , through his own fidelity and simple way ; but he could not enter into my set thought of a stern duty lay upon I , because to his mind the opinion of the world matter nothing so long as a man do aright . for wisdom like this , if wisdom it be , I be a great deal too young and ardent ; and to I fair fame be of almost equal value with clear conscience . and therefore , wise or foolish , rich or poor , beloved or unloved , I must be listless about other thing , and restless in all , until I should establish truth and justice . 
 however , I do my good to be neither ungrateful nor stupidly obstinate , and , begin more and more to allow for honest though hateful opinion , I yield to dear Mrs. Hockin 's wish that I should not do any thing out of keep with english idea and habit . in a word , I accept the Major 's kind offer to see I quite safe in good hand in London , or else bring I straightway back again . and I take only just thing enough for a day or two , mean to come back by the end of the week . and I kiss Mrs. Hockin just enough for that . 
 it would not be a new thing for I to say that " we never know what be go to happen ; " but , new or stale , it be true enough , as old common saying of common - sense   though spurn when not want   show themselves . at first , indeed , it seem as if I be come for nothing , at least as concern what I think the chief business of my journey . the Major have wish to go first to the bank , and appear to think nothing of any thing else ; but I , on the other hand , do not want he there , prefer to keep he out of my money matter , and so he be oblige to let I have my way . 
 I always be sorry when I have be perverse , and it seem to serve I right for willfulness when no Betsy Bowen could be discover either at the place which we try first , or that to which we be send thence . Major Hockin look at I till I could have cry , as much as to hint that the whole of my story be all of a piece , all a wild - goose chase . and be more curious than ever now to go to the bank and ransack , he actually call out to the cabman to drive without delay to Messrs. Shovelin , Wayte , and Shovelin . but I beg he to allow I just one minute while I speak to the servant - maid alone . then I show she a sovereign , at which she open her mouth in more way than one , for she tell I that " though she have faithfully promise to say nothing about it , because of a dreadful quarrel between her mistress and Mrs. Strouss that be now , and a jealousy between they that be quite beyond belief , she could not refuse such a nice young lady , if I would promise faithfully not to tell . " this promise I give with fidelity , and return to the cabman , direct he to drive not to Messrs. Shovelin , Wayte , and Shovelin just yet , but to no . 17 European Square , St. Katharine 's . 
 from a maze of street and rugged corner , and in and out nearly as crooked as those of a narrow human nature , we turn at last into European Square , which be no square at all , but an oblong opening pitch with rough granite , and distinguish with a pump . there be great thoroughfare within a hundred yard , but the place itself seem unnaturally quiet upon turn suddenly into it , only murmurous with distant London din , as the spire of a shell hold the heaving of the sea . after drive three or four time round the pump , for the house be number anyhow , we find no . 17 , and I jump out . 
 " now do not   be in such a fierce hurry , Miss Wood , " cry the Major , who be now a little crusty ; " english lady allow themselves to be hand out , without hurry the gentleman who have the honor . " 
 " but I want to save you the honor , " I say . " I will come back immediately , if you will kindly wait . " and with this I run up the old step , and rang and knock , while several bearded face come and gaze through dingy window . 
 " can I see Mrs. Strouss ? " I ask , when a queer old man in fade brown livery come to the door with a candle in his hand , though the sun be shin . 
 " I be the Meesther Strouss ; when you see I , you behold the good Meeses Strouss also . " 
 " thank you , but that will not do , " I reply ; " my business be with Mrs. Strouss alone . " 
 he do not seem to like this at first sight , but politely put the chain - bolt on the door while he retire to take advice ; and the Major look out of the cab and laugh . 
 " you have well come back while you can , " he say , " though they seem in no hurry to swallow you . " 
 this be intend to vex I , and I do not even turn my head to he . the house look very respectable , and there be railing to the area . 
 " the house be very respectable , " continue Major Hockin , who always seem to know what I be think of , and now in his quick manner run up the step ; " just look , the scraper be clean . you never see that , or at least not often , except with respectable people , Erema . " 
 " pray what would my scraper be ? and who be Erema ? " cry a strong , clear voice , as the chain of the door be set free , and a stout , tall woman with a flush in her cheek confront we . " I never know more than one Erema good mercy ! " 
 my eye meet her , and she turn as pale as death , and fall back into a lobby chair . she know I by my likeness to my father , fall on the memory start by my name ; and strong as she be , the surprise overcome she , at the sound of which up rush the small Herr Strouss . 
 " Vhat be you do dere , all of you ? vhat have you enterprised with my frau ? Explain , Vilhelmina , or I call de policeman , vhat I should say de peeler . " 
 " stop ! " cry the Major , and he stop at once , not for the word , which would have have no power , although I know nothing about it then , but because he have receive a sign which assure he that here be a brother Mason . in a moment the infuriate husband vanish into the rational and docile brother . 
 " lady and gentleman , valk in , if you please , " he say , to my great astonishment ; " Vilhelmina and my good self make you velcome to our poor house . Vilhelmina , arise and say so . " 
 " go to the back kitchen , Hans , " reply Wilhelmina , whose name be " Betsy , " " and do not   come out until I tell you . you will find work to do there , and remember to pump up . I wish to hear thing that you be not to hear , mind you . shut yourself in , and if you soap the door to deceive I , I shall know it . " 
 " Vere goot , vere goot , " say the philosophical german ; " I never meddle with nothing , Vilhelmina , no more than vhat I do for de money and de house . " 
 Betsy , however , be not quite so sure of that . with no more ceremony she lock he in , and then come back to we , who could not make thing out . 
 " my husband be the brave of the brave , " she tell we , while she put down his key on the table ; " and a nobler man never live ; I be sure of that . but every one of they foreigner excuse I , Sir , you be an Englishman ? " 
 " I be , " reply the Major , pull up his little whisker ; " I be so , madam , and nothing you can say will in any way hurt my feeling . I be above nationality . " 
 " just so , Sir . then you will feel with I when I say that they foreigner be dreadful . oh , the day that I ever marry one of them but there , I ought to be ashamed of myself , and my lord 's daughter face I . " 
 " do you know I ? " I ask , with hot color in my face , and my eye , I dare say , glisten . " be you sure that you know I ? and then please to tell I how . " 
 as I speak I be take off the close silk bonnet which I have wear for travel , and my hair , have catch in a pin , fall round I , and before I could put it up , or even think of it , I lay in the great arm of Betsy Bowen , as I use to lie when I be a little baby , and when my father be in his own land , with a home and wife and seven little one . and to think of this make I keep her company in cry , and it be some time before we do any thing else . 
 " well , well , " reply the Major , who detest scene , except when he have make they ; " I shall be off . you be in good hand ; and the cabman pull out his watch when we stop . so do I. but he be sure to beat I . they draw the minute hand on with a magnet , I be tell , while the watch hang on their badge , and they can swear they never open it . wonderful age , very wonderful age , since the time when you and I be young , ma'am . " 
 " yes , Sir ; to be sure , Sir ! " Mrs. Strouss reply , as she wipe her eye to speak of thing ; " but the most wonderful of all thing , do not   you think , be the going of the time , Sir ? no cabby can make it go fast while he wait , or slow while he be a - driving , than the mind inside of we manage it . why , Sir , it wear only like yesterday that this here tall , elegant , royal young lady be a - lying on my breast , and what a hand she be to kick ! and I say that her hair be sure to grow like this . if I be to tell you only half what come across I " 
 " if you do , ma'am , the cabman would make his fortune , and I should lose mine , which be more than I can afford . Erema , after dinner I shall look you up . I know a good woman when I see she , Mrs. Strouss , which do not happen every day . I can trust Miss Castlewood with you . good - by , good - by for the present . " 
 it be the first time he have ever call I by my proper name , and that make I all the more pleased with it . 
 " you see , Sir , why I be oblige to lock he in , " cry the " good woman , " follow to the door , to clear every blur from her virtue ; " for his own sake I do it , for I feel my cry a - come , and to see I cry Lord bless you , the effect upon he be to call out for a walking - stick and a pint of beer . " 
 " all right , ma'am , all right ! " the Major answer , in a tone which appear to I unfeele . " Cabman , be you asleep there ? bring the lady 's bag this moment . " 
 as the cab disappear without my even know where to find that good protector again in this vast maze of million , I could not help let a little cold fear encroach on the warmth of my outburst . I have hear so much in America of the dark , subtle place of London , and the wicked thing that happen all along the Thames , discover or invent by great writer of their own , that the neighborhood of the dock and the thought of rat   to which I could never grow accustomed   make I look with a flash perhaps of doubt at my new old friend . 
 " you be not sure of I , Miss Erema , " say Mrs. Strouss , without take offense . " after all that have happen , who can blame it on you ? but your father be not so suspicious , miss . it might have be well for he if he have accord , leastway , to my belief , which a team of wild horse will never drag out . " 
 " oh , only let I hear you talk of that ! " I exclaim , forget all other thing . " you know more about it than any body I have ever meet with , except my own father , who would never tell a word . " 
 " and quite right he be , miss , accord to his view . but come to my little room , unless you be afraid . I can tell you some thing that your father never know . " 
 " Afraid ! do you think I be a baby still ? but I can not bear that Mr. Strouss should be lock up on my account . " 
 " then he shall come out , " say Mrs. Strouss , look at I very pleasantly . " that be just like your father , Miss Erema . but I fall into the foreign way , be so much with the foreigner . " whether she think it the custom among " foreigner " for wife to lock their husband in back kitchen be more than she ever take the trouble to explain . but she walk away , in her stout , firm manner , and presently return with Mr. Strouss , who seem to be quite content , and make I a bow with a very placid smile . 
 " he be harmless ; his idea be most grand and good , " his wife explain to I , with a nod at he . " but I could not have you in with the gentleman , Hans . he always make mistake with the gentleman , miss , but with the lady he behave quite well . " 
 " yes , yes , with the lady I be nearly always goot , " Herr Strouss reply , with diffidence . " the lady comprehend I right , all right , because I be so habitual with my wife . but the gentleman in London have no comprehension of I . " 
 " then the loss be on their side , " I answer , with a smile ; and he say , " yes , yes , they lose vere much by I . " 




 CHAPTER XXIII 

 BETSY 's TALE 

 now I scarcely know whether it would be more clear to put into narrative what I hear from Betsy Bowen , now Wilhelmina Strouss , or to let she tell the whole in her own word , exactly as she herself tell it then to I . the story be so dark and sad or at least to myself it so appear that even the little break and turn of light thought or lively manner , which could scarcely fail to vary now and then the speaker 's voice , seem almost to grate and jar upon its sombre monotone . on the other hand , by omit these , and depart from her homely style , I might do more of harm than good through fail to convey impression , or even fact , so accurately . whereas the gist and core and pivot of my father 's life and fate be so involved   though not evolve   that I would not miss a single point for want of time or diligence . therefore let I not deny Mrs. Strouss , my nurse , the right to put her word in her own way . and before she begin to do this she take the trouble to have every thing clear away and the tray bring down , that her boarder   chiefly german   might leave their plate and be drive to their pipe . 
 " if you please , Miss Castlewood , " Mrs. Strouss say , grandly , " do you or do you not approve of the presence of ' my man , ' as he call himself ? an improper expression , in my opinion ; such , however , be their nature . he can hold his tongue as well as any man , though none of they be very sure at that . and he know pretty nigh as much as I do , so far as his English can put thing together , be well accustom in German . for when we be court I be fain to tell he all , not to join he under any false pretense , miss , which might give he ground against I . " 
 " yes , yes , it be all vere goot and true so goot and true as can be . " 
 " and you might find he come very handy , my dear , to run of any kind of message . he can do that very well , I assure you , miss well than any Englishman . " 
 see that he wish to stay , and that she desire it , I beg he to stop , though it would have be more to my liking to hear the tale alone . 
 " then sit by the door , Hans , and keep off the draught , " say his Wilhelmina , kindly . " he be not very tall , miss , but he have good shoulder ; I scarcely know what I should do without he . well , now , to begin at the very beginning : I be a Welshwoman , as you may have hear . my father be a farmer near Abergavenny , hold land under Sir Watkin Williams , an old friend of your family . my father have too many girl , and my mother scarcely know what to do with the lot of we . so some of we go out to service , while the boy staid at home to work the land . one of my sister be lady' - maid to Lady Williams , Sir Watkin 's wife , at the time when your father come visit there for the shooting of the moor - fowl , soon after his marriage with your mother . what a sweet good lady your mother be ! I never see the like before or since . no soon do I set eye upon she but she so take my fancy that I would have go round the world with she . we Welsh be a very hot people , they say not cold - blooded , as the English be . so , wise or foolish , right , wrong , or what might be , nothing would do for I but to take service , if I could , under Mrs. Castlewood . your father be call Captain Castlewood then as fine a young man as ever clink a spur , but without any boast or conceit about he ; and they say that your grandfather , the old lord , keep he very close and spare , although he be the only son . now this must have be let I see , how long ago ? about five - and - twenty year , I think . how old be you now , Miss Erema ? I can keep the week well than the year , miss . " 
 " I be eighteen on my last birthday . but never mind about the time go on . " 
 " but the time make all the difference , miss , although at the time we may never think so . well , then , it must have be well than six - and - twenty year agone ; for though you come pretty fast , in the Lord 's will , there be eight year between you and the first - bear babe , who be only just a - thinking of when I begin to tell . but to come back to myself , as be mother have get too many of we still , and she be glad enough to let I go , however much she might cry over it , as soon as Lady Williams get I the place . my place be to wait upon the lady first , and make myself generally useful , as they say . but it be not very long before I be want in other more important way , and have be bring up among so many child , they find I very handy with the little one ; and be in a poor way , as they be then for people , I mean , of their birth and place they be glad enough soon to make head nurse of I , although I be under - two - and - twenty . 
 " we do not live at the old lord 's place , which be under the hill look on the river Thames , but we have a quiet little house in Hampshire ; for the Captain be still with his regiment , and only come to and fro to we . but a happy little place there could not be , with the flower , and the cow , and the bird all day , and the child run gradually accord to their age , and the pretty brook shin in the valley . and as to the paying of their way , it be true that neither of they be a great manager . the Captain could not bear to keep his pretty wife close ; and she , poor thing , be try always to surprise he with other present besides all the beautiful baby . but they never be in debt all round , as the liar say when the trouble burst ; and if they owe two or three hundred pound , who could justly blame they ? 
 " for the old lord , instead of go on as he should , and widen his purse to the number of the mouth , be niggle at they always for offense or excuse , to take away what little he allow they . the Captain have his pay , which would go in one hand , and the lady have a little money of her own ; but still it be cruel for bring - up people to have nothing well to go on with . not that the old lord be a miser neither ; but it be say , and how far true I know not , that he never would forgive your father for marry the daughter of a man he hat . and some go so far as to say that if he could have do it , he would have cut your father out of all the old family estate . but such a thing never could I believe of a nobleman have his own flesh and blood . 
 " but , money or no money , rich or poor , your father and mother , I assure you , my dear , be as happy as the day be long . for they love one another and their child dearly , and they do not care for any mixing with the world . the Captain have enough of that when put away in quarter ; likewise his wife could do without it well and well at every birth , though once she have be the very gayest of the gay , which you never will be , Miss Erema . 
 " now , my dear , you look so sad and so ' solid , ' as we use to say , that if I can go on at all , I must have something ready . I be quite an old nurse now , remember . han , go across the square , and turn on the left hand round the corner , and then three more street toward the right , and you see one go toward the left , and you go about seven door down it , and then you see a corner with a lamp - post . " 
 " Vilhelmina , I do see de lamp - post at de every corner . " 
 " that will teach you to look more bright , Hans . then you find a shop window with three blue bottle , and a green one in the middle . " 
 " how can be any middle to three , without it be one of they ? " 
 " then let it be two of they . how you contradict I ! take this little bottle , and the man with a gold braid round a cap , and a tassel with a tail to it , will fill it for four - pence when you tell he who you be . " 
 " yes , yes ; I do now comprehend . you send I vhere I never find de vay , because I be in de vay , Vilhelmina ! " 
 I be most thankful to Mrs. Strouss for send her husband   however good and kind - hearted he might be   to wander among many shop of chemist , rather than to keep his eye on I , while I listen to thing that be almost sure to make I want my eye my own . my nurse have see , as any good nurse must , that , grow and form as I might be , the nature of the little child that cry for its mother be in I still . 
 " it be very sad now , " Mrs. Strouss begin again , without reply to my grateful glance ; " Miss Erema , it be so sad that I wish I have never begin with it . but I see by your eye so like your father 's , but soft , my dear , and less troublesome that you will have the whole of it out , as he would with I once when I tell he a story for the sake of another servant . it be just about a month before you be bear , when the trouble begin to break on we . and when once it begin , it never stop until all that be leave run away from it . I have read in the newspaper many and many sad thing come over whole family , such as they call ' shocking tragedy ; ' but none of they , to my mind , could be more galling than what I have to see with my very own eye . 
 " it must have be close upon the middle of September when old Lord Castlewood come himself to see his son 's house and family at Shoxford . we hear that he come down a little on the sudden to see to the truth of some rumor which have reach he about our style of living . it be the first time he have ever be there ; for although he have very often be invite , he could not bear to be under the roof of the daughter , as he say , of his enemy . the Captain , just happen to come home on leave for his autumn holiday , meet his father quite at his own door the very last place to expect he . he afterward acknowledge that he be not pleased for his father to come ' like a thief in the night . ' however , they take he in and make he welcome , and cover up their feeling nicely , as high - breed people do . 
 " what pass among they be unknown to any but themselves , except so far as now I tell you . a well dinner than usual for two be ready , to celebrate the master 's return and the beginning of his holiday ; and the old lord , have travel far that day , be persuade to sit down with they . the five eld child   make all except the baby , for you be not bear , miss , if you please   they be to have sit up at table , as pretty as could be three with their high cushion stool , and two in their arm - chair screw on mahogany , stuff with horsehair , and with rod in front , that the little dear might not tumble out in feeding , which they do it be a sight to see they ! and how they would give to one another , with their finger wet and shin , and say , ' oo , dat for oo . ' oh dear , Miss Erema , you be never bear to see it ! what a blessing for you ! all those six dear darling lay in their little graf within six week , with their mother plant under they ; and the only wonder be that you yourself be not upon her breast . 
 " pay you no heed to I , Miss Erema , when you see I a - whimpering in and out while I be about it . it make my chest go easy , miss , I do assure you , though not at the time of life to understand it . all they child be to have sit up for the sake of their dear father , as I say just now ; but because of their grandfather all be order back . and back they come , as good as gold , with Master George at the head of they , and ask I what milk - tooth be . Grandpa have say that ' a dinner be no dinner if milk - tooth be allow at it . ' the hard old man , with his own tooth false ! he deserve to sit down to no other dinner and he never do , miss . 
 " you may be sure that I have enough to do to manage all the little one and answer all their question ; but never have see a live lord before , and want to know if the child would be like he before so very long , I go quietly down stair , and the big of my dear peep after I . and then , by favor of the parlor - maid for they keep neither butler nor footman now I see the Lord Castlewood , sit at his ease , with a glass of port - wine before he , and my sweet mistress   the Captain 's wife , and your mother , if you understand , miss   do she very well , think of her child , to please he and make the polite to he . to I he seem very much to be thaw to she if you can understand , miss , what my meaning be and the Captain be look at they with a smile , as if it be just what he have hop for . from my own eyesight I can contradict the lie put about by nobody know who , that the father and the son be at hot word even then . 
 " and I even hear my master , when they go out at the door , vainly persuade his father to take such a bed as they could offer he . and good enough it would have be for ten lord ; for I see nothing wonderful in he , nor fit to compare any way with the Captain . but he would not have it , for no other reason of ill - will or temper , but only because he have order his bed at the Moonstock Inn , where his coach and four be rest . 
 " ' I expect you to call I in the morning , George , ' I hear he say , as clear as could be , while his son be help his coat on . ' I be glad I have see you . there be bad than you . and when the time get well , I will see what I can do . ' 
 " with he this mean more than it might have do ; for he be not a man of much promise , as you might tell by his face almost , with his nose so stern , and his mouth screw down , and the wrinkle the wrong way for smile . I could not tell what the Captain answer , for the door bang on they , and it wake the baby , who be dream , perhaps , about his lordship 's face , and his little tooth give he the wind on his chest , and his lung be like bellow bless he ! 
 " well , that stop I , Miss Erema , from be truly accurate in my testimony . what with walk the floor , and thump his back , and rattle of the ring to please he when they put I on the Testament , cruel as they do , with the lawyer ' eye eat into I , and both my ear buzz with sorrow and fright , I may have go too far , with my heart in my mouth , for my mind to keep out of contradiction , wishful as I be to tell the whole truth in a manner to hurt nobody . and without any single lie or glaze of mine , I do assure you , miss , that I do more harm than good ; every body in the room a court they call it , and no big than my good parlor one and all they be convince that I would swear black be white to save my master and mistress ! and certainly I would have do so , and the Lord in heaven think the well of I , for the sake of all they child , if I could have make it stick together , as they do with practice . " 
 at thought of the little good she have do , and perhaps the great mischief , through excess of zeal , Mrs. Strouss be oblige to stop , and put her hand to her side , and sigh . and eager as I be for every word of this miserable tale , no selfish eagerness could deny her need of refreshment , and even of rest ; for her round cheek be white , and her full breast tremble . and now she be begin to make snatch at my hand , as if she see thing she could only tell thus . 




 CHAPTER XXIV 

 BETSY 's TALE   continue . 

 " I be only astonish , my dear , " say my nurse , as soon as she have have some tea and toast , and scarcely the soft roe of a red herring , " that you can put up so well , and abide with my instinct in the way you do . none of your family could have do it , to my knowledge of their disposition , much less the baby that be next above you . but it often come about to go in turn like that ; ' one , three , five , and seven be sweet , while two , four , and six be a - squalling with their foot . ' but the Lord forgive I for an ill word of they , with their precious little body wash , and lay in their pattern till the judgment - day . 
 " but put by the word I say in the dirty little room they please to call a ' court , ' and the Testament so filthy that no lip could have a hold of it , my meaning be to tell you , miss , the very thing that happen , so that you may fairly judge of they . the Captain come back from go with his father , I be sure , in less than twenty minute , and smoke a cigar in his elegant way , quite happy and content , for I see he down the staircase . as for sign of any haste about he , or wipe of his forehead , or fumble with his handkerchief , or be in a stew in any sort of way as the stupid cook who let he in declare , by reason of her own have be at the beer - barrel solemnly , miss , as I hope to go to heaven , there be nothing of the sort about he . 
 " he go into the dining - room , and mistress , who have be up stair to see about the baby , go down to he ; and there I hear they talk as pleasant and as natural as they always be together . not one of they have the small sense of trouble hang over they ; and they put away both the decanter and cruet , and come up to bed in their proper order , the master stop down just to finish his cigar and see to the door and the bringing up the silver , because there be no man - servant now . and I hear he laugh at some little joke he make as he go into the bedroom . a happy household never go to bed , nor one with well hope of a happy time to come . and the baby sleep beside his parent in his little cot , as his mother like to have he , with his blessed mouth wide open . 
 " now we three   cook and Susan and myself   be accustom to have a good time of it whenever the master first come home and the mistress be take up with he . we use to count half an hour more in bed , without any of that wicked bell - clack , and then go on to thing accord to their order , without any body to say any thing . accordingly we be all snug in bed , and turn over for another tuck of sleep , when there come a most vicious ringing of the outer bell . ' you get up , Susan , ' I hear the cook say , for there only be a door between we ; and Susan say , ' Blest if I will ! only Tuesday you put I down about it when the baker come . ' not a peg would either of they stir , no more than to call name on one another ; so I slip on my thing , with the bell go clatter all the while , like the day of judgment . I feel it to be hard upon I , and I go down cross a little just enough to give it well to a body I be not afraid of . 
 " but the Lord in his mercy remember I , miss ! when I open the door , I have no blood leave . there stand two man , with a hurdle on their shoulder , and on the hurdle a body , with the head hang down , and the front of it slouch , like a sack that have be steal from ; and behind it there be an authority with two button on his back , and he wait for I to say something ; but to do so be beyond I . not a bit of caution or of fear about my sham dress - up , as the bad folk put it afterward ; the whole of such thought be beyond I outright , and no thought of any thing come inside I , only to wait and wonder . 
 " ' this corpse belongeth here , as I be inform , ' say the man , who seem to be the master of it , and be proud to be so . ' young woman , do not   you please to stand like that , or every duffer in the parish will be here , and the boy that come hanker after it . you be off ! ' he cry out to a boy who be call some more round the corner . ' now , young woman , we must come in if you please , and the least say the soon mend . ' 
 " ' oh , but my mistress , my mistress ! ' I cry ; ' and her time up , as nigh as may be , any day or night before new moon . ' oh , Mr. Constable , Mr. Rural Polishman , take it to the tool shed , if you ever have a wife , Sir . ' now even this be turn against we as if I have expect it . they say that I must have know who it be , and to a certain length so I do , miss , but only by the dress and the manner of the corpse , and lie with an attitude there be no contradicting . 
 " I can not tell you now , my dear , exactly how thing follow . my mind be go all hollow with the sudden shock upon it . however , I have think enough to make no noise immediate , nor tell the other foolish girl , who would have set up bellowing . have year to deal with little one bring knowledge of the rest to we . I think that I must have go to master 's door , where Susan 's order be to put his shaving water in a tin , and fetch he out , with no disturbance , only in his dressing - gown . and when I tell he what it be , his rosy color turn like sheet , and he just say , ' hush ! ' and nothing more . and guess what he mean , I run and put my thing on properly . 
 " but have time to think , the shock begin to work upon I , and I be fit for nothing when I see the child smile up with their tongue out for their bread and milk , as they use to begin the day with . and I do assure you , Miss Erema , my bitter thought be of your coming , though unknown whether male or female , but both most inconvenient then , with thing in such a state of thing . you have much to answer for , miss , about it ; but how be you to help it , though ? 
 " the tool - shed door be too narrow to let the hurdle and the body in , and find some large sea - kale pot stand out of use against the door , the two man   who be tired with the weight and fright , I dare say   set down their burden upon these , under a row of hollyhock , at the end of the row of bee - hive . and here they wipe their forehead with some rag they have for handkerchief , or one of they with his own sleeve , I should say , and , gain their breath , they begin to talk with the boldness of the sunrise over they . but Mr. Rural Polishman , as he be call in those part , be walk up and down on guard , and despise of their foolish word . 
 " my master , the Captain , your father , miss , come out of a window and down the cross - walk , while I be at the green door peep , for I think that I might be want , if only to take order what be to be do inside . the constable stiffly touch his hat , and march to the head of the hurdle , and say , 
 " ' do you know this gentleman ? ' 
 " your father take no more notice of he than if he have be a stiff hollyhock , which he might have resemble if he have be good - look . the Captain think highly of discipline always , and no kind gentleman could there be to those who give his due to he . but that man 's voice have a low and dirty impertinent sort of a twang with it . nothing could have be more unlucky . every thing depend on that fellow in an ignorant neighborhood like that ; and his lordship , for such he be now , of course , would not even deign to answer he . he stand over his head in his upright way by a good foot , and order he here and there , as the fellow have be expect , I do believe , to order his lordship . and that make the bitter enemy of he , be newly send into these part , and puff up with authority . and the two miller 's man could not help grin , for he have wave they about like a pair of dog . 
 " but to suppose that my master ' be unmove , and take it brutally '   as that wretch of a fellow swore afterward , only show what a stuck - up dolt he be . for when my master have examine his father , and make his poor body be bring in and spread on the couch in the dining - room , and send I hot - foot for old Dr. Diggory down at the bottom of Shoxford , Susan peep in through the crack of the door , with the cook to hold her hand behind , and there she see the Captain on his knee at the side of his father 's corpse , not say a word , only with his head down . and when the doctor come back with I , with his night - gown positive under his coat , the first thing he say be , ' my dear Sir my lord , I mean do not   take on so ; such thing will always happen in this world ; ' which show that my master be no brute . 
 " then the Captain stand up in his strength and height , without any pride and without any shame , only in the power of a simple heart , and he say word fit to hang he : 
 " ' this be my doing ! there be no one else to blame . if my father be dead , I have kill he ! ' 
 " several of we now be look in , and the news go out like a winnowing woman with no one to shut the door after she ; our passage be crowd with people that should have have a tar - brush in their face . and of course a good score of they run away to tell that the Captain have murder his father . the milk - man stand there with his yoke and can , and his naily boot on our new oil - cloth , and , not be able to hide himself plainly , he pull out his slate and begin to make his bill . 
 " ' away with you all ! ' your father say , come suddenly out of the dining - room , while the doctor be unbutton my lord , who be dead with all his day clothe on ; and every body brush away like fly at the depth of his voice and his stature . then he bolt the door , with only our own people and the doctor and the constable inside . your mother be sleep like a lamb , as I could swear , have have a very tiring day the day before , and be well away from the noise of the passage , as well as at a time when they must sleep whenever sleep will come , miss . bless her gentle heart , what a blessing to be out of all that scare of it ! 
 " all this time , you must understand , there be no sign yet what have happen to his lordship , over and above his be dead . all of we think , if our mind make bold to think , that it must have please the Lord to take his lordship either with an appleplexy or a sudden heart - stroke , or , at any rate , some other gracious way not have any flow of blood in it . but now , while your father be go up stair for he know that his father be dead enough to be sure that your mother be quiet , and perhaps to smooth she down for trouble , and while I be run away to stop the ranting of the child , old Dr. Diggory and that rural officer be handle poor Lord Castlewood . they set he to their liking , and they cut his clothe off so Susan tell I afterward and then they find why they be force to do so , which I need not try to tell you , miss . only they find that he be not dead from any wise visitation , but because he have be shoot with a bullet through his heart . 
 " Old Dr. Diggory come out shake , and without any wholesome sense to meet what have arise , after all his practice with dead man , and he call out ' murder ! ' with a long thing in his hand , till my master leap down the stair , twelve at a time , and lay his strong hand on the old fool 's mouth . 
 " ' would you kill my wife ? ' he say ; ' you shall not kill my wife . ' 
 " ' Captain Castlewood , ' the constable answer , pull out his staff importantly , ' consider yourself my prisoner . ' 
 " the Captain could have throttle he with one hand , and Susan think he would have do it . but , instead of that , he say , ' very well ; do your duty . but let I see what you mean by it . ' then he walk back again to the body of his father , and see that he have be murder . 
 " but , oh , Miss Erema , you be so pale ! not a bit of food have you have for hour . I ought not to have tell you such a deal of it to once . let I undo all your thing , my dear , and give you something cordial ; and then lie down and sleep a bit . " 
 " no , thank you , nurse , " I answer , call all my little courage back . " no sleep for I until I know every word . and to think of all my father have to see and bear ! I be not fit to be his daughter . " 




 CHAPTER XXV 

 BETSY 's TALE   Concluded . 

 " well , now , " continue Mrs. Strouss , as soon as I could persuade she to go on , " if I be to tell you every little thing that go on among they , miss , I should go on from this to this day week , or I might say this day fortnight , and then not half be do with it . and the bad of it be that those little thing make all the odd in a case of that sort , show what the great thing be . but only a counselor at the Old Bailey could make head or tail of the going on that follow . 
 " for some reason of his own , unknown to any living being but himself , whether it be pride   as I always say   or something deep   as other people think , he refuse to have any one on earth to help he , when he ought to have have the deep lawyer to be find . the constable caution he to say nothing , as it seem be lay down in their order , for fear of crimination . and he smile at this , with a high contempt , very fine to see , but not bodily wise . but even that jack - in - office could perceive that the poor Captain think of his sick wife up stair , and his little child , ten time for one thought he ever give to his own position . and yet I must tell you that he would have no denial , but to know what it be that have kill his parent . when old Dr. Diggory 's hand be shake so that his instrument would not bite on the thing lodge in his lordship 's back , after pass through and through he , and he be call for somebody to run for his assistant , who do you think do it for he , Miss Erema ? as sure as I sit here , the Captain ! his face be like a rock , and his hand no less ; and he say , ' allow I , doctor . I have be in action . ' and he fetch out the bullet which show awful nerve , accord to my way of thinking as if he have be a man with three row of tooth . 
 " ' this bullet be just like those of my own pistol ! ' he cry , and he sit down hard with amazement . you may suppose how this go against he , when all he desire be to know and tell the truth ; and people say that of course he get it out , after a bottleful of doctor fail , because he know well how it be put in . ' 
 " ' I shall now go and see the place , if you please , or whether you please or not , ' my master say . ' constable , you may come and point it out , unless you prefer go to your breakfast . my word be enough that I shall not run away . otherwise , as you have act on your own authority , I shall act on mine , and tie you until you have obtain a warrant . take your choice , my man ; and make it quickly , while I offer it . ' 
 " the rural polishman star at this , be use on the other hand to be make much of . but see how capable the Captain be of act up to any thing , he make a sulky scrape , and say , ' Sir , as you please for the present , ' weight his voice on those last three word , as much as to say , ' pretty soon you will be handcuff . ' ' then , ' say my master , ' I shall also insist on the presence of two person , simply to use their eye without any fear or favor . one be my gardener , a very honest man , but apt to be late in the morning . the other be a faithful servant , who have be with we for several year . their name be Jacob Rigg and Betsy Bowen . you may also bring two witness , if you choose . and the miller 's man , of course , will come . but order back all other . ' 
 " ' that be perfectly fair and straightforward , my lord , ' the constable answer , fall naturally into abeyance to order . ' I be sure that all of we wish your lordship kindly out of this rum scrape . but my duty be my duty . ' 
 " with a few more word we all set forth , six in number , and no more ; for the constable say that the miller 's man , who have first find the late Lord Castlewood , be witness enough for he . and Jacob Rigg , whose leg be far apart   as he say   from trench celery , take we through the kitchen - garden , and out at a gap , which save every body know . 
 " then we pass through a copse or two , and across a meadow , and then along the turnpike - road , as far as now I can remember . and along that we go to a stile on the right , without any house for a long way off . and from that stile a foot - path lead down a slope of grass land to the little river , and over a hand - bridge , and up another meadow full of tree and bush , to a gate which come out into the road again a little to this side of the Moonstock Inn , save a quarter of a mile of road , which run straight up the valley and turn square at the stone bridge to get to the same inn . 
 " I can not expect to be clear to you , miss , though I see it all now as I see it then , every tree , and hump , and hedge of it ; only about the distance from this to that , and that to the other , they would be beyond I . you must be on the place itself ; and I never could carry distance no , nor even clever man , I have hear my master say . but when he come to that stile he stop and turn upon all of we clearly , and as straight as any man of man could be . ' here I see my father last , at a quarter past ten o'clock last night , or within a few minute of that time . ' I wish to see he to his inn , but he would not let I do so , and he never bear contradiction . he say that he know the way well , have fish more than thirty year ago up and down this stream . he cross this stile , and we shake hand over it , and the moon be bright , I look into his face , and he say , ' my boy , God bless you ! ' know his short way , I do not even look after he , but turn away , and go straight home along this road . upon my word as an Englishman , and as an officer of her Majesty , that be all I know of it . now let we go on to the to the other place . 
 " we all of we know in our heart , I be sure , that the Captain speak the simple truth , and his face be grand as he look at we . but the constable think it his duty to ask , 
 " ' do you hear no sound of a shot , my lord ? for he fall within a hundred yard of this . ' 
 " ' I hear no sound of any shot whatever . I hear an owl hoot as I go home , and then the rattle of a heavy wagon , and the bell of horse . I have say enough . let we go forward . ' 
 " we obey he at once ; and even the constable look right and leave , as if he have be wrong . he sign to the miller 's man to lead the way , and my lord walk proudly after he . the path be only a little narrow track , with the grass , like a front of hair , fall over it on the upper side and on the under , drop away like side curl ; such a little path that I be wonder how a great lord could walk over it . then we come down a steep place to a narrow bridge across a shallow river abridge make of only two plank and a rail , with a prop or two to carry they . and one end of the handrail be fasten into a hollow and stubby old hawthorn - tree , overhang the bridge and the water a good way . and just above this tree , and under its shadow , there come a dry cut into the little river , not more than a yard or two above the wooden bridge , a water - trough such as we have in Wales , miss , for the water to run in , when the farmer please ; but now there be no water in it , only gravel . 
 " the cleverest of the miller 's man , though , neither of they have much intellect , step down at a beck from the constable , right beneath the old ancient tree , and show we the mark on the grass and the gravel make by his lordship where he fall and lay . and it seem that he must have fall off the bridge , yet not into the water , but so as to have room for his body , if you see , miss , partly on the bank , and partly in the hollow of the meadow trough . 
 " ' have you search the place well ? ' the Captain ask . ' have you find any weapon or implement ? ' 
 " ' we have find nothing but the corpse , so far , ' the constable answer , in a surly voice , not like to be teach his business . ' my first duty be to save life , if I could . these man , upon find the body , run for I , and know who it be , I come with it to your house . ' 
 " ' you act for the good , my man . now search the place carefully , while I stand here . I be on my parole , I shall not run away . Jacob , go down and help they . ' 
 " whether from be in the army , or what , your father always speak in such a way that the most stiff - necked people begin without think to obey he . so the constable and the rest go down , while the Captain and I stand upon the plank , look at the four of they . 
 " for a long time they look about , accord to their attitude , without find any thing more than the sign of the manner in which the poor lord fall , and of these the constable pull out a book and make a pencil memorial . but presently Jacob , a spry sort of man , cry , ' Hulloa ! whatever have I get hold of here ? many a good craw - fish have I pull out from this bank when the water come down the gully , but never one exactly like this here afore . ' 
 " ' name of the Lord ! ' cry the constable , jump behind the hawthorn stump ; ' do not   point it at I , you looby ! it be load , load one barrel , do not   you see ? put it down , with the muzzle away from I . ' 
 " ' hand it to I , Jacob , ' the Captain say . ' you understand a gun , and this go off just the same . ' Constable Jobbins have no fear . ' yes , it be exactly as I think . this pistol be one of the double - barrel pair which I buy to take to India . the barrel be rifle ; it shoot as true as any rifle , and almost as hard up to fifty yard . the right barrel have be fire , the other be still load . the bullet I take from my father 's body most certainly come from this pistol . ' 
 " ' can ' e say , can ' e say then , who do it , master ? ' ask Jacob , a man very sparing of speech , but ready at a beck to jump at constable and miller 's man , if only law be with he . ' can ' e give a clear account , and let I chuck ' un in the river ? ' 
 " ' no , Jacob , I can do nothing of the kind , ' your father answer ; while the rural man come up and face thing , not be afraid of a fight half so much as he be of an accident ; by reason of his own mother have be blow up by a gunpowder start at Dartford , yet come down all right , miss , and have he three month afterward , accord to his own confession ; nevertheless , he come up now as if he have always be upright , in the world , and he say , ' my lord , can you explain all this ? ' 
 " your father look at he with one of his strange gaze , as if he be measure the man while try his own inward do of his own mind . proud as your father be , as proud as ever can be without cruelty , it be my firm belief , Miss Erema , go on a woman 's judgment , that if the man 's eye have come up to my master 's sense of what be virtuous , my master would have up and tell he the depth and content of his mind and heart , although totally go beyond he . 
 " but Jobbins look back at my lord with a grin , and his little eye , hard to put up with . ' have you nothing to say , my lord ? then I be afeared I must ask you just to come along of I . ' and my master go with he , miss , as quiet as a lamb ; which Jobbins say , and even Jacob fancy , be a conscience sign of guilt . 
 " now after I have tell you all this , Miss Erema , you know very nearly as much as I do . to tell how the grief be break to your mother , and what her state of mind be , and how she sit up on the pillow and cry , while thing go on from bad to bad , and a verdict of ' willful murder ' be bring against your father by the crowner 's man , and you come headlong , without so much as the bird in the ivy to chirp about you , right into the thick of the bad of it . I do assure you , Miss Erema , when I look at your bright eye and clear figure , the Lord in heaven , who have make many cripple , must have look down special to have bring you as you be . for trouble upon trouble fall in heap , fast than I can wipe my eye to think . to begin with , all the servant but myself and gardener Jacob run away . they say that the old lord haunt the house , and walk with his hand in the middle of his heart , pull out a bullet if he meet any body , and sigh ' murder ' three time , till every hair be crawl . I take it on myself to fetch the Vicar of the parish to lay the evil spirit , as they do in Wales . a nice kind gentleman he be as you could see , and wear a velvet skull - cap , and wait with his leg up . but whether he feel that the power be not in he , or whether his old lordship be frightened of the Church , they never make any opportunity between they to meet and have it out , miss . 
 " then it seem as if Heaven , to avenge his lordship , rain down pestilence upon that house . a horrible disease , the bad I ever meet , break out upon the little harmless dear , the pride of my heart and of every body 's eye , for lovelier or well one never come from heaven . they be all go to heaven in a fortnight and three day , and lay in the church - yard at one another 's side , with little bed of mould to the measure of their stature , and their little cart and drum , as they make I promise , ready for the judgment - day . oh , my heart be break , miss , my heart be break ! I cry so , I think I could never cry more . 
 " but when your dear mother , who know nothing of all this   for we put all their illness , by the doctor 's order , away at the further end of the house , when she be a little well of grievous pain and misery   for be so upset her time be hard , when she sit up on the pillow , look like a bride almost , except that she have what bride have not   a little red thing in white flannel at her side then she say to I , ' I be ready , Betsy ; it be high time for all of they to see their little sister . they always love the baby so , whenever there be a new one . and they be such man and woman to it . they have be so good this time that I have never hear they once . and I be sure that I can trust they , Betsy , not to make the baby cry . I do so long to see the darling . now do not even whisper to they not to make a noise . they be too good to require it ; and it would hurt their little feeling . ' 
 " I have well have be shoot , my dear , accord as the old lord be , than have the pain that go through all my heart , to see the mother so . she sit up , lean on one arm , with the hand of the other round your little head , and her beautiful hair be come out of its loop , and the color in her cheek be like a shell . past the fringe of the curtain , and behind it too , her soft bright eye be a - look here and there for the first to come in of her child . the Lord only know what lie I tell she , so as to be satisfied without they . first I say they be all go for a walk ; and then that the doctor have order they away ; and then that they have get the measle . that last she believe , because it be bad than what I have say before of they ; and she beg to see Dr. Diggory about it , and I promise that she should as soon as he have do his dinner . and then , with a little sigh , be very weak , she go down into her nest again , with only you to keep her company . 
 " well , that be bad enough , as any mortal sufferer might have say ; enough for one day at any rate . but there be almost bad to come . for when I be have a little sit down stair , with my supper and half pint of ale   that come like draw a long breath to we when spar out of sickroom , miss , and have no nursery now on my mind , be think of all the sad business , with only a little girl in the back kitchen come in to muck up the dish , there appear a good knock at the garden door , and I know it for the thumb of the Captain . I lock the young girl up , by know what their tongue be , and then I let your father in , and the candle - sight of he make my heart go low . 
 " he have come out of prison ; and although not be try , his clothe be still in decency , they have great hole in they , and the gloss all go to a smell of mere hedge and ditch . the hat on his head be quite out of the fashion , even if it could be call a hat at all , and his beautiful beard have no sign of a comb , and he look as old again as he have look a month ago . 
 " ' I know all about it . you need not be afraid , ' he say , as I take he to the breakfast - room , where no one up stair could hear we . ' I know that my child be all dead and bury , except the one that be not bear yet . Ill news fly quick . I know all about it . George , Henrietta , Jack , Alf , little Vi , and Tiny . I have see their graf and count they , while the fool of a policeman beat his glove through the hedge within a rod of I . oh yes , I have much to be thankful for . my life be in my own hand now . ' 
 " ' oh , master ; oh , Captain ; oh , my lord ! ' I cry ; ' for the sake of God in heaven , do not   talk like that . think of your sweet wife , your dear lady . ' 
 " ' Betsy , ' he answer , with his eye full upon I , noble , yet frightful to look at , ' I be come to see my wife . go and let she know it , accord to your own discretion . ' 
 " my discretion would have be not to let he see she , but go on and write to she from foreign country , with the salt sea between they ; but I give you my word that I have no discretion , but from pity and majesty obey he . I know that he must have break prison , and by good right ought to be starve . but I could no more offer he the cold ham and pullet than take he by his beard and shake he . 
 " ' be he come , at last , at last ? ' my poor mistress say , whose wit be wander after her child . ' at last , at last ! then he will find they all . ' 
 " ' yes , ma'am , at last , at the last he will , ' I answer , while I think of the burial service , which I have hear three time in a week for the little one go to their graf in pair to save ceremony ; likewise of the Epistle of Saint Paul , which be not like our Lord 's way of talk at all , but argue instead of comfort . and not to catch she up in that weak state , I say , ' he will find every one of they , ma'am . ' 
 " ' oh , but I want he for himself , for himself , as much as all the rest put together , ' my dear lady say , without listen to I , but put her hand to her ear to hearken for even so much as a mouse on the stair . ' do bring he , Betsy ; only bring he , Betsy , and then let I go where my child be . '

 CHAPTER XXVI 

 AT the bank 

 in tell that sad tale my faithful and soft - hearted nurse have often prove her own mistake in say , as she do , that tear can ever be exhaust . and I , for my part , though I could scarcely cry for eager listening , be bad off perhaps than if I have wet each sad fact as it go by . at any rate , be it this way or that , a heavy and sore heart be leave I , too distracted for ask question , and almost too depressed to grieve .

 CHAPTER XXVII 

 COUSIN MONTAGUE 

 Mr. Shovelin go to a corner of the room , which might be call his signal - box , have a little row of port - hole like a toy frigate or accordion , and there he make sound which bring step very promptly , one clerk carry a mighty ledger , and the other a small strong - box .

" 
 certainly I do , and the banker split the seal with an ebony - handle paper - knife , and very soon unlock the steel - rib box , whose weight be chiefly of itself . some cotton - wool lie on the top to keep the all - penetrative dust away , and then a sheet of blue foolscap paper , partly cover with clear but crooked writing , and under that some little twist of silver paper , screw as if there have be no time to tie they , and a packet of letter hold together by a glitter bracelet .

 " open it , and never think of they , " say i. " like the rest , they have forsake he . please to read it to yourself , and then tell we . "

' a banker must never encroach upon the province of the lawyer . but so far as a layman may judge , Major Hockin , I think you will have to transfer to I the care of this young lady . " 
 " I shall be only too happy , I assure you , " the Major answer , truthfully . " my wife have a great regard for she , and so have I the very great , the strong regard , and warm parental feeling ; as you know , Erema . but but , I be not so young as I be ; and I have to develop my property . "

 in spite of pride , or by its aid , my foolish eye be full of tear , and I give he a look of gratitude which remind he of my father , as he say in so many word .

Erema , my dear , you must be most anxious to get to the bottom of it . " 
 so I be , but desire even more that his curiosity should be foil . " we must leave that to Mr. Shovelin , " I say .

" 
 " we have take up a great deal of your time , Sir , I be sure , " say the Major , find that he could take no more . " we ought to be , and we be , most grateful . " 
 " well , " the banker answer , as we begin to move , ' such thing do not happen every day . but there be no friend like an old friend , Erema , as I mean to call you now . I be to have be your godfather ; but I fear that you never have be baptize . "

"

" never mind , my dear , we will make that all right . you shall not be a savage always . we will take the opportunity to change your name .  " Jemima ! " I cry . " oh , Mr. Shovelin , save I from ever be call Jemima ! rather would I never be baptize at all . "

 " if you please ; but later in the day , when I be more at leisure . I do not run away very early . come at half past four to this door , and knock . I hear every sound at this door in my room ; and the place will be grow quiet then . " 
 he show we out into a narrow alley through a heavy door sheathe with iron , and soon we recover the fair light of day , and the brawl and roar of a London street . 
 " now where shall we go ? " the Major ask , as soon as he have find a cab again ; for he be very polite in that way .  CHAPTER XXIX 

 AT the PUMP 

 this blow be so sharp and heavy that I lose for the moment all power to go on . the sense of ill fortune fall upon I , as it fall upon strong people , when a sudden gleam of hope , break through long trouble , mysteriously fade away . 
 even the pleasure of indulge in the gloom of evil luck be a thing to be ashamed of now , when I think of that good man 's family thus , without a moment 's warning , rob of love and hope and happiness . but Mrs. Strouss , who often brood on predestination , imbittere all my thought by say , or rather convey without word , that my poor father taint of some Divine ill - will have re - appeared , and even kill his banker . 
 Betsy hold most low - church view , by nature be a Dissenter . she call herself a baptist , and in some strange way have stop I thus from ever have be baptize . I do not understand these thing , and the battle fight about they ; but know that my father be a member of the English Church , I resolve to be the same , and tell Betsy that she ought not to set up against her master 's doctrine . then she herself become ashamed of try to convert I , not only because of my ignorance   which make argument like shoot into the sea , but chiefly because she could mention no one of title with such theology . 
 this settle the question at once ; and remember   to my shame   what opinion I have hold even of Suan Isco , while be in the very same predicament myself , reflect also what Uncle Sam and Firm would have think of I , have they know it , I anticipate the Major and his dinner party by go to a quiet ancient clergyman , who examine I , and be satisfied with little , take I to an old City church of deep and damp retirement . and here , with a great din of traffic outside , and a mildewy depth of repose within , I be present by certain sponsor   the clerk and his wife and his wife 's sister , and hear good word , and hope to keep the impression , both outward and inward , gently make upon I . 
 I need not say that I keep , and now receive with authority , my old name ; though the clerk prefix an aspirate to it , and indulge in two syllable only . but the ancient parson know its meaning , and look at I with curiosity ; yet , be a gentleman of the old school , put never a question about it . 
 now this be do , and full tiding thereof send off to Mrs. Hockin , to save trouble to the butcher , or other disappointment , I scarcely know how to be move next , though move I must before very long . for it cost I a great deal of money to stay in European Square like this , albeit Herr Strouss be of all man the most generous , by his own avowal , and his wife   by the same test   noble - hearted among woman . yet each of they speak of the other 's pecuniary view in such a despond tone   when the other be out of the way , and so lament to have any thing at all to say about cash by compulsion of the other also both , when meet together , be so large and reckless , and not to be insult by a thought of payment , that it come to pass that my money do nothing but run away between they . 
 this be not their fault at all , but all my own , for be unable to keep my secret about the great nugget . the Major have tell I not to speak of this , accord to wise experience ; and I have not the small intention of do an atom of mischief in that way ; but somehow or other it come out one night when I be be pity for my desolation . and all the charge against I begin to be double from that moment . 
 if this have be all , I should not have care so much , be quite content that my money should go as fast as it come in to I . but there be another thing here which cost I as much as my board and lodging and all the rest of my expense . and that be the iron pump in European Square . for this pump stand in the very centre of a huddled district of famine , filth , and fever . when once I have see from the lead of our house the quag of reek life around , the stub and snag of chimney - pot , the gash among they entitle street , and the break blain call house , I be quite ashamed of pay any thing to become a Christian . 
 Betsy , who stand by I , say that it be well than it use to be , and that all these people live in comfort of their own idea , fiercely resent all interference , and be good to one another in their own rough way . it be more than three year since there have be a single murder among they , and even then the man who be kill confess that he deserve it . she tell I , also , that in some mining district of Wales , well know to she , thing be a great deal bad than here , although the people be not half so poor . and finally , look at a ruby ring which I have beg she to wear always , for the sake of her truth to I , she beg I to be wise than to fret about thing that I could not change . " all these people , whose hovel I see , have the mean of grace before they , and if they would not stretch forth their hand , it be only because they be vessel of wrath . her pity be rather for our poor black brother who have never enjoy no opportunity , and therefore must be castaway . " 
 be a stranger , and so young , and accustom to receive my doctrine   since first I go to America , I drop all intention of attempt any good in place where I might be murder . but I could not help look at the pump which be in front , and the poor thing who come there for water , and , most of all , the child . with these it be almost the joy of the day , and perhaps the only joy , to come into this little open space and stand , and put their back up stiffly , and stare about , ready for some good luck to turn up such as a horse to hold , or a man come out of the dock with a half - penny to spare and then , in failure of such golden hope , to dash about , in and out , after one another , splashing , and kick over their own can , kettle , jar , or bucket , and stretch their dirty little naked leg , and show very often fine white chest , and bright tooth wet with laughter . and then , when this chivy be do , and their quick little heart beat aloud with glory , it be pretty to see they all rally round the pump , as crafty as their better , and watch with sly humor each other 's readiness to begin again . 
 then suddenly a sense of neglect duty would seize some little body with a hand to its side , nine time out of ten a girl , whose mother , perhaps , lie sick at home , and a stern idea of responsibility begin to make the bucket clank . then might you see , if you care to do so , orderly management have its turn a demand for pin and a tucking up of skirt   which scarcely seem worthy of the great young fuss , large child scold little one not a bit more muddy than themselves , the while the very least child of all , too young as yet for chivying , and only come for company , would smooth she comparatively clean frock down , and look up at her sister with condemnatory eye . 
 Trivial as they be , these thing amuse I much , and make a little checker of reflect light upon the cloud of selfish gloom , especially when the real work begin , and the child , vie with one another , set to at the iron handle . this be too large for their little hand to grasp , and by mean of some grievance inside , or perhaps through a cruel trick of the plumber , up go the long handle every time small finger be too confiding , and there it stand up like the tail of a rampant cow , or a branch inaccessible , until an old shawl or the cord of a peg - top could be cast up on high to reduce it . but some engineering boy , " highly gifted , " like Uncle Sam 's self , " with machinery , " have discover an ingenious cure for this . with the help of the girl he use to fasten a fat little thing , about twelve month old , in the bend at the middle of the handle , and there   like a ham on the steelyard   hang this baby and enjoy seesaw , and laugh at its own utility . 
 I never see this , and the splashing and dribble and play and bright revelry of water , without forget all sad counsel and discretion , and rush out as if the dingy pump be my own delicious Blue River . People use to look at I from the window with pity and astonishment , suppose I to be craze or frantic , especially the Germans . for to run out like this , without a pocket full of money , would have be insanity ; and to run out with it , to their mind , be even clear proof of that condition . for the money go as quickly as the water of the pump ; on this side and on that it fly , each child in succession make deep drain upon it , in virtue of still deep woe . they be dreadful little story - teller , I be very much afraid ; and the long face pull , as soon as I come out , in contrast with all the recent glee and frolic , suggest to even the young charity suspicion of some inconsistency . however , they be so ingenious and clever that they work my pocket like the pump itself , only with this unhappy difference , that the former have no inexhaustible spring of silver , or even of copper . 
 and thus , by a reason   as cogent as any of more exalted nature , be I drive back to my head - quarter , there to abide till a fresh supply should come . for Uncle Sam , generous and noble as he be , do not mean to let I melt all away at once my share of the great Blue River nugget , any more than to make duck and drake of his own . indeed , that rock of gold be still untouched , and healthily repose in a banker 's cellar in the good town of Sacramento . People be allow to go in and see it upon payment of a dollar , and they come out so thirsty from feast upon it that a bar be set up , and a pile of money make all the gentleman , and lady even bad than they , take a reckless turn about small money after see that . but dear Uncle Sam refuse every cent of the profit of all this excitable work . it be wholly against his wish that any thing so artificial should be do at all , and his sense of religion condemn it . he say , in his very first letter to I , that even a heathen must acknowledge this champion nugget as the grand work of the Lord yet discover in America a country more full of all work of the Lord than the rest of the world put together . and to keep it in a cellar , without any air or sun , grate harshly upon his idea of right . 
 however , he do not expect every body to think exactly as he do , and if they could turn a few dollar upon it , they be welcome , as have large family . and the balance might go to his credit against the interest on any cash advance to he . not that he mean to be very fast with this , never have run into debt in all his life . 
 this , put shortly , be the reason why I could not run to the pump any long . I have come into England with money enough to last I   accord to the sawyer 's calculation   for a year and a half of every needful work ; whereas , in less than half that time , I be arrive at my last penny . this remind I of my dear father , who be nearly always in trouble about money   although so strictly upright ; and at first I be proud to be like he about this , till I come to find the disadvantage . 
 it must not even for a moment be imagine that this make any difference in the behavior of any one toward I . Mrs. Strouss , Herr Strouss , the lady on the stair , and a very clever woman who have get no room , but be kindly accommodate every where , as well as the baron on the first floor front , and the gentleman from a hotel at Hanover , who look out the other way , and even the child at the pump not one make any difference toward I   as an enemy might , perhaps , suppose   because my last half crown be go . it be admit upon every side that I ought to be forgive for my random cast of money , because I know no well , and be sure to have more in a very little time . and the child of the pump come to see I go away , through street of a mile and a half , I should think ; and they carry my thing , look after one another , so that none could run away . and be forbid at the platform gate , for want of respectability , they set up a cheer , and I wave my hat , and promise , amidst great applause , to come back with it full of sixpence . 




 CHAPTER XXX 

 COCKS and COXCOMBS 

 Major Hockin bring the only fly as yet to be find in Bruntsea , to meet I at Newport , where the railway end at present , for want of further encouragement .
