 pass through the church - yard , which be my near way , and glance sadly at the " fairy ring , " I begin to have some uneasiness about the possible issue of my new scheme . such a thing require more thinking out than I have give to it . for instance , what reason could I give the miller for ask so strange a thing of he ? and how could the whole of the valley be hinder from make the great talk about the stoppage of their own beloved Moon , even if the Moon could be stop without every one of they rush down to see it ? and if it be so talked of , would it not be certain to come to the ear of that awful man ? and if so , how long before he find I out , and send I to rejoin my family ? 
 these thought compel I to be more discreet ; and have lately do a most honorable thing , in refuse to read that letter , I feel a certain right to play a little trick now of a purely harmless character . I run back therefore to my writing - desk , and take from its secret drawer a beautiful golden american eagle , a large coin , large and handsomer than any in the english coinage . Uncle Sam give it to I on my birthday , and I would not have take 50 pound for it . with this I hurry to that bridge of fear , which I have not yet bring myself to go across ; and then , not to tell any story about it , I snip a little hole in the corner of my pocket , while my hand be still steady ere I have to mount the bridge . then pinch that hole up with a squeeze , I run and get upon that wicked bridge , and then let go . the heavy gold coin fall upon the rotten plank , and happily roll into the water , as if it be glad not to tempt its maker to any more sin for the sake of it . 
 shut up thought , for fear of despise myself for the coinage of such a little trick , I hurry across the long meadow to the mill , and go through the cow - gate into the yard , and the dog begin to bark at I . see that he have a strong chain on , I regard he with lofty indignation . " do you know what Jowler would do to you ? " I say ; " Jowler , a dog worth ten of you . he would take you by the neck and drop you into that pond for dare to insult his mistress ! " the dog appear to feel the force of my remark , for he lie down again , and with one eye watch I in a manner amusing , but insidious . then , take good care to keep out of his reach , I go to the mill - pond and examine it . 
 it look like a very nice pond indeed , long , and large , and well bank up , not make into any particular shape , but produce little rushy elbow . the water be now rather low , and very bright   though the Moon itself be not a crystal stream , and a school of young minnow , just watch a water - spider with desirous awe , at sight of I break away , and reunite , with a speed and precision that might shame the whole of our very good modern fighting . then many other thing make a dart away , and furrow the shadow of the willow , till distance quiet the fear of man that most mysterious thing in nature and the shallow pool be at peace again , and bright with unruffled reflection . 
 " what ail the dog ? " say a deep gruff voice ; and the poor dog receive a contemptuous push , not enough to hurt he , but to wound his feeling for do his primary duty . " Servant , miss . what can I do for you ? foot - path be t'other side of that there hedge . " 
 " yes , but I leave the foot - path on purpose . I come to have a talk with you , if you will allow I . " 
 " sartain ! sartain , " the miller reply , lift a broad floury hat and show a large gray head . " will you come into house , miss , or into gearden ? " 
 I choose the garden , and he lead the way , and set I down upon an old oak bench , where the tinkle of the water through the flood - gate could be hear . 
 " so you be come to paint the mill at last , " he say . " many a time I have   look out for you . the young leddy down to Mother Busk 's , of course . many be the time we have   long for you to come , you remind we so of somebody . why , my old missus can not   set eye on you in church , miss , without be force to sit down a'most . but we think it very pretty of you not to come , miss , while the trouble be so new upon we . " 
 something in my look or voice make the old man often turn away , while I tell he that I would make the very good drawing of his mill that I could manage , and would beg he to accept it .

 " but you have other leave . she be not the only one . please , Mr. Withypool , to try to think of that . and your dear wife still alive to share your trouble . just think for a moment of what happen to my father . his wife and six child all sweep off in a month and I just bear , to be bring up with a bottle ! " 
 I never mean , of course , to have say a word of this , but be carry away by that common old idea of console great sorrow with a great one . and the sense of my imprudence break vexatiously upon I when the old man come and stand between I and his daughter 's portrait . 
 " well , I never ! " he exclaim , with his bright eye steadfast with amazement . " I know you now , miss . now I know you . to think what a set of blind newts we must be ! and you the very moral of your poor father , in a female kind of way ! to be sure , how well I know the Captain ! a nice man never walk the earth , neither a more unlucky one .  " hush , miss , hush ! not my own wife shall know , unless your own tongue telleth she . a proud man I shall be , Miss Raumur , " he continue , with emphasis on my local name , " if aught can be find in my power to serve you . why , Lord bless you , miss , " he whisper , look round , " your father and I have spend hour together ! he be that pleasant in his way and word , he would drop in from his fishing , when the water be too low , and sit on that very same bench where you sit , and smoke his pipe with I , and tell I about battle , and ask I about bread . and many a time I have slip up the gate , to give he more water for his fly to play , and the fish not to see he so plainly . ah , we have have many pleasant spell together ; and his eld boy and girl , Master George and Miss Henrietta , use to come and fetch our egg . my Polly there be in love with he , we say ; she sit upon his lap so , when she be two year old , and play with his beautiful hair , and blubber oh , she do blubber , when the Captain go away ! " 
 this invest Polly with new interest for I , and make I determine to spare no pain in put she pretty figure well upon the plank . then I say to the miller , " how kind of you to draw up your sluice - gate to oblige my father ! now will you put they down and keep they down , to do a great service both to he and I ? "

Miller Sims , a mile or so down river , must be settle with , to fill his dam well , and begin to discharge , when the upper water fail , so as not to dry the Moon all down the valley , which would have cause a commotion . Miller Sims be own brother - in - law to Master Withypool , that could be arrange easily enough , after one day 's notice . but a hard thing to manage would be to do the business without rouse curiosity , and set abroad a rumor which would be sure to reach my enemy . and the hard thing of all , say Master Withypool , smile as he think of what himself have once be , would be to keep those bless boy away , who find out every thing , and go every where . not a boy of Shoxford but would be in the river , or dance upon its empty bed , screech and scollop up into his cap any poor bewildered trout chase into the puddle , if it be allow to leak out , however feebly , that the Moon water be to stop run . and then how be I to seek for any thing ? 
 this be a puzzle . but , with counsel , we do solve it . and we quietly stop the Moon , without man or boy be much the wiser . 




 CHAPTER XLIII 

 go to the bottom 

 it be not needful to explain every thing , any more than it be for I to tell the miller about my golden eagle , and how I have manage to lose it in the Moon a trick of which now I be heartily ashamed , in the face of honest kindness . so I need not tell how Master Withypool manage to settle with his man , and to keep the boy unwitting of what be about to come to pass . enough that I get a note from he to tell I that the little river would be run out , just when all Shoxford be intent upon its dinner , on the second day after I have see he . and he could not say for certain , but think it pretty safe , that nobody would come near I , if I manage to be there at a quarter before one , when the stream would begin to run dry , and I could watch it . I send back a line by the pretty little girl , a sister of poor Polly , to say how much I thank he , and how much I hop that he himself would meet I there , if his time allow . for he have be too delicate to say a word of that ; but I feel that he have a good right to be there , and , know he now , I be not afraid . 
 nearly every thing come about as well as could be wish almost . Master Withypool take the precaution , early in the morning , to set his great fierce bull at large , who always stop the foot - path . this bull know well the power of a valley in conduct sound ; and he love to stand , as if at the mouth of a funnel , and roar down it to another bull a mile below he , belong to his master 's brother - in - law . and when he do this , there be scarcely a boy , much less a man or woman , with any desire to assert against he the public right of thoroughfare . throughout that forenoon , then , this bull bellow nobly , still find many very wicked fly about , so that two mitche boy , who mean to fish for minnow with a pin , be oblige to run away again . 
 however , I be in the dark about he , and as much afraid of he as any body , when he break into sight of I round a corner , without any token of amity .  much as I have watch this bridge from a distance , or from my sheltering - place , I have never be able to bring myself to make any kind of sketch of it , or even to insert it in a landscape , although it be very well suited and expressive , from its crooked and antique simplicity . the overhanging , also , of the hawthorn - tree   not ruddy yet , but russety with its color crop of coral , and the shaggy freak of ivy above the twisted trunk , and the curve of the meadow and bold elbow of the brook , be such as an artist would have pitch his tent for , and tantalize poor London people with a dream of cool repose . 
 as yet the little river show no sign of do what the rustic or surely it should have be the cockney be suppose to stand still and wait for . there be no great rush of headlong water , for that be not the manner of the stream in the very bad of weather ; but there be the usual style of come on , with lip and step at the side , and cord of run toward the middle . quite enough , at any rate , to make the trout jump , without any omen of impend drought , and to keep all the play and the sway of movement go on serenely . 
 I begin to be afraid that the miller must have fail in his stratagem against the water - god , and that , as I have read in Pope 's Homer , the liquid deity would beat the hero , when all of a sudden there be sign that man be the master of this little rustic . broadsword of flag and rapier of water - grass , which have be quiver merrily , begin to hang down and to dip themselves in loop , and the stone of the brink show dark green stripe on their side as they stand naked . then fine little cake of conglomerate stuff , which only a great man of nature could describe , come float about , and curdle into corner , and hold on to one another in long - tail string . but they might do what they like , and make their very good of it , as they fall away to nothing upon stone and mud . for now more important thing begin to open , the like of which never have be yield up before plot of slimy gravel , vary with long streak of yellow mud , dot with large double shell , and part into little oozy run by wriggle water - weed . and here be great commotion and sad panic of the fish , large fellow splash and quite jump out of water , as their favorite hover and shelf run dry , and dart away , with their poor back in the air , to the deep hole they could think of . hundred must have come to flour , lard , and butter if boy have be there to take advantage . but luckily thing have be do so well that boy be now in their least injurious moment , destroy nothing bad than their own dinner . 
 a very little way below the old wooden bridge the little river run into a deepish pool , as generally happen at or near a corner , especially where there be a confluence sometimes . and see nothing , as I begin to search intently , stir with a long - handle spud which I have bring , I conclude that even my golden eagle have be carry into that deep place . however , water or no water , I resolve to have it out with that dark pool as soon as the rest of the channel should be drain , which take a tormenting time to do ; and have thick boot on , I pin up my skirt , and jump down into the shoal , begin to paddle in a fashion which remind I of childish day pass pleasantly in the Blue River . 
 too busy thus to give a thought to any other thing , I do not even see the miller , until he say , 
 " good - day , miss , " lift his hat , with a nice kind smile . " very busy , miss , I see , and right you be to be so . the water will be upon we again in less than half an hour . now let I clear away they black weed for you . I bring this little shivel a - purpose . if I may make so bold , miss , what do ' e look to find here ? " 
 " I have not the very small notion , " I could only answer ; " but if there be any thing , it must be in that hole . I have search all the shallow part so closely that I doubt whether even a sixpence could escape I , unless it be bury in the mud or pebble . oh , how can I manage to search that hole ? there must be a yard of water there . " 
 " one thing I ought to have tell ' e for to do , " Master Withypool whisper , as he go on shovel " to do what the boy do when they lose a farden to send another after un . if so be now , afore the water be run out , you have stand on that there bridge , and drop a bright coin into it , a new half crown or a two - shilling piece , why , the chance would be that the run of the current would ' a take it nigh to the likeli spot for hold any other little matter as might ' a drop , permiskous , you might say , into this same water . " 
 " I have do so , " I answer ; " I have do that very thing , though not at all with that object . the day before yesterday a beautiful coin , a golden eagle of America , fall from my pocket on that upper plank , and roll into the water . I would not lose it for a great deal , because it be give to I by my dear friend , the great of all miller . " 
 " and ha'n't   you find it yet , miss ? well , that be queer . perhaps we shall find it now , with something to the back of it . I think yon hole be too far below the bridge . but there your gold must be , and something else , most likely . plaise to wait a little bit , and we will have the wet out of un . I never should ' a thought of that but for your gold guinea , though . " 
 with these word Master Withypool pull his coat off and roll up his shirt sleeve , display arm fit to hold their own even with Uncle Sam 's almost ; and then he fall to with his shovel and dig , while I run with my little spud to help . 
 " Plaise keep out of way , miss ; I be afeard of knock you . not but what you work very brave indeed , miss . " 
 know what man be concern " female effort , " I get out of the strong man 's way , although there be plenty of room for I . what he want to do be plain enough to dig a trench down the empty bed of the Moon River , deep enough to drain that pit before the stream come down again . 
 " never think to run a race against my own old dam , " he say , as he stop for a moment to recover breath . " we never know what we may have to do . old dam must be a'most bust now . but she be sound enough , till her beginneth to run over . " 
 I do not say a word , because it might have do some mischief , but I could not help look rather anxiously up stream , for fear of the water come down with a rush , as it very soon must do . Master Withypool have be work , not as I myself would have do , from the lip of the dark pit downward , but from a steep run some twenty yard below , where there be almost a little cascade when the river be full flow ; from this he have make his channel upward , cut deep as he come along , till now , at the brink of the obstinate pool , his trench be two foot deep almost . I have no idea that any man could work so with a shovel , which seem such a clumsy tool compare with a spade : but a gentleman who know the country and the people tell I that , with their native weapon , Moonites will do as much digging in an hour as other folk get through in an hour and a half with a spade . but this may be only , perhaps , because they be work hard .

 HERMETICALLY seal

 CONVICTION

 CHAPTER XLVI 

 VAIN ZEAL 

 leave his telescope level at the man , the Major march off with his opera - glass in a consciously provoke style , and Mrs. Hockin most heartily join I in condemn such behavior . in a minute or two , however , she would not have one word say against he , and the tide of her mind   as befit a married woman   be beyond all science ; so that the drift of all word come back to her husband 's extraordinary merit . and certainly these , if at all like her description , deserve to be dwell upon at very precious period .

 CHAPTER XLVII 

 cadmeian victory 

 before two o'clock of the following day Major Hockin and myself be in London , and ready to stay there for two or three day , if it should prove needful . before leave Bruntsea I have write briefly to Lord Castlewood , tell he that important matter have take I away from Shoxford , and as soon as I could explain they , I would come and tell he all about it . this be do only through fear of his being annoy at my independence .

Scarcely think a hofficer would ' a try evasion . "

"

 Major Hockin 's breath be short , through too much talk without action , and he wait for a minute at this door , to come back to his equanimity . and I think that our female breath fall short for the very opposite reason when we do too much and talk too little ; which happily seldom happen .

" I could trust these man with the Koh - i - noor ; which we could have do well , I believe , than it be do by the Hollanders . but we do not   get the chance to do much in diamond , through the old superstition about Amsterdam , and so on . no , no ; the only thing I can not   trust my man about be to work as hard when I be away as when I be there . and now , Sir , what can I do for you ? any more Bruntsea pebble ? the last be not worth the cutting .  " you do not mean to say that you know the artist ? " I could not help exclaim , though determine not to speak . " oh , then , we shall find out every thing ! " 
 " Erema , you be a well , you be a silly ! " major Hockin exclaim , and then color with remember that rather he should have let my lapse pass . but the lapidary seem to pay no attention , only to be call down to some one far below . " now mind what you say , " the Major whisper to I , just as if he be the essence of discretion . 
 " the work - room be clear now , " Mr. Handkin say ; " the fellow be delighted to get their afternoon . now you see that I have to take off this hoop , and there lie the difficulty . I could have take out the gold back , as I say , with very little trouble , by simply cut it . but the locket would never have be quite the same , though we put a new back ; and , more than that , the pressure of the tool might flaw the enamel , or even crack the portrait , for the make of this thing be peculiar . now first I submit the rim or verge , without touch the brilliant , mind you , to the action of a little preparation of my own a gentle but penetrative solvent . you be welcome to watch I ; you will be none the wiser ; you be not in the trade , though the young lady look as if she would make a good polisher . very well : if this be an ordinary closure , with two flat surface meeting , the solvent would be absorb into the adhesion , expansion would take place , and there we have it . but this be what we call a cyme - joint , a cohesion of two curved surface , form in a reflex curve which admit the solvent most reluctantly , or , indeed , not at all , without too long application . for that , then , another kind of process be needful , and we find it in frictional heat apply most gradually and judiciously . for that I must have a buff - leather wheel , whose revolution be time to a nicety , and that wheel I only have in this room . now you see why I send the man away .  though I watch his work with great interest , it be out of my power to describe it now , and , moreover , it be not needful . major Hockin , accord to his nature , grow quite restless and impatient , and even go out for a walk , with his cane unpacked and unsheathe against cabman . but I be content to wait and watch , have always hear and think that good work will not do itself , but must have time and skill to second it . and Mr. Handkin , move arm , palm , and finger beautifully , put the same thought into word . 
 " good work take a deal of time to do ; but the man that do it all the time know well that it will take long to undo . here it come undo at last ! "

 there be nothing more inside this locket , except two little wisps of hair tie with gold thread , and the miniature upon ivory , bear on the back some anagram , probably that of the artist . 
 already have I pass through a great many trouble , change , chance , and adventure which always seem strange   when I come to look back , but never surprise I at the moment . indeed , I might almost make bold to pronounce that not many person of my age and sex have be visit , wholly against their own will , by such a series of incident , not to say marvelous , but at any rate fairly to be call unusual . and throughout they perhaps it will be acknowledge by all who have care to consider they , that up to the present time I do not fail more than themselves might have do in patience . and in no description of what come to pass have I color thing at all in my own favor at least so far as intention go neither lay myself out to get sympathy , though it often would have do I a world of good .

 my comrade turn back , and put these question ; and the private inquirer answer that they have no idea of his whereabouts , but could easily imagine many good reason for his present reserve of claim . for instance , he might be wait for discovery of further evidence ; or   which be even more likely   for the death of the present Lord Castlewood , which could not be very far distant , and would remove the chief opponent . it grieve I deeply to find that my cousin 's condition be so notorious , and treat of in such a cold - blooded way , like a mule fall lame , or a Chinaman in Frisco . 
 " my dear , you must grow use to such thing , " Major Hockin declare , when he see that I be vex , after leave those selfish premise . " if it be not for death , how could any body live ? right feeling be show by consider such point , and make for the demise of other even more preparation than for our own . otherwise there be a selfishness about it by no means Christian - minded . you look at thing always from such an intense and even irreligious point of view . but such thing be out of my line altogether . your Aunt Mary understand they well . " 
 " would you be able , " I say , " to account to Aunt Mary conscientiously for that dreadful story which I hear you tell ? I scarcely know where I stand , Major Hockin . " 
 " you mean about Montague ? family honor must be defend at any price . child , I be greatly pained to go beyond the truth ; but in such a case it be imperative . I be shocked and amazed at my cousin 's conduct ; but how could I let such a fellow know that ? and think what I owe to his father , Sir Rufus ? no , no ; there be time when Bayard himself must stretch a point . honor and religion alike demand it ; and Mrs. Hockin need never hear of it . " 
 " certainly I shall not speak of it , " I answer , though a little surprised at his argument ; " but you mean , of course , to find out all about it . it seem to I such a suspicious thing . but I never could bear Sir Montague . " 
 the Major smile grimly , and , perceive that he wish to drop the subject , I say no more . he have many engagement in London always , and I must not attempt to engross his time . however , he would not for a moment hear of leave I any where but with Betsy , for perhaps he see how strange I be . and , be alone at last with she , I could keep up my pride no long . 
 through all that have happen , there never have be such a dreadful trial as I have bear this day without a word to any one . danger and loss and sad dreariness of mind , from want of young companionship ; mystery also , and obscurity of life , have always be my fortune . with all of these I have strive , to the good of my very small ability , have from nature no gift except the dull one of persistence . and throughout that struggle I have feel quite sure that a noble yearning for justice and a lofty power of devotion be my two impelling principle . but now , when I see myself sprung of low birth , and the father of my worship base - bear , down fall all my arduous castle , and I crave to go under the earth and die . 
 for every word of Mr. Goad , and every crooked turn of little thing in twist against I even the Major 's last grim smile all begin to work together , and make up a wretched tumult , sound in my ear like drum . where be the use of go on , of prove any body 's guilt or any body 's innocence , if the utmost issue of the whole would be to show my father an impostor ? then , and only then , I know that love of abstract justice be to little mind impossible , that sense of honor be too prone to hang on chance of birth , and virtue 's fountain , self - respect , spring but ill from parental taint . 
 when I could no long keep such bitter imagining to myself , but pour they forth to Betsy , she merely laugh , and ask I how I could be such a simpleton . only to think of my father in such a light be beyond her patience ! where be my pride , she would like to know , and my birth , and my family manner ? however , she do believe there be something in my idea , if you turn they inside out , and take hold of they by the other end . it be much more likely , to her mind , that the villain , the unknown villain at the bottom of all the misery , be really the son bear out of wedlock , if any such there be at all , and therefore a wild harum - scarum fellow like Ishmael in the Book of Genesis . and it would be just of a piece , she think , with the old lord 's character to drive such a man to desperation by refuse to give he a farthing . 
 " all that might very well be , " I answer ; " but it would in no way serve to explain my father 's conduct , which be the great mystery of all . " nevertheless , I be glad to accept almost any view of the case rather than that which have force itself upon I since the opening of the locket . any doubt of that most wretched conclusion be a great relief while it last ; and , after so long a time of hope and self - reliance , should I cast away all courage through a mere suspicion ? 
 while I be thus re - assure myself , and be re - assured by my faithful nurse , sad news arrive , and drive my thought into another crooked channel . Mrs. Hockin , to meet my anxiety for some tiding from California , have promise that if any letter come , she would not even wait for the post , but forward it by special messenger . and thus , that very same evening , I receive a grimy epistle , in an unknown hand , with the postmark of Sacramento . tear it open , I read as follow : 
 " MISS ' REMA , no good luck ever come , since you , to this Blue River Station , only to be wash away , and rob by greaser , and shoot through the rib , and get more work than can do , and find an almighty nugget send by Satan . and now the very bad luck of all have come , wholly and out of all denial , by you and your face and grace and french going on . not that I do not like you , mind ; for you always be very polite to I , and do your good when you find I try to put up with the trial put on I . but now this trial be the bad of all that ever come to my establishing ; and to go away now as I use to think of do when tyrannize upon be out of my way altogether , and only an action fit for a half - breed . Sawyer Gundry hath cut and run , without a word behind he no instruction for order in hand , and pour in no direction where to find he , not even ' God bless you ' to any one of the many hand that look up to he . only a packet of dollar for I to pay the wage for two month to come , and a power of lawyer to receive all debt , and go on anyhow just the same . and to go on just the same be more than the bad of we have the heart for , without the sight of his old red face . he may have be pretty sharp , and too much the master now and then , perhaps ; but to do without he be a darn sight bad , and the hand do not   take to I like he . many be the time I have see his fault , of have his own way , and such like , and pay a man beyond his time if his wife be out of order . and many be the time I have say myself I be fitter to be at the head of it . 
 " about that I be right enough , perhaps , if I have start upon my own hook ; but to stand in the track he have wear to his own foot be to go into crooked compass . there be never a day without some hand threaten to strike and to well himself , as if they be hog to come and go accord to the acorn ; and such low word I can never put up with , and pack they off immediate . no place can be carry on if the master be to shut up his lip to impudence . and now I have only get three hand leave , with work enough for thirty , and they three only stop on , I do believe , to grumble of I if the Sawyer do come home ! 
 " but what we all want to know and old Suan take a black stick to make mark for you be why the old man hath run away , and where . Young Firm , who be get a sight too uppish for I to have long put up with he , he be go about here , there , and every where , from the very first time of your go away , open his mouth a deal too much , and ask low question how long I stop to dinner . Old Suan say he be troubled in his mind , as the pale - face do about young girl , instead of drag they to their wigwam ; and she would give he a spell to get over it . but nothing come of that ; and when the war break out , he have word with his grandfather , and go off , so they say , to join the rebel . 
 " Sawyer let he go , as proud as could be , though he would soon have cut his own head off ; and the very same night he sit down by his fire and sham to eat supper as usual . but I happen to go in to get some order , and , my heart , I would never wish to see such thing again ! 
 " the old man would never waste a bit of victual , as you know , Miss ' Rema ; and , be acquaint with Suan 's way of watch , he have slip all his supper aside from his plate , and put it on a clean pocket - handkerchief to lock it in the press till his appetite should serve ; and I catch he in the act , and it vex he . ' Ha'n't   you the manner to knock at the door ? ' he say ; and I say , ' certainly , ' and go back and do it ; and , trouble as he be , he grin a bit . then he bow his great head , as he always do when he know he have go perhaps a trifle too far with a man in my position . I nod to forgive he , and he stand across , and see that he could do no less than liquor I , after such behavior . but he only bring out one glass ; and I say , ' come , Colonel , square be square , you know . ' ' excuse of I , Martin , ' he say ; ' but no drop of strong drink pass the brim of my mouth till this gallivanting be do with . I might take too much , as the old man do , to sink what they do not   want to think on . ' ' you mean about bully - cock firm , ' say I ; ' rebel firm nigger - driver firm . ' ' hush ! ' he say ; ' no bad word about it . he have go by his conscience and his heart . what do we know of what come inside of he ? ' 
 " this be true enough , for I never do make that boy out to my liking : and the old man now be as stiff as a rock , and pretty nigh as peculiar . he make I a cocktail of his own patent , to show how firm his hand be ; but the line of his face be like wainscot moulding , and the cord of his arm stand out like cog . then he take his long pipe , as he may have do perhaps every blessed night for the last fifty year ; but that length of time ought to have learn he well than to go for to fill it upside down . ' ha , ha ! ' he say ; ' every thing be upside down since I be a man under heaven country and nation and kindred and duty ; and why not a old tobacco - pipe ? that be the way baby blow bubble with they . we shall all have to smoke them that way if our noble republic be bust up . fill your , and try it , Martin . ' 
 " instead of enjoy my cocktail , Miss ' Rema , I never be so down at mouth ; for , to my mind , his old heart be break while he carry on so . and let every body say what they will , one thing there be no denying of . never be see on this side of the big hill a man fit to walk in the track of Uncle Sam , so large and good - hearted accord to his light , hard as a grizzly bear for a man to milk he , but soft in the breastbone as a young prairie - hen for all folk down upon their nine - pin . 
 " you may be surprised , miss , to find I write so long . fact be , the thing will not   go out of my mind without it . and it give I a comfort , after all I may have say , to put good opinion upon paper . if he never should turn up again , my language will be to his credit ; whereas if he do come back , with the bet a horse to a duck against it , to his pride he will read this testimonial of your , faithfully , MARTIN CLOGFAST . 
 " P.S. can not   carry on like this much long . enough to rip one 's heart up . you never would know the old place , miss . the head of the horse be as long as their tail with the way they carry they ; the moss be as big as a Spaniard 's beard upon the kitchen door - sill ; and the old dog howl all day and night , like fifty thousand scalper . Suan saith , if you be to come back , the lad might run home after you . ' tisn't   the lad I care about so much , but poor old Sawyer , at his time of life , swallow up in the wilderness . " 




 CHAPTER L 

 the PANACEA 

 as if my own trouble be not enough , so deeply be I grieve by this sad news that I have a great mind to turn back on my own and fly to far - off disaster . to do so appear for the moment a noble thing , and almost a duty ; but now , look back , I perceive that my instinct be right when it tell I to stay where I be , and see out my own sad story first . and Betsy grow hot at the mere idea of my hankering after a miller 's affair , as she very rudely express it . to hear about lord and lady , and their crime and adventure , be lovely ; but to dwell upon people of common birth , and in trade , be most unbeseeming . a man who mend his own mill , and have hand like horn well , even she be of well blood than that , she hop . 
 before these large and liberal view have fairly be expound , Major Hockin arrive , with his mind in such a state that he open his watch every second . 
 " Erema , I must speak to you alone , " he cry ; " no , not even you , Mrs. Strouss , if you please . if my ward like to tell you , why , of course she can ; but nobody shall say that I do . there be thing that belong to the family alone . the most loyal retainer you know what I mean . " 
 " General , I be not aware that you belong to the family . but this way , Sir ; this way , if you please . there be lath and plaster to that wall , and a crack in the panel of the door , Sir . but here be a room where I keep my jam , with double brick and patent lock , from sweet - toothed lodger . the ' scutcheon go over the key - hole , General . perhaps you will see to that , while I roll up the carpet outside ; and then , if any retainer come , you will hear their footstep . " 
 " bless the woman , what a temper she have ! " whisper the Major , in dread of her ear . " be she go , Erema ? she want discipline . " 
 " yes , she be go , " I say , try to be lightsome ; " but you be enough to frighten any one . " 
 " so far from that , she have quite frighten I . but never mind such trifle . Erema , since I see you I have discover , I may almost say , every thing . " 
 come upon I so suddenly , even with all allowance make for the Major 's sanguine opinion of his own deed , this have such effect upon my flurry brain that practice alone enable I to stand upright and gaze at he . 
 " perhaps you imagine when you place the matter in my hand , Miss Castlewood , " he go on , with sharp twinkle from the gable of his eye , but soft caress to his whisker , " that you would be leave in the hand of a man who encourage a crop of hay under his foot . never do you or any body make a great mistake . that be not my character , Miss Castlewood . " 
 " why do you call I ' Miss Castlewood ' so ? you quite make I doubt my own right to the name . " 
 Major Hockin look at I with surprise , which gladden even more than it sham I . clearly his knowledge of all , as he describe it , do not comprise the disgrace which I fear . 
 " you be almost like Mrs. Strouss to - day , " he answer , with some compassion . " what way be the wind ? I have often observe that when one female show asperity , nearly all the other do the same . the weather affect they more than man , because they know nothing about it . but to come back be you prepared to hear what I have get to tell you ? " 
 I bow without say another word . for he should be almost the last of mankind to give a lecture upon irritation . 
 " very well ; you wish I to go on . perceive how sadly you be upset by the result of those interview , first with Handkin , and then with Goad , after leave you here I drive at once to the office , studio , place of business , or whatever you please to call it , of the famous fellow in the portrait line , whose anagram , private mark , or whatever it be , be burn into the back of the ivory . Handkin tell I the fellow be dead , or , of course , his work would be worth nothing ; but the name be carry on , and the register keep , at a little place somewhere in Soho , where , on the strength of his old repute , they keep up a small trade with inferior hand . I give they a handsome order for a thing that will never be handsome , I fear my old battered physiognomy . and then I produce the locket which in some queer state of mind you have give I , and make they hunt out their old book , and at last discover the very entry . but to verify it I must go to Paris , where his son be live . " 
 " whose son ? Lord Castlewood 's ? " 
 " Erema , have you take leave of your sens ? what son have Lord Castlewood ? the artist 's son , to be sure ; the son of the man who do the likeness . be it the vellum and the stuff upon it that have so upset your mind ? I be glad that you show it to I , because it would have be mean to do otherwise . but show it to no one else , my dear , except your cousin , Lord Castlewood . he have the first right of all to know it , though he will laugh at it as I do . trumpery of that sort ! let they produce a certify copy of a register . if they could do that , need they ever have shoot that raffish old lord I beg pardon , my dear your highly respected grandfather ? no , no ; do not   tell I . Nicholas Hockin be never in any way famous for want of brain , my dear , and he tell you to keep your pluck up . " 
 " I never can thank you enough , " I reply , " for such inspiriting counsel . I have be rather miserable all this day . and I have have such a letter from America ! " 
 without my intend any offer of the kind , or have such idea at the furth tip of any radius of mind , I find myself under a weight about the waist , like the thing the young girl put on now . and this be the arm of the Major , which have be knock about in some action , but be useful still to let other people know , both in this way and that , what he think of they . and now it let I know that he pity I . 
 this kindness from so old a soldier make I partial to he . he have take an age to understand I , because my father be out of the army almost before I be bear , and therefore I have no tradition . also , from want of drilling , I have be awkward to this officer , and sometimes mutinous , and sometimes a coward . all that , however , he forgive I when he see I so downhearted ; and while I be strive to repress all sign , the quivering of my lip perhaps suggest thought of kissing . whereupon he kiss my forehead with nice dry lip , and tell I not to be at all afraid . 
 " how many time have you be brave ? " he inquire , to set I counting , know from all his own child , perhaps , that nothing stop futile tear and the waste of sob like prompt arithmetic . " Six , if not seven , time you have display considerable valor . be you go to fall away through some wretched imagination of your own ? now do not   stop to argue time will not allow it . I have put Cosmopolitan Jack as well upon the track of Captain Brown . I have not tell you half of what I could tell , and what I be do ; but never mind , never mind ; it be well that you should not know too much , my dear . young mind , from their want of knowledge of the world , be inclined to become uneasy . now go to bed and sleep soundly , Erema , for we have lot to do to - morrow , and you have have a most worrying day to - day . to - morrow , of course , you must come with I to Paris . you can parleyvoo well than I can . " 
 however , as it happen , I do nothing of the kind , for when he come back in the morning , and while he be fidget and hurry I , and vow that we should lose the tidal train , a letter from Bruntsea be put into my hand . I see Mrs. Price 's clear writing , follow by good Aunt Mary 's crooked line , and know that the latter must have receive it too late to be send by her messenger . in few word it tell I that if I wish to see my cousin alive , the only chance be to start immediately . 
 shock and self - reproach and wonder come   as usual   before grief , which always mean to stay , and wait to get its mourning ready . I love and respect my cousin more deeply than any one living , save Uncle Sam ; and now to lose they both at once seem much too dreadful to be true . there be no time to think . I take the Major 's cab , and hurry off to Paddington , leave he to catch his tidal train . 
 alas ! when I get to Castlewood , there be but a house of mourning ! Faithful Stixon 's eye be dim , and he point upward and say , " hush ! " I enter with great awe , and ask , " how long ? " and he say , " four - and - twenty hour now ; and a more peacefull end be never see , and to lament be sinful ; but he be bless if he could help it . " I tell he , through my tear , that this be greatly to his credit , and he must not crush fine feeling , which be an honor to our nature . and he say that I be mistress now , and must order he to my liking . 
 I ask he to send Mrs. Price to I , if she be not too busy ; and he answer that he believe she to be a very good soul , and handy . and if he ever have be think to speak in a sense disparishing of she , such thing should not be bear in mind , with great affliction over we . Mrs. Price , hear that I be come , already be on her way to I , and now glance at the door for Mr. Stixon to depart , in a manner past misunderstanding . 
 " he give himself such air ! " she say ; ' sometimes one would think but I will not trouble you now with that , Miss Castlewood , or Lady Castlewood which do you please to be call , miss ? they say that the barony go on , when there be no more viscount . " 
 " I please to be call ' Miss Castlewood , ' even if I have any right to be call that . but do not   let we talk of such trifle now . I wish to hear only of my cousin . " 
 " well , you know , ma'am , what a sufferer he have be for year . if ever an angel have pain all over , and one leg compulsory of a walking - stick , that angel be his late lordship . he would stand up and look at one , and give order in that beautiful silvery voice of his , just as if he be lie on a bed of down . and never a twitch , nor a hitch in his face , nor his word , nor any other part of he . I assure you , miss , that I have be quite amazed and overwhelm with interest while look at his poor leg , and think " 
 " I can quite enter into it . I have feel the same . but please to come to what have happen lately . " 
 " the very thing I be at the point of do . then last Sunday , God alone know why , the pain do not come on at all . for the first time for seven year or more the pain forget the time - piece . his lordship think that the clock be wrong ; but wait with his usual patience , though miss it from the length of custom , instead of be happy . but when it be come to an hour too late for the proper attack of the enemy , his lordship send order for Stixon 's boy to take a good horse and ride to Pangbourne for a highly respectable lawyer . there be no time to fetch Mr. Spines , you see , miss , the proper solicitor , who live in London . the gentleman from Pangbourne be here by eight o'clock ; and then and there his lordship make his will , to supersede all other will . he put it more clearly , the lawyer say , than he himself could have put it , but not , of course , in such legal word , but doubtless far more beautiful . nobody in the house be forget ; and the rule of law being , it seem , that those with good cause to remember must not witness , two of the tenant be send for , and write down their name legitimate . and then his lordship lie back and smile , and say , ' I shall have no more pain . ' 
 " all that night and three day more he sleep as sound as a little child , to make up for so many year . we call two doctor in ; but they only whisper and look dismal , and tell we to have hot water ready at any hour of the day or night . nobody love he as I do , miss , from see so much of his trouble and miraculous way of bear they ; and I sit by the hour and hour , and watch he , trust no pay nurse . 
 " it must have be eight o'clock on Wednesday morning what be to - day ? oh , Friday then Thursday morning it must have be , when the cloud open up in the east , and the light of the sun be on the window - sill , not glare or star , but play about , with pattern of leaf between it ; and I go to screen it from his poor white face ; but he open his eye , as if he have be half awake , half dream , and he try to lift one of his thin , thin hand to tell I not to do it . so I let the curtain stay as it be , and creep back , and ask , very softly , ' will your lordship have some breakfast ? ' 
 " he do not seem to comprehend I , but only watch the window ; and if ever a blessed face there be , look toward heaven 's glory , his lordship have it , so that I could scarcely keep from sob . for I never have see any live body die , but know that it must be so . he hear I catch my breath , perhaps , or at any rate he look at I ; and the poor angel know that I be a woman ; and be full of high respect , as he always be for female in spite of the way they have serve he it become apparent to his mind that the pearl button of his neck be open , as order by the doctor . and he try to lift his hand to do it ; and then he try to turn away , but could not manage either . poor dear ! the only movement he could make be to a well world . 
 " then I draw the sheet across his chest , and he give I a little smile of thank , and perhaps he know whose hand it be . but the look of his kind soft eye be flicker not steady , I mean , miss but glance and stop and go astray , as drop of rain do on the window - glass . but I could not endure to examine he much ; at such a holy time I feel that to watch death be unholy . 
 " perhaps I ought to have ring the bell for other to be present . but his lordship be always shy , you know , miss ; and with none of his kindre leave , and no wife to say ' good - by ' to he , right or wrong I resolve alone to see he depart to his everlasting rest . and people may talk about hireling , but I think nobody love he as I do . " 
 here Mrs. Price break fairly down , and I could not help admire she . to a faithful servant 's humility and duty she have add a woman 's pure attachment to one more gifted than herself , and ruin for life by her own sex . but she fall away frightened and ashamed beneath my look , as if I have catch she in sacrilege . 
 " well , miss , we all must come and go , " she begin again , rather clumsily ; " and , good and great as he be , his lordship have leave few to mourn for he . only the bird and beast and animal that he be so good to ; they will miss he , if man do not . there come one of his favorite pigeon , white as snow all over , and sit on the sill of the window , and coo , and arch up its neck for his finger . and he try to put his finger out , but they be ice already . whether that or something else bring home his thought , who know , miss ? but he seem to mix the pigeon up with some of his own experience . 
 " ' say that I have forgive she , if ever she do harm to I , ' he whisper , without move lip . ' Times and time , when I be young , I be not always steady ; ' and then he seem to wander in his mind among old place ; and he would have laugh at something if his voice have be sufficient . 
 " ' bitter grief and pain shall never come again , ' he seem to breathe , with a calm , soft smile , like a child with its rhyme about the rain when the sun break out ; and sure enough , the sun upon the quilt above his heart be shin , as if there could be no more cloud . then he whisper a few short word to the Lord , more in the way of thank than prayer , and his eye seem to close of their own accord , or with some good spirit soothe they . and when or how his sleep pass from this world into the other there be scarcely the flutter of a nerve to show . there he lie , like an image of happiness . will you come and see he ? " 
 I follow she to the bedroom , and be very glad that I do so ; for it show I the bliss of a good man 's rest , and take away my fear of death . 




 CHAPTER LI 

 LIFE sinister 

 when business and the little care of earthly life awake again , every one tell I   to my great surprise and no small terror at first , but soon to increase acquiescence   that I be now the mistress of the fair estate of Castlewood , and , the male line be extinct , might claim the barony , if so please I ; for that , upon default of male heir , descend by the spindle . and as to the property , with or without any will of the late Lord Castlewood , the great part would descend to I under unbarred settlement , which he be not know to have meddle with . on the contrary , he confirm by his last will the settlement which they tell I be quite needless and leave I all that he have to leave , except about a thousand pound distribute in legacy . a private letter to I be seal up with his will , which , of course , it would not behoove I to make public . but thus much since our family history be , alas ! so notorious in duty to he I should declare . he beg I , if his poor lose wife of whom he have never speak to I should re - appear and need it , to pay she a certain yearly sum , which I think a great deal too much for she , but resolve to obey he exactly . 
 neither the will nor the letter contain any reference to my grandfather , or the possibility of an adverse claim . I could not , however , be quit of deep uneasiness and anxiety , but stanchly determined that every acre should vanish in fold of " the long robe " rather than pass to a crafty villain who have rob I of all my kindre . my hatred of that man deepen vastly , as he become less abstract , while my terror decrease in proportion . I begin to think that , instead of be the reckless fiend I have take he for , he be only a low , plotting , cold - blooded rogue , without even courage to save he . by this time he must have hear all about I , my pursuit of he , and my presence here then why not come and shoot I , just as he shoot my grandfather ? 
 the idea of this be unwelcome ; still , I feel no sort of gratitude , but rather a lofty contempt toward he for not have spirit to try it . in Shoxford church - yard he have express   if Sexton Rigg be not then deceive   an unholy wish to have I there , at the foot of my brother and sister . also he have try to get hold of I doubtless with a view to my quietude when I be too young to defend myself , and leave at haphazard in a lawless land . what be the reason , if his mind be still the same , for cease to follow I now ? be I to be treat with contempt as one who have try she good and could do nothing , as a feeble creature whose movement be not even worth inquiry ? anger at such an idea begin to supersede fear , as my spirit return . 
 meanwhile Major Hockin be make no sign as to what have befall he in Paris , or what Cosmopolitan Jack be about . but , strangely enough , he have send I a letter from Bruntsea instead of Paris , and address in grand style to no less a person than " the right honorable Baroness Castlewood " a title which I have resolve , for the present , neither to claim nor acknowledge . in that letter the Major mingle a pennyweight of condolence with more congratulation than the post could carry for the large stamp yet invent . his habit of mind be to magnify thing ; and he magnify my small grandeur , and seem to think nothing else worthy of mention . 
 through love of the good kind cousin I have lose , even more than through common and comely respect toward the late head of the family , I feel it impossible to proceed , for the present , with any inquiry , but leave the next move to the other side . and the other side make it , in a manner such as I never even dream of . 
 about three week after I became , in that sad way , the mistress , escape one day from lawyer and agent , who hold I in dreary interview , with long computation of this and of that , and formalitie almost endless , I go , for a breath of good earnest fresh air , beyond precinct of garden or shrubbery . to I these seem in mild weather to temper and humanize the wind too strictly , and take the wild spirit out of it ; and now , for the turn of the moment , no wind could be too rough to tumble in . after long month of hard trouble , and worry , and fear , and sad shame , and deep sorrow , the natural spring of clear youth into air and freedom set I upward . for the nonce there be nothing upon my selfish self to keep it downward ; trouble be bubble , and grief a low thief , and reason almost treason . I drink the fine fountain of air unsullie , and the golden light stamp with the royalty of sun . 
 hilarious moment be but short , and soon cold sense come back again . already I begin to feel ashamed of young life 's selfish outburst , and the vehement spring of mere bodily health . on this account I sit down sadly in a little cove of hill , whereto the soft breeze from the river come up , with a tone of wavelet , and a sprightly water - gleam . and here , in fern and yellow grass and tufte bight of bottom growth , the wind make entry for the sun , and they play with one another . 
 Besting here , and thinking , with my face between my hand , I wonder what would be the end . nothing seem secure or certain , nothing even steady or amenable to foresight . even guess - work or the wide cast of dream be always wrong . to - day the hill and valley , and the glorious wood of wreathen gold , bright garnet , and deep amethyst , even that blue river yet unvexed by autumn 's turbulence , and border with green pasture of a thousand sheep and cattle to - day they all be mine   so far as mortal can hold ownership   to - morrow , not a stick , or twig , or blade of grass , or fall leaf , but might call I a trespasser . to see they while they still be mine , and to regard they humbly , I rise and take my black hat off a black hat trim with mourn gray . then turn round , I meet a gaze , the wild , dark , and most awful ever fix on human face . 
 " who be you ? what do you want here ? " I falter forth , while shrink back for flight , yet dread or unable to withdraw my gaze from his . the hollow ground bar all escape ; my own land be a pit for I , and I must face this horror out . here , afar from house or refuge , hand of help , or eye of witness , front to front I must encounter this atrocious murderer . 
 for moment , which be age to I , he stand there without a word ; and dare not to take my eye from his , lest he should leap at I , I have no power   except of instinct , and could form no thought of he , for mortal fear fall over I . if he would only speak , would only move his lip , or any thing ! 
 " the Baroness be not brave , " he say at last , as if reproachfully ; " but she need have no fear now of I . do her ladyship happen to know who I be ? " 
 " the man who murder my grandfather . " 
 " yes , if you put a false color on event . the man who punish a miscreant , accord to the truer light . but I be not here to argue point . I intend to propose a bargain . once for all , I will not harm you . try to listen calmly . your father behave like a man to I , and I will be no bad to you . the state of the law in this country be such that I be force to carry fire - arm . will it conduce to your peace of mind if I place myself at your mercy ? " 
 I try to answer ; but my heart be beat so that no voice come , only a flutter in my trembling throat . wrath with myself for want of courage wrestle in vain with pale , abject fear . the hand which offer I the pistol seem to my daze eye crimson still with the blood of my grandfather . 
 " you will not take it ? very well ; it lie here at your service . if your father 's daughter like to shoot I , from one point of view it will be just ; and but for one reason , I care not . do not   look at I with pity , if you please . for what I have do I feel no remorse , no shadow of repentance . it be the good action of my life . but time will fail , unless you call upon your courage speedily . none of your family lack that ; and I know that you possess it . call your spirit up , my dear . " 
 " oh , please not to call I that ! how dare you call I that ? " 
 " that be right . I do it on purpose . and yet I be your uncle . not by the law of man , but by the law of God if there be such thing . now , have you the strength to hear I ? " 
 " yes ; I be quite recover now . I can follow every word you say . but but I must sit down again . " 
 " certainly . sit there , and I will stand . I will not touch or come near to you than a story such as mine require . you know your own side of it ; now hear mine . 
 " More than fifty year ago there be a brave young nobleman , handsome , rich , accomplished , strong , not give to drink or gambling , or any fashionable vice . his fault be few , and chiefly three he have a headstrong will , love money , and possess no heart at all . with chance in his favor , this man might have do as most man do who have such gift from fortune . but he happen to meet with a maiden far beneath he in this noble world , and he set his affection such as they be upon that poor young damsel . 
 " this be Winifred Hoyle , the daughter of Thomas Hoyle , a farmer , in a lonely part of Hampshire , and among the moor of Rambledon . the nobleman lose his way , while fish , and be thirsty , go to ask for milk . what matter how it come about ? he manage to win her heart before she hear of his rank and title . he persuade she even to come and meet he in the valley far from her father 's house , where he be will not to angle ; and there , on a lonely wooden bridge across a little river , he kneel down   as man use to do   and pledge his solemn truth to she . his solemn lie his solemn lie ! 
 " such love as his could not overleap the bar of rank or the pale of wealth be you listen to I carefully ? or , at any rate , not both of they . if the poor farmer could only have give his winifred 50,000 pound , the peer would have drop his pride , perhaps , so far as to be honest . but farmer in that land be poor , and Mr. Hoyle could give his only child his blessing only . and this he do in London , where his simple mind be all abroad , and he know not church from chapel . he take his daughter for the wife of a lord , and so she take herself , poor thing ! when she be but his concubine . in 1809 such trick be easily play by villain upon young girl so simple . 
 " but he give her attestation and certificate under his own hand ; and her poor father sign it , and see it secure in a costly case , and then go home as proud as need be for the father of a peer , but swear to keep it three year secret , till the king should give consent . such foul lie it be the pride of a lord to tell to a farmer . 
 " you do not exclaim of course you do not . the instinct of your race be in you , because you be legitimate . those of the rob side be in I , because I be of the robbed . I be your father 's eld brother . which be the bad , you proud young womam , the dastard or the bastard ? " 
 " you have wrong , most bitter wrong , " I answer , meet fierce eye mildly ; " but you should remember that I be guiltless of those wrong , and so be my father . and I think that if you talk of birth so , you must know that gentleman speak quietly to lady . " 
 " what concern be that of mine ? a gentleman be some one 's son . I be the son of nobody . but to you I will speak quietly , for the sake of your poor father . and you must listen quietly . I be not famous for sweet temper . well , this great lord take his toy to Paris , where he have she at his mercy . she could not speak a word of French ; she do not know a single soul . in vain she pray he to take she to his english home ; or , if not that , to restore she to her father . not to be too long about it any more than he be a few month be enough for he . he find fault with her manner , with her speech , her dress , she every thing all which he have right , perhaps , to do , but should have use it early . and she , although not bear to the noble privilege of weariness , have be an old man 's darling , and could not put up with harshness . from word they come to bad , until he strike she , tell she of her shame , or rather his own infamy , and leave she among stranger , helpless , penniless , and brokenhearte , to endure the consequence . 
 " there and thus I see the light beneath most noble auspex . but I need not go on with all that . as long as human rule remain , this happy tale will always be repeat with immense applause . my mother 's love be turn to bitter hatred of his lordship , and , when her father die from grief , to eager thirst for vengeance . and for this purpose I be bear . 
 " you see that for a bastard I have be fairly educate ; but not a farthing do his lordship ever pay for that , or even to support his casual . my grandfather Hoyle leave his little all to his daughter Winifred ; and upon that , and my mother 's toil and mine , we have keep alive . lose sight of my mother gladly for she be full of pride , and hop no more to trouble he , after get her father 's property he marry again , or rather he marry for the first time without perjury , which enable the man to escape from it . she be of his own rank as you know the daughter of an earl , and not of a farmer . it would not have be safe to mock she , would it ? and there be no temptation . 
 " the history of my mother and myself do not concern you . such people be of no account until they grow dangerous to the great . we live in cheap place and wander about , care for no one , and care for by the same . Mrs. Hoyle and Thomas Hoyle we call ourselves when we want name ; and I do not even know the story of our wrong till the heat and fury of youth be past . both for her own sake and mine my mother conceal it from I . pride and habit , perhaps , have dull she just desire for vengeance ; and , know what I be , she fear the thing which have befall I . but when I be close upon thirty year old , and my mother eight - and - forty for she be betray in her teen a sudden illness seize she . believe her death to be near , she tell I , as calmly as possible , every thing , with all those large , quiet view of the past , which at such a time seem the regular thing , but make the wrong tenfold blacker . she do not die ; if she have , it might have be well both for she and I , and many other people . be you tired of my tale ? or do you want to hear the rest ? " 
 " you can not be ask I in earnest , " I reply , while I watch his wild eye carefully . " tell I the rest , if you be not afraid . " 
 " Afraid , indeed ! then , for want of that proper tendance and comfort which a few pound would have bring she , although she survive , she survive as a wreck , the mere relic and ruin of her poor unhappy self . I sink my pride for her sake , and even deign to write to he , in rank and wealth so far above I , in every thing else such a clot below my heel . he do the most arrogant thing a snob can do he never answer my letter . 
 " I scrap together a little money , and make my way to England , and come to that house which you now call yours and beard that noble nobleman that father to be so proud of ! he be get on now in year , and grow , perhaps , a little nervous , and my first appearance scar he . he get no obeisance from I , you may be certain , but still I do not revile he . I tell he of my mother 's state of mind , and the great care she require , and demand that , in common justice , he , have bring she to this , should help she . but nothing would he promise , not a sixpence even , in the way of regular allowance . any thing of that sort could only be arrange by mean of his solicitor . he have so expensive a son , with a very large and grow family , that he could not be pledge to any yearly sum . but if I would take a draft for 100 pound , and sign an acquittance in full of all claim , I might have it , upon prove my identity . 
 " what identity have I to prove ? he have take good care of that . I turn my back on he and leave the house , without even ask for his curse , though as precious as a good man 's blessing . 
 " it be a wild and windy night , but with a bright moon rise , and go across this park or whatever it be call I meet my brother . at a crest of the road we meet face to face , with the moon across our forehead . we have never meet till now , nor even hear of one another ; at least he have never hear of I . he start back as if at his own ghost ; but I have nothing to be startle at , in this world or the other . 
 " I make his acquaintance , with deference , of course , and we get on very well together . at one time it seem good luck for he to have illegitimate kindre ; for I save his life when he be tangle in the weed of this river while bath . you owe I no thank . I think twice about it , and if the name would have end with he , I would never have use my basket - knife . by trade I be a basket - maker , like many another ' love - child . ' 
 " however , he be grateful , if ever any body be , for I run some risk in do it ; and he always do his very good for I , and encourage I to visit he . not at his home of course that would never do but when he be with his regiment . short of money as he always be , through his father 's nature and his own , which in some point be the very opposite , he be even desirous to give I some of that ; but I never take a farthing from he . if I have it at all , I would have it from the proper one . and from he I resolve to have it . 
 " how terrified you look ! I be come to it now . be you sure that you can bear it ? it be nothing very harrowing ; but still , young lady " 
 " I feel a little faint , " I could not help say ; " but that be nothing . I must hear the whole of it . please to go on without mind I . " 
 " for my own sake I will not , as well as for your . I can not have you faint , and bring people here . go to the house and take food , and recover your strength , and then come here again . I promise to be here , and your father 's daughter will not take advantage of my kindness . " 
 though his eye be fierce   instead of be sad   and full of strange tempestuous light , they bear some likeness to my father 's , and assert power over I . reluctant as I be , I obey this man , and leave he there , and go slowly to the house , walk as if in a troubled dream . 




 CHAPTER LII 

 for life , DEATH 

 upon my return , I see nothing for a time but fan and feather of brown fern , dark shag of ling , and pod spur of broom and furze , and wisps of grass . with great relief   of which I feel ashamed while even breathe it , I think that the man be afraid to tell the rest of his story , and have flee ; but ere my cowardice have much time for self - congratulation a tall figure rise from the ground , and fear compel I into courage . for throughout this long interview more and more I feel an extremely unpleasant conviction . that stranger might not be a downright madman , nor even what be call a lunatic ; but still it be clear that upon certain point the law of this country , for instance , and the value of rank and station his opinion be so outrageous that his reason must be affect . and , even without such proof as these , his eye and his manner be quite enough . therefore I have need of no small caution , not only concern my word and gesture , but as to my look and even thought , for he seem to divine these last as quickly as they flash across I . I never have learn to conceal my thought , and this first lesson be an awkward one . 
 " I hope you be well , " he say , as kindly as it be possible for he to speak . " now have no fear of I , once more I tell you . I will not sham any admiration , affection , or any thing of that kind ; but as for harm you why , your father be almost the only kind heart I ever meet ! " 
 " then why do you send a most vile man to fetch I , when my father be dead in the desert ? " 
 " I never do any thing of the sort . it be do in my name , but not by I ; I never even hear of it until long after , and I have a score to settle with the man who do it . " 
 " but Mr. Goad tell I himself that you come and say you be the true Lord Castlewood , and order he at once to America . I never see truth more plainly stamp on a new situation the face of a rogue than I see it then on the face of Mr. Goad . " 
 " you be quite right ; he speak the truth to the utmost of his knowledge . I never see Goad , and he never see I . I never even dream of pretend to the title . I be personate by a mean , low friend of Sir Montague Hockin ; base - bear as I be , I would never stoop to such a trick . you will find out the meaning of that by - and - by . I have take the law into my own hand it be the only way to work such law I have commit what be call a crime . but , compare with Sir Montague Hockin , I be white than yonder shearle on his way to the river for his evening drink . " 
 I gaze at his face , and could well believe it . the set sun shine upon his chin and forehead good , resolute , well - mark feature ; his nose and mouth be keen and clear , his cheek curt and pale   though they would have be well for be a trifle clean . there be nothing suggestive of falsehood or fraud , and but for the wildness of the eye and flash of cold ferocity , it might have be call a handsome face . 
 " very well , " he begin again , with one of those jerk which have frighten I , " your father be kind to I , very kind indeed ; but he know the old lord too well to attempt to interpose on my behalf . on the other hand , he give no warning of my manifest resolve ; perhaps he think it a woman 's threat , and I no well than a woman ! and partly for his sake , no doubt , though mainly for my mother 's , I make the short work which I make ; for he be horribly straiten and in his free , light way he tell I so by his hard curmudgeon of a father . 
 " to that man , hopeless as he be , I give fair grace , however , and plenty of opening for repentance . none of they would he embrace , and he think scorn of my lenity . and I might have go on with such weakness long , if I have not hear that his coach - and - four be order for the Moonstock Inn . 
 " that he should dare thus to pollute the spot where he have so forswear himself ! I resolve that there he should pay justice , either with his life or death . and I go to your father 's place to tell he to prepare for disturbance ; but he be go to see his wife , and I simply borrow a pistol . 
 " now you need not be at all afraid nor shrink away from I like that . I be bind upon strict justice than any judge that set forth on circuit ; and I mean to give , and do give , what no judge afford to the guilty the chance of lead a well life . I have bring my mother to England , and she be in a poor place in London ; her mind be fail more and more , and revert to her love - time , the one short happiness of her life . ' if I could but see he , if I could but see he , and show he his tall and clever son , he would forgive I all my sin in think ever to be his wife . oh , Thomas ! I be too young to know it . if I could but see he once , just once ! ' 
 " how all this drive I no tongue can tell . but I never let she know it ; I only say , ' Mother , he shall come and see you if he ever see any body more ! ' and she trust I and be satisfied . she only say , ' take my picture , Thomas , to remind he of the happy time , and his pledge to I inside of it . ' and she give I what she have keep for year in a bag of chamois leather , the case of which I speak before , which even in our hard time she would never send to the pawn - shop . 
 " the rest be simple enough . I swear by the God , or the Devil , who make I , that this black - hearted man should yield either his arrogance or his life . I follow he to the Moon valley , and fate ordain that I should meet he where he forswear himself to my mother ; on that very plank where he have breathe his deadly lie he breathe his last . would you like to hear all about it ? " 
 for answer I only bow my head . his calm , methodical way of tell his tale , like a common adventure with a dog , be more shocking than any fury . 
 " then it be this . I watch he from the Moonstock Inn to a house in the village , where he din with company ; and I do not even know that it be the house of his son , your father so great a gulf be fix between the legitimate and the bastard ! he have cross the wooden bridge in go , and be sure to cross it in come back . how he could tread those plank without contrition and horror but never mind . I resolve to bring he to a quiet parley there , and I wait in the valley . 
 " the night be soft , and dark in patch where the land or wood close in ; and the stream be brown and throw no light , though the moon be on the upland . time and place alike be fit for our little explanation . the path wind down the meadow toward I , and I know that he must come . my firm intention be to spare he , if he give I a chance of it ; but he never have the manner to do that . 
 " here I wait , with the cold leaf flutter around I , until I hear a firm , slow step come down the narrow path . then a figure appear in a stripe of moonlight , and stop , and rest on a staff . perhaps his lordship 's mind go back some five - and - thirty year , to time when he tell pretty story here ; and perhaps he laugh to himself to think how well he have get out of it . whatever his meditation be , I let he have they out , and wait . 
 " if he have even sigh , I might have feel more kindness toward he ; but he only give something between a cough and a grunt , and I clearly hear he say , ' gout to - morrow morning ! what the devil do I drink port - wine for ! ' he strike the ground with his stick and come onward , think far more of his foot than heart . 
 " then , as he plant one foot gingerly on the timber and stay himself , I leap along the bridge and meet he , and without a word look at he . the moon be top the crest of the hill and throw my shadow upon he , the last that ever fall upon his body to its knowledge . 
 " ' Fellow , out of the way ! ' he cry , with a most commanding voice and air , though only too well he know I ; and my wrath against he begin to rise . 
 " ' you pass not here , and you never make another live step on this earth , ' I say , as calmly as now I speak , ' unless you obey my order . ' 
 " he see his peril , but he have courage perhaps his only virtue . ' Fool ! whoever you be , ' he shout , that his voice might fetch he help ; ' none of these moon - strike way with I ! if you want to rob I , try it ! ' 
 " ' you know too well who I be , ' I answer , as he make to push I back . ' Lord Castlewood , here you have the choice to lick the dust , or be dust ! here you forswore yourself ; here you pay for perjury . on this plank you kneel to poor Winifred Hoyle , whom you ruin and cast by ; and now on this plank you shall kneel to her son and swear to obey he or else you die ! ' 
 " in spite of all his pride , he tremble as if I have be Death himself , instead of his own dear eld son . 
 " ' what do you want ! ' as he ask , he lay one hand on the rickety rail and shake it , and the dark old tree behind he shake . ' how much will satisfy you ? ' 
 " ' Miser , none of your money for we ! it be too late for your half crown ! we must have a little of what you have grudge have none to spare your honor . my demand be simple , and only two . my mother be fool enough to yearn for one more sight of your false face ; you will come with I and see she . ' 
 " ' and if I yield to that , what next ? ' 
 " ' the next thing be a trifle to a nobleman like you . here I have , in this blue trinket   false gem and false gold , of course , your solemn signature to a lie . at the foot of that you will have the truth to write , " I be a perjured liar ! " and proudly sign it " Castlewood , " in the presence of two witness . this can not hurt your feeling much , and it need not be expensive . ' 
 " fury flash in his bright old eye , but he strove to check its outbreak . the gleaning of life , after threescore year , be well , in such lordly field , than the whole of the harvest we get . he know that I have he all to myself , to indulge my filial affection . 
 " ' you have be mislead ; you have never hear the truth ; you have only hear your mother 's story . allow I to go back and to sit in a dry place ; I be tired , and no long young ; you be bind to hear my tale as well . I pass a dry stump just now ; I will go back : there be no fear of interruption . ' my lord be talk against time . 
 " ' from this bridge you do not budge until you have go on your knee and swear what I shall dictate to you ; this time it shall be no perjury . here I hold your curse pledge ' 
 " he strike at I , or at the locket no matter which but it fly away . my right arm be cripple by his heavy stick ; but I be leave - handed , as a bastard should be . from my left hand he take his death , and I throw the pistol after he : such love have he earn from his love - child ! "
