 Thomas Castlewood , or Hoyle , or whatever else his name be , here break off from his miserable word , and , forget all about my presence , set his gloomy eye on the ground . lightly he might try to speak , but there be no lightness in his mind , and no spark of light in his poor dead soul . be so young , and unacquainted with the turn of life - wear mind , I be afraid to say a word except to myself , and to myself I only say , " the man be mad , poor fellow ; and no wonder ! " 
 the sun be set , not upon the vast Pacific from desert height , but over the quiet hill and through the soft valley of tame England ; and , different as the whole scene be , a certain other sad and fearful sunset lie before I : the fall of night upon my die father and his helpless child , the hour of anguish and despair ! here at last be the cause of all lay horribly before I ; and the pity deeply move I pass into cold abhorrence . but the man be lose in his own vision . 
 " so in your savage wrath , " I say , " you kill your own father , and in your fright leave mine to bear the brunt of it . " 
 he raise his dark eye heavily , and his thought be far astray from mine . he do not know what I have say , though he know that I have speak . the labor of call to mind and tell his treatment of his father have work upon he so much that he could not freely shift attention . 
 " I come for something , something that can be only have from you , " he say , " and only since your cousin 's death , and something most important . but will you believe I ? it be wholly go , go from mind and memory ! " 
 " I be not surprised at that , " I answer , look at his large wan face , and while I do so , lose half my horror in strange sadness . " whatever it be , I will do it for you ; only let I know by post . " 
 " I see what you mean not to come any more . you be right about that , for certain . but your father be good to I , and I love he , though I have no right to love any one . my letter will show that I wrong he never . the weight of the world be off my mind since I have tell you every thing ; you can send I to the gallow , if you think fit , but leave it till my mother die . good - by , poor child . I have spoil your life , but only by chance consequence , not in murder - birth as I be bear . " 
 before I could answer or call he back , if I even wish to do so , he be far away , with his long , quiet stride ; and , like his life , his shadow fall , chilling , sombre , cast away . 




 CHAPTER LIII 

 BRUNTSEA DEFIANT 

 thus at last by no direct exertion of my own , but by turn after turn of thing to which I blindly give my little help the mystery of my life be solve . many thing yet remain to be fetch up to focus and see round ; but the point of point be settle . 
 of all concern , my father alone stand blameless and heroic . what tear of shame and pride I shed , for ever have doubt he ! not doubt his innocence of the crime itself , but his motif for take it upon he . I have be mean enough to dream that my dear father outraged justice to conceal his own base birth ! 
 that ever such thought should have enter my mind may not make I charitable to the wicked thought of the world at large , but , at any rate , it ought to do so . and the man in question , my own father , who have starve himself to save I ! well have I be the most illegal child ever issue into this cold world , than dare to think so of my father , and then find he the model of every thing . 
 to hide the perjury , avarice , and cowardice of his father , and to appease the bitter wrong , he have even bow to take the dark suspicion on himself , until his wronged and half - sane brother   to whom , moreover , he owe his life   should have time to fly from England . no doubt he blame himself as much as he condemn the wretched criminal , because he have leave his father so long unwarned and so unguarded , and have thoughtlessly use light word about he , which fall not lightly on a stern , distempered mind . hence , perhaps , the exclamation which have tell against he so . 
 and then when he break jail which also tell against he terribly to revisit his shattered home , it be likely enough that he mean after that to declare the truth , and stand his trial as a man should do . but his wife , perhaps , in her poor weak state , could not endure the thought of it , know how often jury be injury , and see all the weight against he . she naturally pledge he to pursue his flight , " for her sake , " until she should be well able to endure his trial , and until he should have more than his own pure word and character to show . and probably if he have then be try , with so many thing against he , and no production of that poor brother , his tale would have seem but a flimsy invention , and " guilty " would have be the verdict . and they could not know that , in such case , the guilty man would have come forward , as we shall see that he mean to do . 
 when my father hear of his dear wife 's death , and believe , no doubt , that I be bury with the rest , the gloom of a broken and fated man , like polar night , settle down on he . what matter to he about public opinion or any thing else in the world just now ? the sin of his father be on his head ; let they rest there , rather than be trumpet by he . he have nothing to care for ; let he wander about . and so he do for several year , until I become a treasure to he for parental be not intrinsic value and then , for my sake , as now appear , he betake we both to a large kind land . 
 revolve these thing sadly , and a great many more which need not be tell , I think it my duty to go as soon as possible to Bruntsea , and tell my good and faithful friend what I be loath to write about . there , moreover , I could obtain what I want to confirm I the opinion of an upright , law - abide , honorable man about the course I propose to take . and there I might hear something more as to a thing which have trouble I much in the deep of my own trouble the melancholy plight of dear Uncle Sam . Wild , and absurd as it may appear to people of no gratitude , my heart be set upon fare forth in search of the noble Sawyer , if only it could be reconcile with my duty here in England . that such a proceeding would avail but little , seem now , alas ! too manifest ; but a plea of that kind generally mean that we have no mind to do a thing . 
 be that as it will , I make what my dear Yankees to use the Major 's impertinent phrase call ' straight track " for that ancient and obsolete town , rejuvenize now by its Signor . the cause of my good friend 's silence not to use that affected word " reticence " be quite unknown to I , and disturb my spirit with futile guess . 
 Resolute , therefore , to pierce the bottom of every survive mystery , I make claim upon " Mr. Stixon , junior " as " Stixon 's boy " have now vindicate his right to be call , up to supper - time and he with high chivalry respond . not yet be he wed to Miss Polly Hopkins , the daughter of the pickle - pork man ; otherwise would he or could he have make telegraphic blush at the word " Bruntsea ? " and would he have be quite so eager to come ? 
 such thing be trifle , compare to our own , which naturally fill the universe . I be bind to be a great lady now , and patronize and regulate and drill all the doing of nature . so I durst not even ask , though desire much to do so , how young Mr. Stixon be get on with his delightful polly . and his father , as soon as he find I turn into the mistress , and " his lady "   as he would have I call thenceforth , whether or no on my part , not another word would he tell I of the household sentiment , politic , or romance . it would have be think a thing beneath I to put any nice little question now , and I be oblige to take up the tone which other use toward I . but all the while I long for freedom , Uncle Sam , Suan Isco , and even Martin of the Mill . 
 Law business , however , and other hinderance , keep I from start at once for Bruntsea , impatient as I be to do so . indeed , it be not until the morning of the last Saturday in November that I be able to get away . the weather have turn to much rain , I remember , with two or three tempestuous night , and the wood be almost bare of leaf , and the Thames look brown and violent . 
 in the fly from Newport to Bruntsea I hear great roller thunder heavily upon the steep bar of shingle , and such a lake of water shine in the old bed of the river that I quite believe at first that the Major have carry out his grand idea , and bring the river back again . but the flyman shake his head , and look very serious , and tell I that he fear bad time be come . what I see be the work of the Lord in heaven , and no man could prevail against it . he have always say , though no concern of his for he belong to Newport that even a british officer could not fly in the face of the Almighty . he himself have a brother on the work , regular employ , and draw good money , and proud enough about it ; and the time he have tell he across a pint of ale howsomever , our place be to hope for the good ; but the top of the spring be not come yet , and a pilot out of Newport tell he the water be make uncommon strong ; but he do hope the wind have nigh blow itself out ; if not , they would have to look bless sharp tomorrow . he have hear say that in time of Queen Elizabeth sixscore of house be wash clean away , and the river itself knock right into the sea ; and a thing as have be once might just come to pass again , though folk be all so clever now they think they wor above it . but , for all that , their grandfather ' goggle might fit they . but here we be in Bruntsea town , and , bless his old eye yes ! if I please to look along his whip , I might see ancient pilot come , he do believe , to warn of they ! 
 follow his guidance , I descry a stout old man , in a sailor 's dress , weather - proof hat , and long boot , stand on a low seawall , and hold vehement converse with some Bruntsea boatman and fisherman who be sprawl on the stone as usual . 
 " Driver , you know he . take the low road , " I say , " and ask what his opinion be . " 
 " no need to ask he , " the flyman answer ; " old bank would never be here , miss , if he be of two opinion . he hath come to fetch his daughter out of harm , I doubt , the wife of that there Bishop Jim , they call he the chap with two nail to his thumb , you know . would you like to hear how they all take it , miss ? " 
 with these word he turn to the right , and drive into Major Hockin 's " Sea Parade . " there we stop to hear what be go on , and it prove to be well worth our attention . the old pilot perhaps have exhausted reason , and now be begin to give way to wrath . the afternoon be deepen fast , with heavy gray cloud lower , show no definite edge , but streak with hazy line , and spot by some little murky blur or blot , like tar pot , carry slowly . 
 " Hath Noah 's Ark ever tell a lie ? " the ancient pilot shout , point with one hand at these , and with a clinch fist at the sea , whence come puff of sullen air , and turn his gray lock backward . " Mackerel sky when the sun get up , mermaiden 's egg at noon , and now afore sunset Noah 's Arks ! any of they breweth a gale of wind , and the three of they bode a temp . and the top of the spring of the year to - morrow . be ye daft , or all go upon the spree , my man ? your father would ' a know what the new moon mean . be this all that cometh out of larn to read ? " 
 " have a pinch of ' bacco , old man , " say one , " to help you off with that stiff reel . what consarn can he be of yourn ? " 
 " do not   you be put out , mate , " cry another . " never come sea as could top that bar , and never will in our time . go and calk your old leaky craft , Master Banks . " 
 " we have ride out a good many gale without seek prophet from Newport a place never heerd on when this old town be make . " 
 " come and wet your old whistle at the ' Hockin Arms , ' bank . you must want it , after that long pipe . " 
 " ' Hockin Arms , ' indeed ! " the pilot answer , turn away in a rage from they . " what Hockin arm will there be this time to - morrow ? Hockin leg want , more likely , and Hockin wing . and you poor grinning ninny , as ought to have four leg , ye'll be pray that ye have they to - morrow . however , ye've   have warning , and ye can not   blame I . the power of the Lord be in the air and sea . be this the sort of stuff ye trust in ? " 
 he set one foot against our Major 's wall an action scarcely honest while it be so green and , come from a hale and very thickset man , the contemptuous push send a fathom of it outward . rattle , rattle go the new patent concrete , start up the lazy - pat fellow down below . 
 " you will try the wall of a jail , " cry one . " you go to Noah 's Ark , " shout another . the rest bid he go to a place much bad ; but he button his jacket in disdain , and march away , without spoil the effect by any more weak word . 
 " right you be , " cry my flyman " right you be , Master Banks . they lubber will sing another song to - morrow . Gee up , old hoss , then ! " 
 all this , and the ominous scowl of the sky and menacing roar of the sea   already crowd with black roller , disturb I so that I could say nothing , until , at the corner of the grand new hotel , we meet Major Hockin himself , attire in a workman 's loose jacket , and carry a shovel . he be cover with mud and dry flake of froth , and even his short white whisker be incrust with sparkle of brine ; but his face be ruddy and smile , and his manner as hearty as ever . 
 " you here , Erema ! oh , I beg pardon Baroness Castlewood , if you please . my dear , again I congratulate you . " 
 " you have as little cause to do that as I fear I can find in your case . you have no news for I from America ? how sad ! but what a poor plight you yourself be in ! " 
 " not a bit of it . at first sight you might think so ; and we certainly have have a very busy time . send back the fly . leave your bag at our hotel . Porter , be quick with Lady Castlewood 's luggage . one piece of luck befall I to receive so often this beautiful hand . what a lot of young fellow now would die of envy " 
 " I be glad that you still can talk nonsense , " I say ; " for I truly be frighten at this great lake , and so many of your house even stand in the water . " 
 " it will do they good . it will settle the foundation and crystallize the mortar . they will look twice as well when they come out again , and never have rat or black beetle . we be foolish enough to be frighten at first ; and there may have be danger a fortnight ago . but since that tide we have work day and night , and every thing be now so stable that fear be simply ridiculous . on the whole , it have be a most excellent thing quite the making , in fact , of Bruntsea . " 
 " then Bruntsea must be make of water , " I reply , gaze sadly at the gulf which part we from the Sea Parade , the Lyceum , and Baths , the Bastion Promenade , and so on ; beyond all which the streaky turmoil and misty scud of the wave be see . 
 " make of beer , more likely , " he retort , with a laugh . " if my fellow work like horse which they do they also drink like fish . their mouth be so dry with the pickle , they say . but the total abstainer be the bad , be out of practice with the can . however , let we make no complaint . we ought to be truly thankful ; and I shall miss the exercise . that be why you have hear so little from I . you see the position at a glance . I have never be to Paris at all , Erema . I have not rub up my parleywoo , with a blast from Mr. Bellows . I be stop by a telegram about this job acrior illum . I have some Latin once , quite enough for the House of Commons , but it all ooze out at my elbow ; and to lady   by some superstition   it be rude though they treat we to bad french enough . never mind . what I want to say be this , that I have do nothing , but respect your sad trouble ; for you take a wild fancy to that poor bedridden , who never do you a stroke of good except about Cosmopolitan Jack , and whose removal have come at the very nick of time . for what could you have do for money , with the Yankees cut each other 's throat , and your nugget quite sure to be annex , or , at the very good , square up in greenback ? " 
 " you ought not to speak so , Major Hockin . if all your plan be not under water , I should be quite put out with you . my cousin be not bedridden ; neither be he at all incapable , as you have call he once or twice . he be an infinitely superior man to to what one generally see ; and when you have hear what I have to tell , in his place you would have do just as he do . and as for money , and ' happy release ' as the people who never want it for themselves express it such word simply sicken I ; at great time they be so sordid . " 
 " what be there in this world that be not sordid to the young in one sense , and to the old in another ? " 
 Major Hockin so seldom speak in this didactic way , and I be so unable to make it out , that , have expect some tiff on his part at my juvenile arrogance , I be just in the mould for a deep impression from sudden stamp of philosophy . I have nothing to say in reply , and he go up in my opinion greatly . 
 he know it ; and he say , with touching kindness , " Erema , come and see your dear aunt Mary . she have have an attack of rheumatic gout in her thimble - finger , and her maid have worry she out of her life , and by far the most brilliant of her cock   worth 20 pound they tell I   breathe his last on Sunday night , with gape , or croup , or something . this be why you have not hear again from she . I have be in the trench day and night , stone out the sea with his own stone , by a new form of concrete discover by myself . and unless I be very much mistaken in fact , I do not hesitate to say but such thing be not in your line at all . let we go up to the house . our job be do , and I think Master Neptune may pound away in vain . I have get a new range in the kitchen now , partly of my own invention ; you can roast , or bake , or steam , or stew , or frizzle kabob all by turn a screw . and not only that , but you can keep thing hot , pip hot , and ripen , as it be , well than when they first be do . instead of any burned iron taste , or scum on the gravy , or clottiness , they mellow by wait , and make their own sauce . if I ever have time I shall patent this invention ; why , you may burn brick - dust in it , bath - brick , hearth - stone , or potsherd ! at any hour of the day or night , while the sea be in this condition , I may want my dinner ; and there we have it . we say grace immediately , and down we sit . let we take it by surprise , if it can be take so . up through my chief drive , instanter ! I think that I scarcely ever feel more hungry . the thought of that range always set I off . and one of its countless beauty be the noble juicy fragrance . " 
 Major Hockin certainly possess the art so meritorious in a host of make people hungry ; and we mount the hill with alacrity , after pass his letter - box , which remind I of the mysterious lady . he point to " Desolate Hole , " as he call it , and say that he believe she be there still , though she never come out now to watch their house . and a man of dark and repel aspect have be see once or twice by his workman , during the time of their night relay , rapidly walk toward Desolate Hole . how any one could live in such a place , with the roar and the spray of the sea , as it have be , at the very door , and through the window , some people might understand , but not the Major . 
 Good Mrs. Hockin receive I with her usual warmth and kindness , and scold I for have fail to write more to she , as all people seem to do when conscious of have neglect that duty themselves . then she show I her thimble - finger , which certainly be a little swollen ; and then she pour forth her gratitude for her many blessing , as she always do after any little piece of grumble . and I tell she that if at her age I be only a quarter as pleasant and sweet of temper , I should consider myself a blessing to any man . 
 after dinner my host produce the locket , which he have keep for the purpose of show it to the artist 's son in Paris , and which he admire so intensely that I wish it be mine to bestow on he . then I tell he that , through a thing wholly unexpected the confession of the criminal himself no journey to Paris be needful now . I repeat that strange and gloomy tale , to the loud accompaniment of a rise wind and roar sea , while both my friend listen intently . 
 " now what can have lead he so to come to you ? " they ask ; " and what do you mean to do about it ? " 
 " he come to I , no doubt , to propose some bargain , which could not be make in my cousin 's lifetime . but the telling of his tale make he feel so strange that he really could not remember what it be . as to what I be to do , I must beg for your opinion ; such a case be beyond my decision . " Mrs. Hockin begin to reply , but stop , look dutifully at her lord . 
 " there be no doubt what you be bind to do , at least in one way , " the Major say . " you be a british subject , I suppose , and you must obey the law of the country . a man have confess to you a murder no matter whether it be commit twenty year ago or two minute ; no matter whether it be a savage , cold - blooded , premeditated crime , or whether there be thing to palliate it . your course be the same ; you must hand he over . in fact , you ought never to have let he go . " 
 " how could I help it ? " I plead , with surprise . " it be impossible for I to hold he . " 
 " then you should have shoot he with his own pistol . he offer it to you . you should have grasp it , point it at his heart , and tell he that he be a dead man if he stir . " 
 " Aunt Mary , would you have do that ? " I ask . " it be so easy to talk of fine thing ! but in the first place , I have no wish to stop he ; and in the next , I could not if I have . " 
 " my dear , " Mrs. Hockin reply , perceive my distress at this view of the subject , " I should have do exactly what you do . if the law of this country ordain that woman be to carry they out against great strong man , who , after all , have be sadly injure , why , it prove that woman ought to make the law , which to my mind be simply ridiculous . " 




 CHAPTER LIV 

 BRUNTSEA DEFEATED 

 little sleep have I that night . such conflict be in my mind about the proper thing to be do next , and such a war of the wind outside , above and between the distant uproar of the long tumultuous sea . of that sound much be intercept by the dead bulk of the cliff , but the wind swing fiercely over this , and rattle through all shelter . in the morning the storm be furious ; but the Major declare that his weather - glass have turn , which prove that the gale be break . the top of the tide would be at one o'clock , and after church we should behold a sight he be rather proud of the impotent wrath of the wind and tide against his patent concrete . 
 " my dear , I scarcely like such talk , " Mrs. Hockin gently interpose . " to I it seem almost defiant of the power of the Lord . remember what happen to poor Smeaton at least I think his name be Smeaton , or Stanley , be it ? but I dare say you know well . he defy the strength of the Lord , like the people at the mouth of their tent , and he be swallow up . " 
 " Mary , my dear , get your prayer - book . Rasper 's fly be wait for we , and the parson have no manner . when he drop off , I present to the living ; and I be not at all sure that I shall let George have it . he be fond of procession , and all that stuff . the only procession in the Church of England be that of the lord of the manor to his pew . I will be the master in my own church . " 
 " of course , dear , of course ; so you ought to be . it always be so in my father 's parish . but you must not speak so of our poor George . he may be ' high - church , ' as they call it ; but he know what be due to his family , and he have a large one come . " 
 we set off hastily for the church , through blast of rain and buffet of wind , which threaten to overturn the cab , and the seaward window be white , as in a snowstorm , with pellet of froth , and the drift of sea - scud . I try to look out , but the blur and the dash obscure the sight of every thing . and though in this low road we be partly shelter by the pebble ridge , the driver be several time oblige to pull his poor horse up and face the wind , for fear of our be blow over . 
 that ancient church , with its red - tile spire , stand well up in the good old town , at the head of a street whose principal object now certainly be to lead to it . three hundred year ago that street have business of its own to think of , and be brave perhaps with fine man and maid at the time of the spanish Armada . its only bravery now be the good old church , and some queer gable , and a crypt   which be true to itself by be bury up to the spandrel , and one or two corner where saint use to stand , until they be pelt out of they , and where fisher - like man , in the lodge season , stand sell fish catch at Billingsgate . but to Bruntsea itself the great glory of that street be rather of hope than of memory . Bailiff Hopkins have take out three latticed window , and put in one grand one of plate - glass , with " finish " blind all varnish . and even on a Sunday morning Bruntsea want to know what ever the bailiff be at behind they . some say that he do all his pickling on a Sunday ; and by put up ' spectacle glass " he have challenge the old inhabitant to come and try his focus . 
 despite all the rattle and roar of the wind , we go on in church as usual . the vicar have a stout young curate from Durham , who could outshout any temp , with a good stone wall between they ; and the Bruntsea folk be of thick constitution than to care an old hat for the weather . whatever be ' send by the Lord " they take with a grumble , but no excitement . the clock in front of the gallery tell the time of the day as five minute to twelve , when the vicar , a pleasant old - fashioned man , pronounce his text , which he always do thrice over to make we sure of it . and then he hitch up his old black gown , and direct his gaze at the lord of the manor , to impress the whole church with authority . Major Hockin acknowledge in a proper manner this courtesy of the minister by rub up his crest , and look even more wide - awake than usual ; whereas Aunt Mary , whose kind heart long to see her own son in that pulpit , calmly settle back her shoulder , and arrange her head and eye so well as to seem at a distance in rapt attention , while have a nice little dream of her own . but suddenly all be break up . the sexton   whose license as warden of the church , and even whose duty it be to hear the sermon only fitfully , from the tower arch , where he watch the boy , and sniff the bakehouse of his own dinner   to the consternation of every body , this faithful man run up the nave , with his hand above his head , and shout , 
 " all Brownzee be awash , awash " sound it so as to rhyme with " lash " " the zea , the zea be all over we ! " 
 the clergyman in the pulpit turn and look through a window behind he , while all the congregation rise . 
 " it be too true , " the preacher cry ; " the sea be in over the bank , my friend . every man must rush to his own home . the blessing of the Lord be on you through his fearful visitation ! " 
 he have no time to say more ; and we think it very brave of he to say that , for his own house be in the low village , and there he have a wife and child sick . in half a minute the church be empty , and the street below it full of people , strive and struggle against the blast , and breast it at an incline like swimmer , but beat back ever and anon and hurl against one another , with tattered umbrella , hat go , and bonnet hang . and among they , like gull before the wind , blow dollop of spray and chunk of froth , with every now and then a slate or pantile . 
 all this be so bad that scarcely any body find power to speak , or think , or see . the Major do his very good to lead we , but could by no mean manage it . and I scream into his sound ear to pull Aunt Mary into some dry house for she could not face such buffeting and to let I fare for myself as I might . so we leave Mrs. Hockin in the bailiff 's house , though she want sadly to come with we , and on we go to behold the bad . and thus , by run the bye of the wind , and craftily hug the corner , we get to the foot of the street at last , and then could go no far . 
 for here be the very sea itself , with furious billow pant . before we roll and run a fearful surf of crested whiteness , tear by the screeching squall , and toss in clash tuft and pinnacle . and into these came , sweep over the shattered chine of shingle , gigantic surge from the outer deep , tower as they cross the bar , and comb against the sky - line , then rush onward , and drive the huddle of the ponde wave before they . 
 the tide be yet rise , and at every blow the wreck and the havoc grow bad and bad . that long sweep of brick - work , the " Grand Promenade , " bow and bulge , with wall and window knuckle in and out , like wattle ; the " Sea Parade " be a parade of sea ; and a bathing - machine wheel upward lay , like a wreck Noah 's Ark , on the top of the " Saline - Silico - Calcareous Baths . " 
 the Major stand by I , while all his construction " go by the board , " as they say at sea ; and verily every thing be at sea . I grieve for he so that it be not the spray alone that put salt drop on my cheek . and I could not bear to turn and look at his good old weather - beat face . but he be not the man to brood upon his woe in silence . he might have use nice language , perhaps , but his inner sense be manful . 
 " I do not   care a damn , " he shout , so that all the woman hear he . " I can only say I be devilish glad that I never let one of those house . " 
 there be a little band of seaman , under the shelter of a garden wall , crouch , or sitting , or stand   or whatever may be the attitude , acquire by much voyaging and experience of bad weather , which can not be solve , as to centre of gravity , even by the man who do it , and these man be so take with the Major 's manifesto , clinch at once and clarify to they by strong , short language , that they give he a loud " hurrah , " which fly on the wing of the wind over house - top . so queer and sound be english feeling that now Major Hockin become in truth what hitherto he be in title only the lord and master of Bruntsea . 
 " a boat ! a boat ! " he call out again . " we know not who be drown . the bank still break the wave ; a stout boat surely could live inside it . " 
 " yes , a boat could live well enough in this cockle , though never among they breaker , " old Barnes , the fisherman , answer , who use to take we out for whiting ; " but Lord bless your honor , all the boat be thump to piece , except yonner one , and who can get at she ? " 
 before restore his hand to their proper dwelling - place his pocket he jerk his thumb toward a long white boat , which we have not see through the blind scud . bereft of its brother , or sister for all fluctuate thing be feminine that boat survive , in virtue of stand a few foot high than the rest . but even so , and mount on the last hump of the pebble ridge , it be roll and reel with stress of the wind and the wash of wild water under it . 
 " how nobly our Lyceum stand ! " the Major shout , for any thing less than a shout be dumb . " this be the time to try institution . I be proud of my foundation . " 
 in answer to his word appear a huge brown surge , a mountain ridge , seethe backward at the crest with the spread and weight of onset . this great wave smite all other wave away , or else embody they , and gather its height against the poor wear pebble bank , and descend . a roar distinct above the universal roar proclaim it ; a crash of conflict shake the earth , and the shattered bank be swallow in a world of leap whiteness . when this wild mass dash onward into the swell flood before we , there be no sign of Lyceum leave , but stub of foundation , and a mangle roof roll over and over , like a hen - coop . 
 " well , that beat every thing I ever see , " exclaim the gallant Major . " what noble timber ! what mortise - work ! no London scamp there , my lad . but what come here ? why , the very thing we want ! barne , look alive , my man . run to your house , and get a pair of oar and a bucket . " 
 it be the boat , the last survive boat of all that hail from Bruntsea . that monstrous billow have toss it up like a school - boy 's kite , and drop it whole , with an upright keel , in the inland sea , though nearly half full of water . drive on by wind and wave , it labor heavily toward we ; and more than once it seem certain to sink as it broach to and ship sea again . but half a dozen bold fisherman rush with a rope into the short angry surf to which the poll shingle bank still act as a powerful breakwater , else all Bruntsea have collapse and they haul up the boat with a hearty cheer , and run she up straight with , " yo heave oh ! " and turn she on her side to drain , and then launch she again , with a bucket and a man to bail out the rest of the water , and a pair of heavy oar bring down by Barnes , and nobody know what other thing . 
 " naught to steer with . rudder go ! " cry one of the man , as the furious gale drive the boat , athwart the street , back again . 
 " want another oar , " say Barnes . " what a fool I be to bring only two ! " 
 " here you be ! " shout Major Hockin . " one of you help I to pull up this pole . " 
 through a shattered gate they wad into a little garden , which have be the pride of the season at Bruntsea ; and there from the ground they tear up a pole , with a board at the top nail across it , and the follow not rare legend : " lodging to let . inquire within . first floor front , and back parlor . " 
 " fust - rate thing to steer with ! would never have believe you have the sense ! " so shout Barnes a rough man , roughen by the stress of storm and fright . " get into starn - sheet if so liketh . ye know , ye may be useful . " 
 " I defy you to push off without my sanction . useful , indeed ! I be the captain of this boat . all the ground under it be mine . do you think , you set of salt radical , that I mean to let you go without I ? and all among my own house ! " 
 " look sharp , governor , if you have the pluck , then . mind , we be more like to be swamp than not . " 
 as the boat swing about , Major Hockin jump in , and so , on the spur of the moment , do I. we stagger all about with the heave and roll , and both would have fall on the plank , or out over , if we have not tumble , with opposite impetus , into the arm of each other . then a great wave burst and soak we both , and we fall into sit on a slippery seat . 
 meanwhile two man be tug at each oar , and Barnes himself steer with the sign - board ; and the head of the boat be keep against the wind and the billow from our breakwater . some of these seem resolve   though shorn of depth and height in cross   to rush all over we and drown we in the washer - woman 's dry ground . by skill and presence of mind , our captain , Barnes , foil all their violence , till we get a little shelter from the ruin of the " Young Men 's Christian Institute . " 
 " hold all ! " cry Barnes ; " only keep her head up , while I look about what there be to do . " 
 the sight be a thing to remember ; and be on the well side now of the scud , because it be fly away from we , we could make out a great deal more of the trouble which have befall Bruntsea . the stormy fiord which have usurp the ancient track of the river be about a furlong in width , and troughe with white wave vault over . and the sea rush through at the bottom as well , through score of yard of pebble , as it do in quiet weather even , when the tide be brim . we in the tossing boat , with her head to the inrush of the outer sea , be just like people sit upon the float or raft of a furious weir ; and if any such surge have top the ridge as the one which fling our boat to we , there could be no doubt that we must go down as badly as the Major 's house . however , we hop for the good , and gaze at the desolation inland . 
 not only the Major 's great plan , but all the low line of old Bruntsea , be knock to piece , and lose to knowledge in freak of wind - lash water . man and woman be run about with favorite bit of furniture , or feather - bed , or baby ' cradle , or whatever they have catch hold of . the butt end of the three old street that lead down toward the sea - ground be dip , as if play seesaw in the surf , and the storm make gangway of they and lighthouse of the lamp - post . the old public - house at the corner be down , and the wave leap in at the post - office door , and wreck the globe of the chemist . 
 " Drift and dash , and roar and rush , and the devil let loose in the thick of it . my eye be wear out with it . take the glass , Erema , and tell we who be next to be wash away . a new set of clothe - prop for Mrs. Mangles I pay for the very day I come back from town . " 
 with these word , the lord of the submarine manor   whose strength of spirit amaze I   offer his pet binocular , which he never go without upon his own domain . and fisherman Barnes , as we rise and fall , once more save we from be ' swamp " by his clever way of paddle through a scallop in the stern , with the board about the first floor front to let . 
 the seaman , just keep way on the boat , shelter their eye with their left hand , and fix they on the tumultuous scene . 
 I also gaze through the double glass , which be a very clear one ; but none of we see any human being at present in any peril . 
 " old pilot be right , after all , " say one ; " but what a good job as it come o ' middle day , and good of all of a Sunday ! " 
 " I have heere say , " reply another , " that the like thing come to pass nigh upon three hunder year agone . how do you get your thing out , Jem Bishop ? " 
 Jem , the only one of they whose house be in the havoc , regard with a sailor 's calmness the entry of the sea through his bedroom window , and be go to favor we with a narrative , when one of his mate exclaim ,

 he turn away from I , and gaze back toward the dismal , miserable , spectral desert ; while I stand face the fruitful , delicious , flowery Paradise of all the world . I think of the difference in our lot , and my heart be in misery about he . then I conquer my pride and my littleness and trumpery , and do what the gentle sweet Eve might have do . and never have I grieve for that action since . 
 with tear on my cheek quite undissemble , and a breast not ashamed of flutter , I run to Firm Gundry , and take his right hand , and allow he no refuge from tender wet eye . then before he could come to see the meaning of this haste because of his very high discipline I be out of his distance , and sit on a rock , and I lift my eye , full of eloquence , to his ; then I drop they , and pull my hat forward , and say , as calmly as be possible , " I have do enough . the rest remain with you , Firm Gundry . " 
 the rest remain with he . enough that I be part of that rest ; and if not the foundation or crown of it , something desirous to be both , and fail   if fail it ever do   from no want of trial . Uncle Sam say that I never fail at all , and never do fail in any thing , unless it be when I find that blame nugget , for which we get three wagon - load of greenback ; which   when prosperity at last revive   will pay perhaps for grease all twelve wheel . 
 Jowler admit not that failure even . as soon as he recover from canine dementia , approach very closely to rabie , at see I in the flesh once more   so that the Sierra Nevada ring with avalanche of barking , he tug I to the place where his tooth be set in gold , and prove that he have no hydrophobia . his tooth be scanty now , but he still can catch a salmon , and the bright zeal and loyalty of his soft brown eye and the sprightly elevation of his tail be still among dog as pre - eminent as they be to mankind inimitable . 
 now the war be past , and here we sit by the bank of the soft Blue River . the early storm and young conflict of a clouded life be over . still out of sight there may be yet a sea of trouble to buffet with ; but it be not merely a selfish thought that other will face it with I . dark mystery have be clear away by be confront bravely ; and the lesson have be learn that life   like California flower   be of infinite variety . this little river , ten step wide , on one side have all lupin , on the other side all larkspur . can I tell why ? can any body ? can even itself , so full of voice and light , unroll the reason ? 
 behind we tower the stormy crag , before we spread soft tapestry of earth and sweep of ocean . below we lie my father 's grave , whose sin be not his own , but fall on he , and find he loyal . to he be I loyal also , as a daughter should be ; and in my lap lie my reward for I be no more erema .
